كتاب الصلاة باب الوتر والنوافل
سألت أنساً عن القنوت في الصلاة قال : نعم . قلت : أكان قبل الركوع أو بعده؟ قال : قبله . قلت: فإن فلاناً أخبرني عنك أنك قلت بعده قال كذب إنما قنت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بعد الركوع شهراً. وظاهر الأحاديث يدل على القنوت في جميع السنة، وأما ما رواه أبو داود أن عمر رضي الله عنه جمع الناس على أبي بن كعب فكان يصلي بهم عشرين ليلة من الشهر - يعني رمضان - ولا يقنت بهم إلا في النصف الثاني فإذا كان العشر الأواخر تخلف فصلى في بيته، فلا يدل على تخصيصه بالنصف الثاني من رمضان لأن القنوت فيه يحتمل أن يكون طول القيام فإنه يقال عليه كما يقال على الدعاء وترجح الأول لتخصيص النصف الأخير بزيادة الاجتهاد فليس هو المتنازع فيه والكلام في القنوت في خمسة مواضع: في صفته ومحل أدائه ومقداره ودعائه وحكمه إذا فات . أما الأول فقد ذكره المصنف في باب صفة الصلاة من الواجبات وهو مذهب أبي حنيفة وعندهما سنة كالوتر، ويشهد للوجوب قوله للحسن حين علمه القنوت، اجعل هذا في وترك. والأمر للوجوب لكنه تعقبه في فتح القدير بأنه لم يثبت ومنهم من حاول الاستدلال بالمواظبة المفادة من الأحاديث وهو متوقف على كونها غير مقرونة بالترك مرة لكن مطلق المواظبة أعم من المقرونة به أحياناً وغير المقرونة ولا دلالة للأعم على الأخص وإلا لوجبت بهذه الكلمات عيناً أو كانت أولى من غيرها لكن المتقرر عندهم الدعاء المعروف اللهم إنا نستعينك كما سيأتي اهـ . وأطلقه فشمل الأداء والقضاء فلذا قالوا: ومن يقضي الصلوات والأوتار يقنت في الأوتار احتياطاً. وعلله الولوالجي في فتاواه بأنه إن كان عليه الوتر كان عليه القنوت وإن لم يكن عليه الوتر فالقنوت يكون في التطوع والقنوت في التطوع لا يضر اهـ . وهو يقتضي أن قضاءه ليس لكونه لم يؤد حقيقة بل احتياطاً وليس هو بمستحب . قال في مآل الفتاوى : ولما لم يفته شيء من الصلوات وأحب أن يقضي جميع الصلوات التي صلاها متداركاً لا يستحب له ذلك إذا كان غالب ظنه فساد ما صلى ورد النهي عنه . وما حكي عن أبي حنيفة أنه قضى صلاة عمره فإن صح النقل فنقول كان يصلي المغرب والوتر أربع ركعات بثلاث قعدات .اهـ. وفي التجنيس : شك في الوتر وهو في حالة القيام أنه في الثانية أم في الثالثة يتم تلك الركعة ويقنت فيها لجواز أنها الثالثة، ثم يقعد فيقوم فيضيف إليها ركعة أخرى ويقنت فيها أيضاً، وهو المختار . فرق بين هذا وبين المسبوق بركعتين في الوتر في شهر رمضان إذا قنت مع الإمام في الركعة الأخيرة من صلاة الإمام حيث لا يقنت في الركعة الأخيرة إذا قام إلى القضاء في قولهم جميعاً . والفرق أن تكرار القنوت في موضعه ليس بمشروع وههنا أحدهما في موضعه والآخر ليس في موضعه فجاز، فأما المسبوق فهو مأمور بأن يقنت مع الإمام فصار ذلك موضعاً له، فلو أتى بالثاني كان ذلك تكراراً للقنوت في موضعه اهـ.
(Book of Prayer, Chapter of Witr and Supererogatory Prayers) I asked Anas about qunut in prayer; he said: Yes. I said: Was it before ruku or after? He said: Before. I said: Such-and-such told me from you that you said after; he said: He lied; the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) only performed qunut after ruku for a month. And the apparent meaning of the hadiths indicates qunut throughout the entire year. As for what Abu Dawud narrated that Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) gathered the people behind Ubayy ibn Ka'b, and he prayed with them twenty nights of the month – meaning Ramadan – and only performed qunut with them in the second half, and when the last ten nights came, he stayed behind and prayed in his house, this does not indicate that it is specific to the second half of Ramadan, because qunut therein could be length of standing, for it is said of that as it is said of supplication, and the first is preferred because the last half is singled out for increased effort, so it is not the point of dispute. And the discussion on qunut is in five places: its nature, its place of performance, its amount, its supplication, and its ruling when missed. As for the first, the author mentioned it in the chapter on the attributes of prayer among the obligations, and it is the madhhab of Abu Hanifa, while according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) it is sunnah like witr. And evidence for obligation is his saying to al-Hasan when he taught him qunut: 'Place this in your witr.' And the command indicates obligation, but it was objected to in Fath al-Qadir that it has not been established, and some attempted to prove it by constancy found in the hadiths, which depends on it not being accompanied by omission once, but absolute constancy is more general than that which is sometimes accompanied by omission and what is not, and the general does not indicate the specific, otherwise these words themselves would be obligatory or more preferable than others, but the well-known among them is the supplication 'Allahumma inna nasta'inuka' as will come. He (the author) was absolute so it includes performance and Qada, therefore they said: Whoever prays the missed prayers and witrs should perform qunut in the witrs as a precaution. And al-Walwaliji explained in his Fatawa that if he had witr upon him, qunut was upon him, and if he did not have witr upon him, then qunut is in supererogatory prayer, and qunut in supererogatory prayer does not harm. This implies that qada is not because it was not actually performed but as a precaution, and it is not recommended. He said in Ma'al al-Fatawa: When nothing of prayers is missed and he wants to perform qada of all prayers he prayed as a catch-up, it is not recommended for him to do so unless he strongly suspects the invalidity of what he prayed, and the prohibition is reported. And what is narrated from Abu Hanifa that he performed qada of his entire life's prayer, if the report is correct then we say he used to pray Maghrib and Witr as four rak'ahs with three sittings. End. And in al-Tajnis: If one doubts in witr while standing whether he is in the second or third rak'ah, he completes that rak'ah and performs qunut in it because it might be the third, then he sits, then stands and adds another rak'ah and performs qunut in it as well, and that is the chosen view. There is a difference between this and the one who is two rak'ahs behind in witr in Ramadan, if he performs qunut with the imam in the last rak'ah of the imam's prayer, he does not perform qunut in the last rak'ah when he stands to complete what he missed, according to all of them. The difference is that repetition of qunut in its place is not prescribed, whereas here one of them is in its place and the other is not, so it is permissible. As for the one who is behind, he is ordered to perform qunut with the imam, so that becomes its place; if he performs a second one, that would be repetition of qunut in its place. End.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the ruling of qunut in the witr prayer, covering its nature, place, and related issues. The author begins by narrating a hadith from Anas ibn Malik regarding the timing of qunut (before or after ruku) and clarifies that the apparent meaning of hadiths supports qunut throughout the year, not only in Ramadan. He then outlines five aspects of qunut: its ruling (wajib or sunnah), its place (before or after ruku), its amount, its supplication, and its ruling when missed. The focus then shifts to the first aspect: the nature of qunut. According to Abu Hanifa, qunut is wajib (obligatory), while according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), it is sunnah. The evidence for obligation is the hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) told al-Hasan ibn Ali: 'Place this in your witr' – the imperative form indicates obligation. However, this hadith is contested; in Fath al-Qadir, it is claimed that the command is not authentically established. Some scholars argue for obligation based on the Prophet's constant practice (muwazabah), but the author refutes this by noting that constant practice is general and does not necessarily mean it was never omitted occasionally. The discussion continues with the words of qunut: the known Hanafi supplication is 'Allahumma inna nasta'inuka...', and if the hadith were to specify different words, those would be obligatory or preferable, but the well-known among Hanafis is the aforementioned. The author then addresses qada (making up missed witr) and the ruling on performing qunut in qada: it is done as a precaution, not because it is originally required. The difference between a doubt case and a masbuq (latecomer) case is explained: in doubt, one can perform qunut in two rak'ahs, whereas a masbuq only performs qunut once with the imam and not again when completing his prayer, because repetition in its proper place is not prescribed. The passage is a detailed fiqh commentary reflecting the Hanafi school's internal differences and practical applications.

Key Terms
القنوت (al-qunūt): A supplication recited in the witr prayer, specifically in the last rak'ah after ruku or before, or in times of calamity.
الوتر (al-witr): An odd-numbered prayer performed after the Isha prayer, consisting of one, three, five, seven, nine, or eleven rak'ahs; the common practice is three rak'ahs.
المواظبة (al-muwāẓabah): The Prophet's constant practice of an action without leaving it, used as evidence for a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling of qunut in witr?
A) Wajib
B) Sunnah mu'akkadah
C) Fard
D) Mustahabb

Key Takeaway
Within the Hanafi school, qunut in witr is sunnah (mufta bihi), though Abu Hanifa considered it wajib; the difference hinges on the authenticity of the hadith evidence.

Salah — Prayer
advanced
15 min
Qunut in Witr: Obligation, Doubt, and the Masbuq Distinction
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qunut repetition during doubt in witr, with a distinction from the masbuq case.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the chosen Hanafi position on repeating qunut when doubting the rak'ah in witr and distinguish it from the masbuq case.

Core Idea
When in doubt about the rak'ah, repeat qunut as precaution; the masbuq does not repeat because one qunut is already in its virtual place.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq unpacks the internal Hanafi dispute over qunut in witr when one doubts whether he is in the second or third rak'ah. The author sets out the issue, presents multiple views, and determines the chosen position (al-mukhtar) based on the principle that qunut is wajib and precaution is preferred. He then contrasts this with the masbuq case where repeating qunut would be a repetition in its proper place, which is not allowed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the parties
The issue is doubt between the second and third rak'ah in witr. The Hanafi majority holds one view; a minority holds another.
Both views are from Hanafi scholars.
2
Examine the majority proof
Qunut is wajib, so doubt mandates precaution (ihtiyat) by performing qunut in the current rak'ah and again in an added rak'ah to ensure it falls in the last rak'ah.
The majority view is declared the chosen view (al-mukhtar).
3
Understand the opposing argument
The opposing view argues that qunut in a non-last rak'ah is a bid'ah, and abandoning a sunnah is easier than committing a bid'ah.
This view is found in al-Muhit and al-Dhakhira.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
When the act is ambiguous between wajib and bid'ah, one performs it as precaution. The author prefers the majority view because qunut is wajib.
The author criticizes al-Dhakhira's view as weak.
5
Apply the distinction with the masbuq
The masbuq does not repeat qunut because his qunut with the imam is considered at the end of his prayer in ruling (hukman). Repeating it would be duplication in the same place, which is not legislated.
This distinction shows the importance of the 'virtual end' concept.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالمواظبة المفادة من الأحاديث وهو متوقف على كونها غير مقرونة بالترك مرة لكن مطلق المواظبة أعم من المقرونة به أحياناً وغير المقرونة ولا دلالة للأعم على الأخص وإلا لوجبت بهذه الكلمات عيناً أو كانت أولى من غيرها لكن المتقرر عندهم الدعاء المعروف اللهم إنا نستعينك كما سيأتي اهـ . وأطلقه فشمل الأداء والقضاء فلذا قالوا: ومن يقضي الصلوات والأوتار يقنت في الأوتار احتياطاً. وعلله الولوالجي في فتاواه بأنه إن كان عليه الوتر كان عليه القنوت وإن لم يكن عليه الوتر فالقنوت يكون في التطوع والقنوت في التطوع لا يضر اهـ . وهو يقتضي أن قضاءه ليس لكونه لم يؤد حقيقة بل احتياطاً وليس هو بمستحب . قال في مآل الفتاوى : ولما لم يفته شيء من الصلوات وأحب أن يقضي جميع الصلوات التي صلاها متداركاً لا يستحب له ذلك إذا كان غالب ظنه فساد ما صلى ورد النهي عنه . وما حكي عن أبي حنيفة أنه قضى صلاة عمره فإن صح النقل فنقول كان يصلي المغرب والوتر أربع ركعات بثلاث قعدات .اهـ. وفي التجنيس : شك في الوتر وهو في حالة القيام أنه في الثانية أم في الثالثة يتم تلك الركعة ويقنت فيها لجواز أنها الثالثة، ثم يقعد فيقوم فيضيف إليها ركعة أخرى ويقنت فيها أيضاً، وهو المختار . فرق بين هذا وبين المسبوق بركعتين في الوتر في شهر رمضان إذا قنت مع الإمام في الركعة الأخيرة من صلاة الإمام حيث لا يقنت في الركعة الأخيرة إذا قام إلى القضاء في قولهم جميعاً . والفرق أن تكرار القنوت في موضعه ليس بمشروع وههنا أحدهما في موضعه والآخر ليس في موضعه فجاز، فأما المسبوق فهو مأمور بأن يقنت مع الإمام فصار ذلك موضعاً له، فلو أتى بالثاني كان ذلك تكراراً للقنوت في موضعه اهـ. وفي المحيط معزياً إلى الأجناس : لو شك أنه في الأولى أو في الثانية أو في الثالثة فإنه يقنت في الركعة التي هو فيها ثم يقعد ثم يقوم فيصلي ركعتين بقعدتين ويقنت فيهما احتياطاً. وفي قول آخر : لا يقنت في الكل أصلاً لأن القنوت في الركعة الثانية والأولى بدعة وترك السنة أسهل من الإتيان بالبدعة والأول أصح لأن القنوت واجب، وما تردد بين الواجب والبدعة يأتي به احتياطاً اهـ. وفي الذخيرة : إن قنت في الأولى أو في الثانية ساهياً لم يقنت في الثالثة لأنه لا يتكرر في الصلاة الواحدة .اهـ. وفيه نظر لأنه إذا كان مع الشك في كونه في محله يعيده ليقع في محله كما قدمناه فمع اليقين بكونه في غير محله أولى أن يعيده كما لو قعد بعد الأولى ساهياً لا يمنعه أن يقعد بعد الثانية، ولعل ما في الذخيرة مبني على القول الضعيف القائل بأنه لا يقنت في الكل أصلاً كما لا يخفي . في موضعه على كل من القولين فلو قنت فيما يقضي لا يكون تكراراً له في موضعه، أما على الأول فظاهر، وأما على الثاني فكذلك لما علمت من أنه جعل ما يقضيه آخر صلاته إلا في القراءة والقنوت . وقد يجاب بأن شرعية القنوت أنها هي في آخر الصلاة حقيقة وحكماً كما في غير المسبوق أو حكماً فقط كما في المسبوق فإن ما يقضيه المسبوق بالنظر إلى ما أدركه مع الإمام آخر صلاته ؛ وما أدركه أولها حقيقة لأن الأول اسم لفرد سابق وبالنظر إلى صلاة الإمام يكون أول صلاته لأن ما أدركه مع الإمام آخر صلاة الإمام فيكون ما يقضيه أول صلاته تحقيقاً للتبعية وتصحيحاً للاقتداء لكنها أولية حكمية ويكون ما أداه مع الإمام أول صلاته حقيقة على النظر الأول وآخرها حكماً على النظر الثاني، وقد اعتبروا الحكم في حق القنوت كيلا يؤدي إلى تكراره الذي هو غير مشروع وحينئذ فإذا قنت مع الإمام يكون قنوته في آخر الصلاة حكماً، وإذا قنت فيما يقضي أيضاً يكون في آخرها حقيقة فلزم تكراره في موضعه الذي هو آخر الصلاة وأما مسألة الشاك فلم يلزم ذلك فيها لأن أحد القنوتين ليس في آخر الصلاة وكان مقتضى عدم مشروعية تكراره المنع ولكنه أمر به لما سيذكره المؤلف عن المحيط. هذا ما ظهر لي والله تعالى أعلم
By the constancy derived from the hadiths, it depends on it not being accompanied by abandonment once, but absolute constancy is more general than that which is occasionally accompanied by abandonment and that which is not, and the general does not indicate the specific, otherwise these words would be obligatory per se or they would be more deserving than others, but what is established with them is the well-known supplication 'Allahumma inna nasta'inuk' as will come. And he made it absolute, so it includes performance and makeup, so they said: Whoever makes up prayers and witrs should perform qunut in the witrs as a precaution. And al-Walwalji justified it in his fatwas: If he was obligated to pray witr, then qunut was upon him, and if he was not obligated to pray witr, then qunut is in supererogatory prayer, and qunut in supererogatory prayer does not harm. This implies that his makeup is not because he did not actually perform it, but as a precaution, and it is not recommended. He said in Ma'al al-Fatawa: Since he did not miss any prayer and wishes to make up all the prayers he performed as a recompense, that is not recommended for him if his dominant assumption is the corruption of what he prayed, and the prohibition of it is reported. And what is narrated about Abu Hanifa that he made up the prayers of his lifetime—if the transmission is authentic, we say: He used to pray Maghrib and Witr with four rak'ahs with three sittings. End. And in al-Tajnis: One doubts in witr while in the standing state whether he is in the second or third; he completes that rak'ah and performs qunut in it because it may be the third, then he sits, then stands, adds another rak'ah, and performs qunut in it as well, and this is the chosen view. A distinction is made between this and the one who is preceded by two rak'ahs in witr in Ramadan when he performed qunut with the imam in the last rak'ah of the imam's prayer, where he does not perform qunut in the last rak'ah when he stands to make up, in the view of all of them. The difference is that repeating qunut in its place is not legislated, and here one of them is in its place and the other is not in its place, so it is permissible. As for the masbuq, he is commanded to perform qunut with the imam, so that becomes its place, and if he performs the second, that would be repetition of qunut in its place. End. And in al-Muhit, citing al-Ajnas: If one doubts whether he is in the first, second, or third, he performs qunut in the rak'ah he is in, then sits, then stands, and prays two rak'ahs with two sittings, and performs qunut in both as a precaution. In another view: He does not perform qunut at all because qunut in the second and first rak'ahs is an innovation, and abandoning the sunnah is easier than committing an innovation. And the first is more correct because qunut is obligatory, and what is ambiguous between the obligatory and innovation is performed as a precaution. End. And in al-Dhakhira: If he performed qunut in the first or second unintentionally, he does not perform qunut in the third because it is not repeated in one prayer. End. But this is questionable because if with doubt about being in its place he repeats it to fall in its place, as we mentioned, then with certainty of being out of its place it is more fitting to repeat it, just as if he sat after the first unintentionally, it does not prevent him from sitting after the second. Perhaps what is in al-Dhakhira is based on the weak view that he should not perform qunut at all, as is not hidden. In its place according to both views, if he performs qunut in what he makes up, it would not be repetition in its place. As for the first, it is apparent, and as for the second, likewise because you know that he made what he makes up as the last part of his prayer except in recitation and qunut. And it may be answered that the legislation of qunut is that it is at the end of the prayer in reality and in ruling, as in the non-masbuq, or only in ruling, as in the masbuq. For what the masbuq makes up, from the perspective of what he caught with the imam, is the last part of his prayer; and what he caught is the first part in reality because 'first' is a name for a preceding individual, and from the perspective of the imam's prayer, it is the first part of his prayer because what he caught with the imam is the last part of the imam's prayer, so what he makes up is the first part of his prayer, for the sake of following and correcting the iqtida, but it is a virtual first, and what he performed with the imam is the first part of his prayer in reality on the first view, and the last part in ruling on the second view. And they considered the ruling concerning qunut so that it does not lead to its repetition, which is not legislated. Therefore, when he performs qunut with the imam, his qunut is at the end of the prayer in ruling, and if he also performs qunut in what he makes up, it would be at the end in reality, necessitating repetition in its place, which is the end of the prayer. As for the case of the one in doubt, that does not apply there because one of the two qunuts is not at the end of the prayer, and the requirement of the illegitimacy of repetition would prevent it, but he is commanded to do so for what the author will mention from al-Muhit. This is what appeared to me, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is an expansion (sharh) of Kanz al-Daqaiq, addressing multiple rulings on qunut in the witr prayer. The author begins by discussing the nature of continued practice (muwazabah) as evidence, noting that it cannot prove obligation without certainty of uninterrupted practice. He then moves to the ruling on qunut in makeup prayers (qada), where the preferred view is to perform qunut as a precaution, though it is not actually recommended. A narration from Abu Hanifa is discussed where he reportedly made up prayers by praying maghrib and witr as four rak'ahs with three sittings, indicating a special method. The core of the passage deals with a person who doubts whether he is in the second or third rak'ah of witr. According to al-Tajnis, the chosen view (al-mukhtar) is to complete the current rak'ah with qunut, then sit, stand for another rak'ah, and perform qunut again. This is contrasted with the case of a masbuq (latecomer) in Ramadan who performed qunut with the imam; when he stands to complete his prayer, he does not repeat qunut, according to all Hanafi scholars. The distinction is that repeating qunut in its proper place (i.e., the last rak'ah) is not legislated, but in the doubt case, one qunut is in its place and the other is not, so repetition is allowed. Al-Muhit cites al-Ajnas with a similar ruling, but also mentions a second view that rejects qunut entirely in such doubt, arguing that qunut in non-last rak'ahs is innovation and avoiding innovation is easier than abandoning a sunnah. The author prefers the first view because qunut is wajib (obligatory), and when there is doubt between an obligation and innovation, one performs it as precaution. Al-Dhakhira's view is critiqued as based on the weak opinion. The passage then elaborates on the masbuq's case, explaining that his qunut with the imam is considered at the end of his prayer in ruling (hukman), even if in reality it is earlier. Thus, performing qunut again in his makeup would constitute repetition in the same place, which is prohibited. The doubt case is different because one qunut is not at the end, so repetition does not violate the principle.

Key Terms
القنوت (al-qunut): A special supplication recited in the witr prayer while standing, considered wajib in the Hanafi school.
الوتر (al-witr): The odd-numbered prayer performed after the night prayer, consisting of one, three, five, etc., rak'ahs; the last rak'ah is the place for qunut.
المسبوق (al-masbuq): A latecomer who joins the prayer after the imam has already started, catching one or more rak'ahs. In this context, a masbuq in witr who performed qunut with the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the chosen view (al-mukhtar) in al-Bahr al-Raiq, what should a person do if he doubts whether he is in the second or third rak'ah of witr?
A) Complete the rak'ah without qunut, then add another rak'ah and perform qunut only in the last rak'ah.
B) Perform qunut in the current rak'ah, then after sitting, stand again and add another rak'ah with qunut, thus performing qunut twice.
C) Leave the prayer and restart because of the doubt.
D) Perform qunut only in the last rak'ah after completing three rak'ahs.

Key Takeaway
When in doubt during witr, the chosen Hanafi position is to complete the current rak'ah with qunut and add another rak'ah with qunut, distinguishing this from the masbuq who does not repeat.

Repeating Qunut in Witr After a Mistake
Intra-Hanafi dispute on repeating qunut after mistake

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on repeating qunut in Witr when mistakenly performed in an earlier rak'ah, evaluate the two conflicting Hanafi opinions, and apply the analogy with inadvertent sitting.

Core Idea
Accidental early qunut does not cancel the obligation to perform it in its proper place.

Qunut in Witr is wajib (obligatory) in the Hanafi school, and its proper place is the third rak'ah. But what if you mistakenly recite it in the first or second rak'ah? Should you repeat it in the third, or does the mistake mean you should skip it altogether? The Hanafi masters debated this, and this lesson walks through the evidence and the preferred view.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on qunut
Recall that in the Hanafi school, qunut in Witr is wajib and must be performed in the third rak'ah. This is the baseline.
2
Present the first view (precaution)
The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq reports that one should perform qunut in all rak'ahs as a precaution, because qunut is wajib and there is doubt about its correct placement.
This view is considered 'more correct' by the author.
3
Present the second view (al-Dhakhira)
The work al-Dhakhira states that if qunut was inadvertently performed in the first or second rak'ah, one should not repeat it in the third, because qunut is not repeated in one prayer.
This view is criticized by the author.
4
Analyze the analogy with sitting after the first rak'ah
The author draws an analogy: if someone inadvertently sits after the first rak'ah, that does not prevent sitting after the second. Similarly, inadvertent qunut should not prevent the correct qunut in the third.
This is a qiyas jali (clear analogy).
5
Identify the tarjih (preferred view)
The author prefers the precaution view because it aligns with the principle of ihtiyat (precaution) when there is doubt between wajib and innovation. The analogy also supports repeating qunut.
The mufta bihi is to repeat qunut in the third rak'ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يقنت في الركعة التي هو فيها ثم يقعد ثم يقوم فيصلي ركعتين بقعدتين ويقنت فيهما احتياطاً. وفي قول آخر : لا يقنت في الكل أصلاً لأن القنوت في الركعة الثانية والأولى بدعة وترك السنة أسهل من الإتيان بالبدعة والأول أصح لأن القنوت واجب، وما تردد بين الواجب والبدعة يأتي به احتياطاً اهـ. وفي الذخيرة : إن قنت في الأولى أو في الثانية ساهياً لم يقنت في الثالثة لأنه لا يتكرر في الصلاة الواحدة .اهـ. وفيه نظر لأنه إذا كان مع الشك في كونه في محله يعيده ليقع في محله كما قدمناه فمع اليقين بكونه في غير محله أولى أن يعيده كما لو قعد بعد الأولى ساهياً لا يمنعه أن يقعد بعد الثانية، ولعل ما في الذخيرة مبني على القول الضعيف القائل بأنه لا يقنت في الكل أصلاً كما لا يخفي .
He performs qunut in the rak'ah he is in, then sits, then stands and prays two rak'ahs with two sittings and performs qunut in both as a precaution. In another saying: He does not perform qunut at all in any of them because qunut in the second and first rak'ah is an innovation and abandoning the sunnah is easier than committing an innovation. The first is more correct because qunut is obligatory, and when something is between the obligatory and innovation, he performs it as a precaution. End. And in al-Dhakhira: If he inadvertently performed qunut in the first or second, he does not perform qunut in the third, because it is not repeated in one prayer. End. And there is a problem with this because if he is in doubt about whether it is in its place, he repeats it to make it fall in its place, as we have stated. So with certainty that it is not in its place, it is even more appropriate to repeat it, just as if he sat after the first inadvertently, that does not prevent him from sitting after the second. Perhaps what is in al-Dhakhira is based on the weak view that holds he does not perform qunut at all in any of them, as is not hidden.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the ruling on repeating qunut in the third rak'ah of Witr when one has mistakenly performed it in the first or second rak'ah. The text first presents a view that one should perform qunut in all rak'ahs as a precaution, then another view that one should not perform qunut at all in the first two because it would be an innovation. The author (of al-Bahr al-Raiq) prefers the first view because qunut is wajib (obligatory) according to the Hanafi school. Then the author quotes from al-Dhakhira that if one inadvertently did qunut in the first or second, he should not repeat it in the third because qunut is not to be repeated in one prayer. The author criticizes this by analogy: if someone inadvertently sits after the first rak'ah, that does not prevent him from sitting after the second. Similarly, if one is certain that the qunut was not in its proper place, it is even more necessary to repeat it in the proper place. The author concludes that al-Dhakhira's view is based on the weak opinion that qunut is not performed at all.

Key Terms
قنوت (qunūt): The supplication recited in the third rak'ah of Witr, which the Hanafi school considers wajib.
سهو (sahw): Forgetfulness or inadvertence during prayer.
بدعة (bid‘ah): Innovation in religion, considered blameworthy.
احتياط (ihtiyāt): Precautionary measure in worship when the ruling is uncertain.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Qunut is a sunnah, so it may be repeated.
B) Qunut is wajib, so the precaution is to perform it in its proper place.
C) The other view is clearly a bid'ah.
D) The analogy with sitting is weak.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, qunut in Witr is wajib; if mistakenly performed early, the safer opinion is to repeat it in the third rak'ah.

Quantity and Supplication of Qunut in Witr
Discussion on length of qunut standing and the supplication dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the quantity of qunut standing and identify the two positions regarding the fixed supplication, explaining which is mufta bihi.

Core Idea
The qunut supplication is not fixed in wording, but the famous du'a is recommended and effectively relied upon.

Qunut in Witr is wajib in the Hanafi school, but there is a nuanced discussion about its length and the specific words. This lesson examines the quantity of standing (equivalent to Surah al-Insyiqaq) and the dispute between early Hanafis who say no fixed du'a and later scholars who recommend the famous transmitted supplication. Understanding this helps you practice Witr correctly and avoid common errors in pronunciation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is qunut in Witr. It is wajib. Focus on two aspects: its quantity (standing length) and its supplication (wording).
2
State the quantity of standing
The source gives the quantity as the length of Surah al-Insyiqaq (Surah 84), based on the Prophet's recitation of 'Allahumma inna nasta'inuk' which is about that length. This is the Hanafi view.
This is not a disputed point in the passage.
3
Trace the dispute on the supplication
Two views within the Hanafi school: (1) Early view (al-Karkhi, zahir al-riwayah): no fixed du'a; any supplication is allowed. (2) Later view (some mashayikh): the famous du'a 'Allahumma inna nasta'inuk' is recommended and effectively fixed because the Salaf agreed on it.
The passage also mentions a third opinion advocating a fixed du'a to prevent invalid prayer.
4
Identify the dalil and the tarjih
The dalil for the quantity is the practice of the Prophet. For the supplication, the evidence includes the variety of Companion reports and the principle that fixed du'a removes tenderness (riqqah). The tarjih in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli favours the second group due to transmitted evidence and continuity.
The passage also discusses the exact wording and pronunciation details (e.g., 'al-jadd', 'mulhiq', 'nahfidu').
5
Apply the ruling to practice
The mufta bihi is to recite the famous du'a. If one recites a different supplication, it is permissible as long as it is meaningful and does not resemble human speech. Mispronunciations that alter meaning (e.g., replacing 'nahfidu' with 'yadhfidu' – meaningless) invalidate the prayer.
The passage warns against errors that make the du'a meaningless.

Source Text

فيمن هديت إلى آخره. وقال بعضهم : الأفضل من الوتر أن يكون فيه دعاء مؤقت لأن الإمام ربما يكون جاهلاً فيأتي بدعاء يشبه كلام الناس فتفسد صلاته، وما روي عن محمد من أن التوقيت في الدعاء يذهب برقة القلب، محمول على أدعية المناسك دون الصلاة. كذا في البدائع. ورجح في شرح منية المصلي قول الطائفة الثانية لما ذكروا وتبركاً بالمأثور الوارد به الأخبار وتوارثه الخلف في سائر الأعصار اهـ. لكن ذكر الاسبيجابي أن ظاهر الرواية عدم توقيته. ثم إن الدعاء المشهور عند أبي حنيفة : اللهم إنا نستعينك ونستغفرك ونؤمن بك ونتوكل عليك ونثني عليك الخير كله، نشكرك ولا نكفرك ونخلع ونترك من يفجرك، اللهم إياك نعبد ولك نصلي ونسجد وإليك نسعى ونحفد نرجو رحمتك ونخشى عذابك إن عذابك بالكفار ملحق. لكن في المقدمة الغزنوية إن عذابك الجد. ولم يذكره في الحاوي القدسي إلا أنه أسقط الواو من «نخلع». والظاهر ثبوتهما . أما إثبات الجد» ففي فيه حكاها ابن مالك في «فعل» و«افعل». وصرح قاضيخان في فتاواه بأنه لو قرأها بالذال المعجمة بطلت صلاته ولعله لأنها كلمة مهملة لا معنى لها.
As for the second, we have mentioned it. As for its quantity, al-Karkhi mentioned that the amount of standing in qunut is the amount of Surah 'Idha al-Sama' Unshaqat, and likewise it is mentioned in al-Asl because it is narrated from the Prophet ﷺ that he used to recite in qunut 'Allahumma inna nasta'inuk, Allahumma ihdina', and both are about the length of this surah. And it is narrated that he would not lengthen the qunut supplication; thus in al-Bada'i. As for its supplication, there is no fixed supplication. Thus al-Karkhi mentioned in Kitab al-Salah because it is narrated from the Companions various supplications in the state of qunut, and because a fixed supplication takes away tenderness as narrated from Muhammad, and thus it distances from being answered, and because one does not fix recitation in any prayer, so in qunut supplication it is more appropriate. Some of our scholars said: The meaning of his saying 'there is no fixed supplication' is other than 'Allahumma inna nasta'inuk' because the Salaf (predecessors) agreed upon it, so it is better to recite it; if he recites other than it, it is permissible; if he recites both, it is good; and it is better to recite after it what the Messenger of Allah taught to al-Hasan ibn Ali as his qunut: 'Allahumma ihdini fiman hadayt...' etc. Some said: It is better that Witr has a fixed supplication because the imam might be ignorant and come with a supplication resembling speech of people which would invalidate his prayer; and what is narrated from Muhammad that fixing a supplication removes tenderness of heart is understood as supplications of rituals (manasik) not prayer. Thus in al-Bada'i. And in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli, the second group's view is preponderant because of what they mentioned and seeking blessing from the transmitted [du'a] that comes in reports and the succession of the latter generations in all ages. End. But al-Isbijabi mentioned that the apparent of the riwaya is that it is not fixed. Then the famous supplication according to Abu Hanifa: Allahumma inna nasta'inuka wa nastaghfiruka wa nu'minu bika wa natawakkalu 'alayka wa nuthni 'alayka al-khayra kullahu, nashkuruka wa la nakfuruka wa nakhla'u wa natruku man yafjuruka, Allahumma iyyaka na'budu wa laka nusalli wa nasjudu wa ilayka nas'a wa nahfidu narju rahmataka wa nakhsha 'adhabaka inna 'adhabaka bil-kuffari mulhiq. But in al-Muqaddimat al-Ghaznawiyyah: 'inna 'adhabaka al-jadd'. And al-Hawi al-Qudsi omitted the waw from 'nakhla'u'. The apparent is that both are established. As for the establishment of 'al-jadd', it is in Mursil Abi Dawud. As for the establishment of the waw in 'wa nakhla'u', it is in the riwaya of al-Tahawi and al-Bayhaqi. And by this is repelled what al-Shumunni mentioned in Sharh al-Niqayah that one does not say 'al-jadd'. And they agreed that it is with kasr of the jim meaning al-haqq (the truth). And they differed about 'mulhiq'; al-Isbijabi corrected kasr of the ha' meaning 'lahaq bihim' (joined them), and some said with fatha, and al-Jawhari stated that it is correct. As for 'nahfidu', it is with fatha of the nun and kasr of the fa' and with an important dal from al-hafad meaning speed, and it is permissible to damm the nun. It is said 'hafada' meaning he hastened, and 'ahfada' is a language variation narrated by Ibn Malik in 'fa'ala' and 'af'ala'. And Qadikhan stated in his Fatawa that if one recites it with dhal mu'jama (i.e., 'yadhfidu'), his prayer becomes invalid, perhaps because it is a meaningless word.
Source pages p. 73

Commentary
This passage discusses two aspects of qunut in Witr: its quantity and its supplication. First, the quantity of standing (al-qiyam) is defined by al-Karkhi as the length of Surah al-Insyiqaq (Surah 84), based on the Prophet's practice of reciting 'Allahumma inna nasta'inuk' which is about that length. Second, the supplication itself: there is a difference of opinion. Al-Karkhi and the early texts state there is no fixed supplication, citing the variety from the Companions and that fixing a supplication might remove tenderness. However, some later scholars (some of our mashayikh) say the statement 'no fixed du'a' excludes the famous 'Allahumma inna nasta'inuk' because the Salaf agreed on it, so it is recommended. Others argue for a fixed supplication to prevent invalid prayer due to ignorance. The author then presents the famous Hanafi qunut as transmitted from Abu Hanifa, with details on its wording (including 'al-jadd' and 'mulhiq' with various readings) and warns against mispronunciations that invalidate the prayer. The preferred view in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli is for the second group (who advocate the fixed du'a) because of transmitted evidence and continuity.

Key Terms
قنوت (qunūt): A specific supplication in Witr, considered wajib in Hanafi school; its quantity is defined by length of standing.
دعاء مؤقت (du'ā' mu'aqqat): A supplication that is fixed with specific words.
ملحق (mulhiq): Part of the qunut du'a; means 'joined' or 'attached' (to the disbelievers).
نحفد (nahfidu): We hasten; part of the qunut du'a. Must be pronounced with dal (د), not dhal (ذ).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends the famous qunut du'a, but any meaningful supplication fulfills the wajib; mispronouncing it with meaningless words invalidates the prayer.

The Reality of Qunut and Substitutes for the Du'a
Determining whether qunut is the standing or the supplication, and options for those who cannot recite.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the reality of qunut, identify the intra-school disagreement, and apply the ruling for a person unable to recite the qunut du'a.

Core Idea
In the Hanafi school, qunut is the standing, not the supplication; the du'a is sunna and may be substituted if necessary.

The term 'qunut' in Witr prayer has been understood differently even within the Hanafi school. Some early authorities defined it as the length of standing, while others equated it with the supplication. This passage also provides practical guidance for those who cannot recite the qunut du'a, offering alternative phrases. We will analyze the evidence and the operative ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed element
Recognize that the dispute is about the 'reality' (haqiqah) of qunut: is it the act of standing (qiyam) or the supplication (du'a)?
Both positions are attributed to Hanafi authorities.
2
Examine the two positions
Note that al-Mujtaba and Abu Amr hold qunut is the standing, citing Quran 39:9. Al-Fatawa al-Sughra holds it is the supplication.
The author indicates the first view should be corrected.
3
Analyze the Quranic evidence
Verse 39:9 (أمن هو قانت آناء الليل) uses 'qanit' to mean devoutly standing in prayer, supporting the standing interpretation.
This is a linguistic and contextual proof.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
The author's statement 'and it should be corrected' (ينبغي تصحيحه) signals that the standing view is the relied-upon position.
Thus, the wajib is the standing; the du'a is sunna.
5
Apply the substitution ruling
For one unable to recite in Arabic or who does not know the du'a, three options are given: saying 'Ya Rabb' three times, 'Allahumma ighfir li' three times, or the verse 'Rabbana atina...'.
These are selected sayings (أقوال مختارة) from the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلم أن المشايخ اختلفوا في حقيقة القنوت الذي هو واجب عنده فنقل في المجتبى عن شرح المؤذني القنوت طول القيام دون الدعاء، وعن أبي عمرو لا أعرف من القنوت إلا طول القيام وبه فسر قوله تعالى أمن هو قانت آناء الليل [الزمر: ٩] وعن الفتاوى الصغرى : القنوت في الوتر هو الدعاء دون القيام .اهـ. وينبغي تصحيحه ومن يحسن القنوت بالغربية أو لا يحفظه ففيه ثلاثة أقوال مختارة : قيل يقول يا رب ثلاث مرات ثم يركع، وقيل يقول اللهم اغفر لي ثلاث مرات وقيل اللهم ربنا آتنا في الدنيا حسنة وفي الآخرة حسنة وقنا عذاب النار.
Then know that the scholars disagreed about the reality of qunut that is obligatory according to him. So it is narrated in al-Mujtaba from Sharh al-Mu'adhdhin that qunut is the length of standing without the supplication. And from Abu Amr: I do not know of qunut except the length of standing, and by this is interpreted His statement Most High 'Amman huwa qanitun ana'a al-layl' [39:9]. And from al-Fatawa al-Sughra: Qunut in Witr is the supplication without the standing. End. And it should be corrected. And whoever cannot perform qunut in Arabic or does not memorize it, there are three selected sayings: Some said: He says Ya Rabb three times then bows; Some said: He says Allahumma ighfir li three times; Some said: Allahumma Rabbana atina fi al-dunya hasanatan wa fi al-akhirati hasanatan wa qina 'adhab al-nar.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage addresses the essence of qunut: is it the act of standing (qiyam) or the supplication (du'a)? Two positions are narrated: one from al-Mujtaba that qunut is the standing only, and one from al-Fatawa al-Sughra that it is the supplication only. The author notes that the correct view should be the first (standing), as it is based on Quranic usage (al-Quran 39:9). Then, for someone who cannot recite the qunut in Arabic or does not know it, three options are given: saying 'Ya Rabb' three times, saying 'Allahumma ighfir li' three times, or reciting the Quranic verse 'Rabbana atina...' (2:201). These are select opinions from the school, providing flexibility for those who cannot recite the full du'a.

Key Terms
قنوت (qunūt): An obligatory element in Witr; according to the preferred view, it is the length of standing (qiyam), not the supplication.
طول القيام (ṭūl al-qiyām): Prolonged standing in prayer as an act of worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in the Hanafi school, what is the reality of qunut in Witr?
A) It is the supplication (du'a) only.
B) It is the length of standing (qiyam) only.
C) It is both the standing and the supplication equally.
D) It is optional.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines qunut as the prolonged standing in Witr, and the supplication is sunna; one who cannot recite may substitute short phrases.

Ruling if Qunut is Forgotten in Witr Prayer
Ruling on forgetting the qunut and remembering after going into ruku'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi ruling when qunut is forgotten in witr and explain the intra-madhhab dispute with Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
If you forget qunut in witr, do not return after ruku' — sacrificing a fard for a wajib is impermissible.

Forgetting parts of prayer is inevitable. But what should one do if the forgotten part is the qunut in witr? The Hanafi school distinguishes between acts integral to the rak'ah and those that are not. This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the ruling and the reasoning behind it, including a key difference with Imam Abu Yusuf.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
What does the relied-upon view (zahir al-riwayah) say about forgetting qunut and remembering after ruku'?
Distinguish between remembering during ruku' and after raising the head.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Abu Yusuf holds that one should return to qunut based on analogy to Quran recitation. Understand his qiyas.
Abu Yusuf compares qunut to al-Fatiha or sura recitation.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Trace the analogy: if al-Fatiha is forgotten and remembered during ruku', one returns and ruku' is invalidated. Why should qunut be different?
The analogue (asl) is recitation; the far' is qunut.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The key distinction: recitation is integral to the rak'ah, qunut is not. Invalidating ruku' for qunut would sacrifice a fard for a wajib.
The illa: whether the omitted act is essential for the rak'ah's completeness.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: if one returns and recites qunut without repeating ruku', per Abu Yusuf the prayer would be invalid (like al-Fatiha), but per Abu Hanifa it remains valid because ruku' stands.
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view (no return).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما حكمه إذا فات محله فنقول : إذا نسي القنوت حتى ركع ثم تذكر، فإن كان بعد رفع الرأس من الركوع لا يعود وسقط عنه القنوت وإن تذكره في الركوع فكذلك في ظاهر الرواية كما في البدائع وصححه في الخانية. وعن أبي يوسف أنه يعود إلى القنوت لشبهه بالقرآن كما لو ترك الفاتحة أو السورة فتذكرها في الركوع أو بعد رفع الرأس منه فإنه يعود وينتقض ركوعه والفرق على ظاهر الرواية أن نقض الركوع في المقيس عليه لإكماله لأنه يتكامل بقراءة الفاتحة والسورة لكونه لا يعتبر بدون القراءة أصلاً، وفي المقيس ليس نقضه لإكماله لأنه لا قنوت في سائر الصلوات والركوع معتبر ،بدونه، فلو نقض لكان نقض الفرض للواجب كذا في البدائع فإن عاد إلى القيام وقنت ولم يعد الركوع لم تفسد صلاته لأن ركوعه قائم لم يرتفض بخلاف المقيس عليه لأن بعوده صارت قراءة الكل فرضاً، والترتيب بين القراءة والركوع فرض، فارتفض ركوعه فلو لم يركع بطلت، فلو ركع وأدركه رجل في الركوع الثاني كان مدركاً لتلك الركعة وإنما لم يشرع القنوت في الركوع مثل تكبيرات العيد إذا تذكرها في حال الركوع حيث يكبر فيه لأنه لم يشرع إلا في محض القيام غير معقول المعنى فلا يتعدى إلى ما هو قيام من وجه دون وجه وهو الركوع، وأما تكبيرات العيد فلم تختص بمحض القيام لأن تكبيرة الركوع يؤتى بها في حال الانحطاط وهي محسوبة من تكبيرات العيد بإجماع الصحابة، فإذا جاز أداء واحدة منها في غير محض القيام من غير عذر جاز أداء الباقي مع قيام العذر بالأولى. ولم يقيد المصنف القنوت بالمخافتة للاختلاف المنبع وغيره مما ذكر . ثم ذكر أن في بعض النسخ «ونخلع» ونسبها أيضاً إلى الوانية ثم قال : ولعله «نخنع» بالنون أي نخضع . أنه قوله : (أصلاً) قيد لقوله بدون القراءة لا لقوله لا يعتبر أي أنه إذا فقدت القراءة أصلاً لا يعتبر، وقيد به لأنه لو وجد من القراءة آية واحدة يكون الركوع بعدها معتبراً قوله : (لكان نقض الفرض للواجب) قد يقال هو كذلك فيما لو عاد لقراءة السورة فإن أجيب بما يذكره المؤلف من بعوده صارت قراءة الكل فرضاً يقال عليه أنه لا يصير فرضاً إلا بعد القراءة، وأما قبلها فهو واجب فإذا رفض الركوع يكون رفض الفرض للواجب فيكون كرفضه للقنوت إلا أن يقال : فرق بين ما هو واجب حالاً ومآلاً وما هو واجب حالاً فرض مآلاً فرفض الركوع لما يكون فرضاً وإن كان قبل الشروع فيه واجباً ليس كرفضه إلى ما هو واجب على كل حال قوله : (حيث يكبر فيه) كذا في شرح المنية لابن أمير حاج الحلبي ومشى عليه في متن التنوير من باب العيد والذي في شرح المنية للشيخ
As for its ruling when its place is missed, we say: If one forgets the qunut until he bows, then remembers: if it is after raising the head from ruku', he does not return and the qunut is remitted. If he remembers during ruku', it is likewise in the apparent [position] of the [transmitted] report as in al-Bada'i, and it is corrected in al-Khaniyya. From Abu Yusuf: he returns to the qunut because of its similarity to the Quran, just as if one omitted al-Fatiha or a sura and remembers during ruku' or after raising the head, then he returns and his ruku' is invalidated. The difference according to the apparent report is that invalidating the ruku' in the analogy (maqis 'alayh) is for its completion, because it is perfected by reciting al-Fatiha and the sura, since it is not considered without recitation at all. In the analogous (maqis), its invalidation is not for completion, because there is no qunut in other prayers, and ruku' is considered without it. So if he invalidated, it would be invalidating the obligatory (fard) for the obligatory (wajib). This is in al-Bada'i. So if he returns to standing and performs qunut but does not repeat the ruku', his prayer is not invalidated because his ruku' stands and is not invalidated, unlike the analogy because by his return, the entire recitation becomes fard, and the order between recitation and ruku' is fard, so his ruku' is invalidated. So if he does not bow, his prayer becomes invalid. If he bows and a person joins him in the second ruku', that person catches that rak'ah. And qunut is not prescribed in ruku', unlike the takbirat of 'Id if one remembers during ruku' where he pronounces takbir, because qunut is prescribed only in pure standing without rational meaning, so it does not extend to what is standing in some aspects but not others, i.e., ruku'. As for takbirat of 'Id, they are not specific to pure standing, because the takbir of ruku' is performed while bowing and is counted from takbirat of 'Id by consensus of the Companions. So if it is permissible to perform one of them in non-pure standing without excuse, then performing the rest with an excuse is more appropriate. And the author did not restrict qunut to being in a low voice because of difference [of opinion]. Then he mentioned that in some copies, 'wa nakhla', and also attributed it to al-Waniyya, then said: perhaps it is 'nakhna' with nun, meaning we submit. [Then a discussion of the word 'aslan' and a note about invalidating fard for wajib.]
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling if one forgets the qunut in witr and remembers after moving to ruku'. The relied-upon position (zahir al-riwayah) is that if one remembers after raising the head from ruku', he does not return and the qunut is dropped. Similarly, if he remembers during ruku', he does not return. This is the view of Abu Hanifa and is confirmed in al-Bada'i and al-Khaniyya. However, Abu Yusuf differs: he argues that qunut is analogous to Quran recitation. If one forgets al-Fatiha or a sura and remembers during ruku', he must return to recitation, and his ruku' is invalidated. By analogy, the same should apply to qunut. The Hanafi response (on behalf of Abu Hanifa) makes a crucial distinction: in the case of al-Fatiha and sura, the ruku' is invalidated because the recitation is essential for the validity of the rak'ah; the rak'ah is only complete with proper recitation. For qunut, however, it is not required for the validity of the rak'ah; ruku' stands without it. Invalidating ruku' for qunut would mean sacrificing a fard (ruku') for a wajib (qunut), which is not permissible. If one were to return and perform qunut without repeating ruku', his prayer remains valid, unlike the case of forgetting a sura where returning without repeating ruku' would invalidate the prayer because the recitation becomes fard and order becomes obligatory. The author also compares to 'Id takbirat: if one remembers the additional takbirat during ruku', he pronounces them there, because takbirat are not restricted to standing. Qunut, however, is specific to standing and cannot be performed in ruku'. This distinction is based on the nature of the acts: takbirat are not rationally restricted to standing, while qunut is. The passage concludes with some textual notes on variants.

Key Terms
ركوع (ruku'): Bowing in prayer; a pillar (rukn) of the prayer.
قنوت (qunut): Supplication recited in witr; wajib per Abu Hanifa.
الفرض للواجب (al-fard lil-wajib): Sacrificing an obligatory act (fard) for a merely wajib act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what should a person do if they forget the qunut in witr and remember after raising their head from ruku'?
A) Return to qunut and repeat the ruku'.
B) Return to qunut without repeating ruku'.
C) Not return; the qunut is remitted.
D) Repeat the entire prayer.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, if qunut is forgotten in witr and remembered after ruku', one does not return; the fard act is prioritized over the wajib.

Ruling on Missing Qunut in Witr: Return or Not?
Explains ruling on missing qunut with qiyas and comparison to Eid takbirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on missing qunut in witr after ruku' and distinguish it from the case of missing Quran recitation.

Core Idea
Forgetting qunut after ruku' does not require return; it is dropped because it is wajib, not fard.

This passage addresses a practical scenario: if one forgets the qunut in witr prayer and remembers after bowing, what should he do? The Hanafi school, based on the distinction between fard and wajib, holds that he should not return. This lesson unpacks that ruling, the reasoning behind it, and a comparison with Eid takbirs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The scenario: a person forgets to recite qunut in witr and remembers it after starting ruku' (bowing). Determine the time of remembrance: during ruku' or after raising the head.
The ruling differs based on whether he remembers during ruku' or after.
2
State the Hanafi ruling (zahir al-riwaya)
According to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, if he remembers after beginning ruku' or after raising his head, he does not return; the qunut is dropped.
This is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).
3
Identify the opposing view
Imam Abu Yusuf holds that he should return to qunut, analogizing it to the case of forgetting Quran recitation (Fatiha or sura).
Abu Yusuf's qiyas: qunut is wajib like recitation, so it should be treated similarly.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response distinguishes: recitation is fard (essential for the rak'ah's validity), while qunut is wajib but not integral. Invalidating a fard (ruku') for a wajib is not allowed.
The key legal principle: a fard cannot be nullified for a wajib.
5
Compare with Eid takbirs
Eid takbirs can be performed in ruku' if missed, because they are not exclusive to pure standing. Qunut is restricted to standing, so it cannot be performed in ruku'.
This contrast shows the scope of the rule: qunut's place is uniquely in standing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الآخرة حسنة وقنا عذاب النار. والظاهر الاختلاف في الأفضلية لا في الجواز وإن الأخير أفضل لشموله، وإن التقييد بمن لا يحسن العربية ليس بشرط بل يجوز لمن يعرف الدعاء المعروف أن يقتصر على واحد مما ذكر لما علمت أن ظاهر الرواية عدم توقيته .
وأما حكمه إذا فات محله فنقول : إذا نسي القنوت حتى ركع ثم تذكر، فإن كان بعد رفع الرأس من الركوع لا يعود وسقط عنه القنوت وإن تذكره في الركوع فكذلك في ظاهر الرواية كما في البدائع وصححه في الخانية. وعن أبي يوسف أنه يعود إلى القنوت لشبهه بالقرآن كما لو ترك الفاتحة أو السورة فتذكرها في الركوع أو بعد رفع الرأس منه فإنه يعود وينتقض ركوعه والفرق على ظاهر الرواية أن نقض الركوع في المقيس عليه لإكماله لأنه يتكامل بقراءة الفاتحة والسورة لكونه لا يعتبر بدون القراءة أصلاً، وفي المقيس ليس نقضه لإكماله لأنه لا قنوت في سائر الصلوات والركوع معتبر ،بدونه، فلو نقض لكان نقض الفرض للواجب كذا في البدائع فإن عاد إلى القيام وقنت ولم يعد الركوع لم تفسد صلاته لأن ركوعه قائم لم يرتفض بخلاف المقيس عليه لأن بعوده صارت قراءة الكل فرضاً، والترتيب بين القراءة والركوع فرض، فارتفض ركوعه فلو لم يركع بطلت، فلو ركع وأدركه رجل في الركوع الثاني كان مدركاً لتلك الركعة وإنما لم يشرع القنوت في الركوع مثل تكبيرات العيد إذا تذكرها في حال الركوع حيث يكبر فيه لأنه لم يشرع إلا في محض القيام غير معقول المعنى فلا يتعدى إلى ما هو قيام من وجه دون وجه وهو الركوع، وأما تكبيرات العيد فلم تختص بمحض القيام لأن تكبيرة الركوع يؤتى بها في حال الانحطاط وهي محسوبة من تكبيرات العيد بإجماع الصحابة، فإذا جاز أداء واحدة منها في غير محض القيام من غير عذر جاز أداء الباقي مع قيام العذر بالأولى. ولم يقيد المصنف القنوت بالمخافتة للاختلاف
المنبع وغيره مما ذكر . ثم ذكر أن في بعض النسخ «ونخلع» ونسبها أيضاً إلى الوانية ثم قال : ولعله «نخنع» بالنون أي نخضع .
أنه
قوله : (أصلاً) قيد لقوله بدون القراءة لا لقوله لا يعتبر أي أنه إذا فقدت القراءة أصلاً لا يعتبر، وقيد به لأنه لو وجد من القراءة آية واحدة يكون الركوع بعدها معتبراً قوله : (لكان نقض الفرض للواجب) قد يقال هو كذلك فيما لو عاد لقراءة السورة فإن أجيب بما يذكره المؤلف من بعوده صارت قراءة الكل فرضاً يقال عليه أنه لا يصير فرضاً إلا بعد القراءة، وأما قبلها فهو واجب فإذا رفض الركوع يكون رفض الفرض للواجب فيكون كرفضه للقنوت إلا أن يقال : فرق بين ما هو واجب حالاً ومآلاً وما هو واجب حالاً فرض مآلاً فرفض الركوع لما يكون فرضاً وإن كان قبل الشروع فيه واجباً ليس كرفضه إلى ما هو واجب على كل حال قوله : (حيث يكبر فيه) كذا في شرح المنية لابن أمير حاج الحلبي ومشى عليه في متن التنوير من باب العيد والذي في شرح المنية للشيخ
The Hereafter is good and save us from the punishment of the Fire. Apparently the difference is in preference, not permissibility, and the latter is better due to its comprehensiveness. Restricting to one who does not know Arabic is not a condition; rather it is permissible for one who knows the well-known supplication to confine himself to one of what was mentioned, because the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) does not specify it. As for its ruling when its time is missed, we say: If he forgot the qunut until he bowed and then remembered, if it is after raising his head from bowing, he does not return and the qunut is dropped. If he remembers while bowing, it is the same in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) as in al-Bada'i' and al-Khaniyya. From Abu Yusuf: he returns to qunut because of its resemblance to the Quran, just as if he left the Fatiha or a sura and remembered it while bowing or after raising his head, he returns and his bowing is invalidated. The difference according to the apparent narration is that invalidating bowing in the analogized case is for its completion, because it is completed by reciting the Fatiha and sura, as it is not considered without recitation at all. But in the case of analogy, invalidating it is not for its completion, because there is no qunut in other prayers, and bowing is considered without it. So if he invalidated it, it would be invalidating a fard for a wajib, as in al-Bada'i'. If he returns to standing and performs qunut and does not repeat the bowing, his prayer is not invalid because his bowing remains valid, unlike the analogized case because by returning, all recitation becomes fard, and the order between recitation and bowing is fard, so his bowing is invalidated. If he does not bow, it becomes invalid. If he bows and a man catches him in the second bowing, he has caught that rak'ah. Qunut is not prescribed in bowing, unlike Eid takbirs when one remembers them while bowing, where he says the takbir in bowing, because qunut is only prescribed in pure standing, its meaning is not rationally understood, so it does not extend to what is standing in one aspect and not in another, i.e., bowing. As for Eid takbirs, they are not exclusive to pure standing because the takbir for bowing is performed during lowering and is counted among the Eid takbirs by consensus of the Companions. Since it is permissible to perform one of them in other than pure standing without an excuse, it is even more permissible to perform the rest with the excuse present. The author did not restrict qunut to quietness due to disagreement... Then he mentioned that in some copies 'wa nakhla'u' and attributed it to al-Waniyya, then said: perhaps it is 'nakhna'u' with a nun, i.e., we humble ourselves. He said: (aslan) is a restriction to his saying 'without recitation', not to his saying 'it is not considered', meaning when recitation is entirely absent, it is not considered. It is restricted because if one verse of recitation is found, the bowing after it is considered. He said: (then it would be invalidating fard for wajib) it might be said so in the case of returning to recite the sura, but if answered by what the author mentions of his return making all recitation fard, it is objected that it does not become fard except after recitation; before that it is wajib. So if he nullifies bowing, he nullifies fard for wajib, similar to nullifying for qunut. But it is said: there is a difference between what is wajib presently and eventually, and what is wajib presently and fard eventually. So nullifying bowing for what will be fard, even if before starting it is wajib, is not like nullifying it for what is wajib in all circumstances. He said: (where he says the takbir in it) as in Sharh al-Munya by Ibn Amir Haj al-Halabi, and he followed it in the text of al-Tanwir from the chapter of Eid, and what is in Sharh al-Munya by the Shaykh.
Source pages p. 75

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the situation when a person forgets the qunut (supplication) in witr prayer and remembers it after having bowed. The Hanafi position (zahir al-riwaya) is that he does not return to perform qunut, whether he remembers after raising his head from ruku' or while in ruku'. The reason is that qunut is an independent supplication not integral to the rak'ah, unlike recitation of the Quran. However, Imam Abu Yusuf holds that he should return to qunut because qunut resembles Quran recitation, analogizing to the case of forgetting the Fatiha or a sura: if one remembers after ruku', he returns and his ruku' is invalidated. The text then explains the distinction: recitation is essential for the validity of the rak'ah; without it, the bowing is not considered. In the case of qunut, bowing is valid without it, so returning would mean invalidating an obligatory act (fard) for an obligatory but lesser act (wajib), which is not allowed. The passage also draws a comparison with Eid takbirs: if one forgets a takbir and remembers while bowing, he says the takbir in bowing and does not return to standing, because Eid takbirs are not exclusive to standing and can be performed in bowing by consensus. The difference is that qunut is only prescribed during pure standing and its meaning is not rationally understood, so it cannot be extended to bowing. The text also discusses textual variants and grammatical points.

Key Terms
القنوت (al-qunut): The supplication recited in the witr prayer, typically after ruku' in the last rak'ah, asking for forgiveness and guidance.
الوتر (al-witr): The odd-numbered prayer performed after the night prayer (isha), consisting of three rak'at, with a specific recitation and qunut.
الركوع (al-ruku'): Bowing in prayer, a pillar (rukn) of salah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person forgets qunut in witr and remembers after raising his head from ruku', what does he do according to the zahir al-riwaya?
A) He returns to standing and performs qunut.
B) He does not return; the qunut is dropped.
C) He performs sajda sahw and continues.
D) He repeats the entire prayer.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling: if the time for qunut (standing after ruku') passes, it is dropped; the distinction between fard (Quran recitation) and wajib (qunut) is critical.

Recitation in Witr and Loudness of Qunut
Explains obligatory and recommended recitation in witr and ruling on jahr/ikhfa' in qunut

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the required recitation in each rak'ah of witr (fard: one verse; wajib: Fatihah + three verses) and explain the Hanafi preferred ruling on jahr/ikhfa' in qunut with Quranic and hadith proofs.

Core Idea
In witr, each rak'ah requires a verse (fard), Fatihah + three verses (wajib), and specific surahs are sunnah; qunut is preferred silently.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains two key rulings for witr prayer: the obligatory and recommended recitation in each rak'ah, and whether the qunut supplication should be recited loudly or quietly. It synthesizes opinions from Abu Hanifa and his disciples, provides Quranic proofs, and notes the intra-Hanafi debate on qunut loudness, concluding with the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its rulings
Extract from the passage the rulings for recitation per rak'ah (fard/wajib/sunnah) and for qunut (jahr/ikhfa'). Note that recitation is mandatory in every rak'ah of witr by consensus.
The passage states: 'reciting a verse in each rak'ah of it is fard, and specifying the Fatihah along with reciting three verses in each rak'ah is wajib, and the three surahs are sunnah.'
2
Locate the dalil for each ruling
For recitation, the verse 'So recite what is easy from the Quran' (73:20) is cited to show that any verse suffices as fard. For qunut quietness, the verse 'Call upon your Lord in humility and privately' (7:55) and the hadith 'The best supplication is hidden' are used.
The dalil_block in the toolbox provides these references.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The verse of supplication indicates that qunut, being a supplication, should be performed quietly to follow the general command. The verse of 'easy recitation' shows that specific surahs are not obligatory, avoiding the misconception that certain surahs are fard.
The term 'خفية' (privately) is the operative word for ikhfa'.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
For qunut loudness, some Hanafis (e.g., from Transoxiana) prefer ikhfa', while others allow jahr for teaching purposes. For recitation, Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn agree on the outcome but differ in reasoning: Abu Hanifa views witr as wajib with nafl possibility, so recitation is obligatory in all rak'at; the Sahibayn view witr as nafl, so recitation is fard by default.
The dispute does not affect the final mufta bihi; see the madhhab_dispute_map.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon position is ikhfa' for qunut, as stated in al-Hidayah and preferred by later scholars. For recitation, the consensus is that each rak'ah requires at least one verse (fard) and adding Fatihah plus three verses is wajib; specific surahs are sunnah and one should vary them to avoid misconception.
Al-Hidayah states that the preferred choice is quietness. The passage also warns against regularly reciting the same surah.

Source Text

٧٦ كتاب الصلاة باب الوتر والنوافل في كل ركعة منه فاتحة الكتاب وسورة ولا يقنت في غيره ويتبع المؤتم قانت الوتر لا الفجر فيه . قال في الذخيرة : استحسنوا الجهر في بلاد العجم للإمام ليتعلموا كما جهر عمر رضي الله عنه بالثناء حين قدم عليه وفد العراق ونص في الهداية على أن المختار المخافتة، وفي المحيط على أنه الأصح وفي البدائع واختار مشايخنا بما وراء النهر الإخفاء في دعاء القنوت في حق الإمام والقوم جميعاً لقوله تعالى ادعوا ربكم تضرعا وخفية [الأعراف : ٥٥] وقول النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم «خير الدعاء الخفي وهو مروي في صحيح ابن حبان. وفصل بعضهم بين يكون القوم لا يعلمونه فالأفضل للامام الجهر ليتعلموا وإلا فالإخفاء أفضل كما في الذخيرة، ومن اختار الجهر به اختار أن يكون دون جهر القراءة كما في منية المصلي.
أن
قوله (وقرأ في كل ركعة منه فاتحة الكتاب وسورة بيان لمخالفته للفرائض فيقرأ في كل ركعة منه حتماً، ونقل في الهداية أنه بالاجماع وفي التجنيس : لو ترك القراءة في الركعة الثالثة منه لم يجز في قولهم جميعاً .اهـ. أما عندهما فلأنه نفل وفي النفل تجب القراءة في الكل، وكذا على قول أبي حنيفة لأن الوتر عنده واجب يحتمل أنه نفل ولكن يترجح جهة الفرضية بدليل فيه شبهة فكان الاحتياط فيه وجوب القراءة في الكل، وقد قدمنا من فعله صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه كان يقرأ في الركعة الأولى سبح اسم ربك الأعلى وفي الثانية قل يا أيها الكافرون» وفي الثالثة «قل هو الله أحد». فالحاصل أن قراءة آية في كل ركعة منه فرض وتعيين الفاتحة مع قراءة ثلاث آيات في كل ركعة واجب والسور الثلاث فيه سنة لكن ذكر في النهاية أنه لا ينبغي أن يقرأ سورة متعينة على الدوام لأن الفرض هو مطلق القراءة بقوله تعالى فاقرؤوا ما تيسر من القرآن ﴾ [المزمل : ٢٠] والتعيين على الدوام يفضي إلى أن يعتقد بعض الناس أنه واجب وأنه لا يجوز غيره لكن لو قرأ بما ورد به الآثار
إبراهيم الحلبي أنه يعود إلى القيام فيكبر فيه فإنه قال : لكن الفرق بين القنوت وبين تكبيرات العيد مشكل حيث ذكروا أنه لو تذكر أنه تركها وهو في الركوع يعود إلى القيام على ما أشار إليه في الكافي، وكذا في تلخيص الجامع الكبير وصرح به في شرحه . والذي ذكره في التلخيص أنه يجوز رفض ركن لم يتم لأجل واجب لم يفت محله، فعلى هذا جاز رفض الركوع لأنه لم يتم لأن تمامه بالرفع لأجل تكبير العيد لأنه واجب لم يفت محله من كل وجه لأن الراكع قائم حكماً فيقال القنوت أيضاً كذلك، ولم أر من تعرض للفرق والذي يظهر أنه كون تكبير العيد مجتمعاً عليه دون القنوت والله أعلم انتهى. ويخالف هذا كله ما سيذكره المؤلف في باب صلاة العيدين حيث قال: ولو أدركه في القيام فلم يكبر حتى ركع لا يكبر في الركوع على الصحيح كما لو ركع الإمام قبل أن يكون فإن الإمام لا يكبر في الركوع ولا يعود إلى القيام ليكبر في ظاهر الرواية ا هـ . ومثله في شرح المنية لابن أمير حاج في باب العيد حيث قال : وإن تذكر في الركوع ففي ظاهر الرواية لا يكبر ويمضي على صلاته، وعلى ما ذكره الكرخي ومشى عليه صاحب البدائع وهو رواية النوادر يعود إلى القيام ويكبر ويعيد الركوع ولا يعيد في الفصلين القراءة ا.هـ. وعلى هذا الذي هو ظاهر الرواية لا حاجة إلى إبداء
Book of Prayer, Chapter of Witr and Supererogatory Prayers: 'In every rak'ah of it (recite) Fatihah of the Book and a surah, and he does not perform qunut in other than it, and the follower follows the qunut of the witr, not the Fajr.' It is said in al-Dhakhira: They considered it good for the imam to recite loudly in non-Arab lands so that they can learn, just as 'Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) recited the praise loudly when the delegation of Iraq came to him. Al-Hidayah states that the preferred choice is quietness. In al-Muhit, it is said that it is the most correct. In al-Bada'i', our scholars from Transoxiana chose concealment (ikhfa') in the qunut supplication for both the imam and the people, based on the verse 'Call upon your Lord in humility and privately' (al-A'raf 7:55) and the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him) 'The best supplication is the hidden one,' which is related in Sahih Ibn Hibban. Some distinguished: if the people do not know it, then it is better for the imam to recite loudly so that they learn; otherwise, concealment is better, as in al-Dhakhira. And whoever chooses loudness chooses that it be lower than the loudness of recitation, as in Munyat al-Musalli. That: His saying (and he recites in every rak'ah of it Fatihah of the Book and a surah) is an explanation of its difference from the obligatory prayers; so he recites in every rak'ah of it necessarily. It is transmitted in al-Hidayah that it is by consensus, and in al-Tajnïs: If he leaves recitation in the third rak'ah of it, it is not valid in the view of all of them. As for the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is because it is supererogatory (nafl), and in supererogatory prayers, recitation is obligatory in all rak'at. Similarly, according to Abu Hanifa, because witr in his view is wajib, but it bears the possibility of being nafl; however, the aspect of obligation preponderates due to evidence containing ambiguity, so the precaution is to require recitation in all. We have previously mentioned from his (peace be upon him) practice that he used to recite in the first rak'ah 'Glorify the name of your Lord, the Most High', in the second 'Say, O disbelievers', and in the third 'Say, He is Allah, the One'. So the conclusion is that reciting a verse in each rak'ah of it is fard, and specifying the Fatihah along with reciting three verses in each rak'ah is wajib, and the three surahs are sunnah therein. But it is mentioned in al-Nihāya that one should not recite a specific surah regularly, because the fard is absolute recitation according to the verse 'So recite what is easy from the Quran' (al-Muzzammil 73:20), and regular specification would lead some people to believe it is obligatory and that nothing else is permissible. However, if one recites as reported in the traditions: Ibrahim al-Halabi that he returns to standing and says the takbir in it, for he said: But the difference between qunut and Eid takbirs is problematic, where they mentioned that if he remembers that he left them while bowing, he returns to standing as indicated in al-Kafi, and similarly in Talkhis al-Jami' al-Kabir and he stated it in his commentary. What is mentioned in al-Talkhis is that it is permissible to abandon an incomplete pillar for the sake of a wajib whose time has not passed from all aspects, because although he is bowing, he is virtually standing. So it is said that qunut is also similar. And I have not seen anyone address the difference, and what appears is that the Eid takbirs are agreed upon while qunut is not. And Allah knows best. End. And this all contradicts what the author will mention in the chapter of the two Eids, where he said: 'If he catches him in standing and does not say the takbir until he bows, he does not say the takbir in bowing according to the correct view, just as if the imam bows before he was, then the imam does not say the takbir in bowing and does not return to standing to say it in the apparent narration.' Similarly in Sharh al-Munya by Ibn Amir Haj in the chapter of Eid, where he said: 'And if he remembers while bowing, in the apparent narration he does not say the takbir and proceeds with his prayer, and according to what al-Karkhi mentioned and followed by the author of al-Bada'i', which is a transmission from al-Nawadir, he returns to standing, says the takbir, and repeats the bowing, and does not repeat the recitation in the two parts.' And upon this which is the apparent narration, there is no need to initiate...
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage covers two main rulings regarding witr prayer. First, it establishes that in every rak'ah of witr, recitation of Fatihah and an additional surah is required (hatman), and this is by consensus. It explains that according to Abu Hanifa, witr is wajib with a shade of nafl, but to be safe, recitation in all rak'at is obligatory. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, since witr is nafl, recitation in all rak'at is fard by analogy to supererogatory prayers. The specific three surahs (al-A'la, al-Kafirun, al-Ikhlas) are sunnah, but it is not recommended to stick to them constantly to avoid misconception that they are obligatory. The minimum fard is one verse per rak'ah. Second, the passage discusses whether qunut should be recited loudly (jahr) or quietly (ikhfa'). The majority of Hanafi scholars prefer quietness based on Quran and hadith, but some allow loudness if the congregation needs to learn. If loud, it should be lower than the loudness of Quran recitation. The passage ends with a return to the earlier discussion about Eid takbirs, noting a contradiction with what the author will later mention, and suggesting that the apparent narration (zahir al-riwaya) is to not return to standing.

Key Terms
الجهر (al-jahr): Loud recitation, i.e., raising the voice in qunut such that others can hear.
الإخفاء (al-ikhfa'): Quiet recitation, i.e., saying qunut in a low voice.
الفاتحة (al-Fatihah): The opening chapter of the Quran, recited in every rak'ah of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on reciting the specific surahs (al-A'la, al-Kafirun, al-Ikhlas) in witr?
A) They are fard (obligatory) in each rak'ah.
B) They are sunnah (recommended) but not obligatory, and one should avoid reciting them constantly.
C) They are wajib (necessary) and omitting them requires sajdah sahw.
D) They are not allowed because the Prophet only recited them once.

Key Takeaway
In witr, reciting at least one verse per rak'ah is fard, adding Fatihah and three verses is wajib, and the three specific surahs are sunnah; qunut should be recited quietly according to the preferred Hanafi view.
