Qunut in Witr: Exclusivity and Method of Recitation
Explains that qunut is only in Witr, not Fajr, and discusses whether to recite audibly or silently.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qunut in Witr, identify the preferred method of recitation (jahr vs. ikhfa'), and apply the dalil from Quran and hadith to support the ruling.

Core Idea
Silent qunut is preferred in Hanafi Witr, but jahr is allowed when needed for teaching.

Qunut is a special supplication recited in Witr prayer. This lesson examines its exclusivity to Witr and the debate over whether the imam should recite it aloud or silently. We will explore the Hanafi position and its proofs, including the difference of opinion within the school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The matn states that qunut is only performed in Witr, not in other prayers. The ruling is that qunut is Sunnah Mu'akkadah in Witr.
2
Locate the dalil
Two evidences are cited: Quran 7:55 (calling upon Allah humbly and secretly) and the hadith 'The best supplication is the hidden one' narrated in Sahih Ibn Hibban.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The command to supplicate 'secretly' indicates that hidden supplication is better, hence qunut should be recited silently (ikhfa').
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some Hanafi sources (al-Dhakhirah) allow jahr (audible recitation) when the congregation does not know the du'a, citing the practice of Umar.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is silence (ikhfa') for both imam and congregation, but jahr is permitted for teaching, and if done, should be softer than Quran recitation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
في كل ركعة منه فاتحة الكتاب وسورة ولا يقنت في غيره ويتبع المؤتم قانت الوتر لا الفجر فيه . قال في الذخيرة : استحسنوا الجهر في بلاد العجم للإمام ليتعلموا كما جهر عمر رضي الله عنه بالثناء حين قدم عليه وفد العراق ونص في الهداية على أن المختار المخافتة، وفي المحيط على أنه الأصح وفي البدائع واختار مشايخنا بما وراء النهر الإخفاء في دعاء القنوت في حق الإمام والقوم جميعاً لقوله تعالى ادعوا ربكم تضرعا وخفية [الأعراف : ٥٥] وقول النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم «خير الدعاء الخفي وهو مروي في صحيح ابن حبان. وفصل بعضهم بين يكون القوم لا يعلمونه فالأفضل للامام الجهر ليتعلموا وإلا فالإخفاء أفضل كما في الذخيرة، ومن اختار الجهر به اختار أن يكون دون جهر القراءة كما في منية المصلي.
In every rak'ah of it is the Opening of the Book and a surah, and he does not perform qunut in other than it, and the follower follows the one performing qunut in Witr, not in Fajr. It is said in al-Dhakhirah: They considered it good for the imam to recite aloud in non-Arab lands so that they may learn, just as Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) recited aloud the praise when the delegation of Iraq came to him. And it is stated in al-Hidayah that the preferred is silence, and in al-Muhit that it is the most correct, and in al-Bada'i that our scholars from Transoxiana chose silence in the qunut supplication for both the imam and the congregation due to His statement: 'Call upon your Lord humbly and secretly' [Al-A'raf: 55] and the statement of the Prophet ﷺ: 'The best supplication is the hidden one,' and it is narrated in Sahih Ibn Hibban. And some differentiated: if the people do not know it, then it is better for the imam to recite aloud so they may learn; otherwise, silence is better, as in al-Dhakhirah. And whoever chooses reciting aloud should do so in a tone lower than the recitation of the Quran, as in Munyat al-Musalli.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding qunut in Witr prayer. The matn states that qunut is performed only in Witr, not in other prayers, and the follower should follow the imam in qunut specifically in Witr, not in Fajr. The commentary from various Hanafi sources discusses whether the imam should recite the qunut supplication aloud or silently. There is a difference of opinion: al-Dhakhirah recommends loud recitation in non-Arab lands so that people learn, citing Umar's practice. However, al-Hidayah and al-Muhit state that silence is the preferred or most correct opinion. The scholars of Transoxiana chose silence for both imam and congregation, based on the Quranic verse commanding humble and hidden supplication and the hadith that the best supplication is hidden. A compromise is mentioned: if the congregation does not know the qunut, the imam should recite aloud for teaching purposes; otherwise, silence is better. If one does recite aloud, it should be softer than the recitation of the Quran.

Key Terms
القنوت (al-qunut): A special supplication recited in certain prayers, specifically Witr in Hanafi school.
الجهر (al-jahr): Audible recitation, as opposed to silent recitation (ikhfa').
الإخفاء (al-ikhfa'): Silent recitation, the recommended method for qunut.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the preferred method for the imam to recite the qunut supplication in Witr?
A) Audibly, louder than Quran recitation.
B) Silently (ikhfa') in most cases.
C) Only audibly when alone.
D) It must be recited silently at all times.

Key Takeaway
Qunut in Witr is preferably recited silently, but jahr is allowed for teaching, based on the Quranic command to supplicate in secret and the prophetic guidance that the best supplication is hidden.

Witr Recitation: Fard, Wajib, and Sunnah Levels
Commentary on the recitation rulings in Witr with intra-Hanafi rationale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on recitation in Witr (fard/wajib/sunnah) and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the basis for mandatory recitation.

Core Idea
In Witr, reciting any verse in each rak'ah is fard, adding Fatiha and three verses is wajib, and the three specific surahs are sunnah.

This passage from Bahr al-Raiq examines the recitation requirements in Witr prayer. It clarifies that while all three Hanafi imams agree on the necessity of recitation in every rak'ah, they differ on the underlying nature of Witr—whether it is nafl (Sahibayn) or wajib (Abu Hanifa). This disagreement leads to the same practical ruling but through different rationales. The text also distinguishes between fard, wajib, and sunnah elements in recitation and provides guidance against rigidly repeating specific surahs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling on recitation in Witr
State that recitation in every rak'ah of Witr is mandatory by consensus among the three Hanafi imams. Note that this differs from fard prayers where recitation is only in the first two rak'ahs.
The matn explicitly says 'and he recited in every rak'ah of it the Opening of the Book and a surah'.
2
Unpack the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Understand the reasoning: Sahibayn view Witr as nafl, so recitation in every rak'ah is required as in supererogatory prayers. Abu Hanifa views Witr as wajib but with suspicion of nafl, so precaution demands recitation in every rak'ah.
The text mentions the same ruling but different talil.
3
Distinguish the levels of obligation
The commentator breaks down: fard (any verse), wajib (specifically Fatiha plus three verses), and sunnah (the three surahs: Al-A'la, Al-Kafirun, Al-Ikhlas).
This is a practical breakdown for the worshipper.
4
Apply the caution from al-Nihayah
Recognize that continuous recitation of the same surahs should be avoided to prevent people from thinking it is obligatory. It is permissible to recite them occasionally.
The fard is absolute recitation; specification is only wajib and continuous practice may lead to false belief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وقرأ في كل ركعة منه فاتحة الكتاب وسورة بيان لمخالفته للفرائض فيقرأ في كل ركعة منه حتماً، ونقل في الهداية أنه بالاجماع وفي التجنيس : لو ترك القراءة في الركعة الثالثة منه لم يجز في قولهم جميعاً .اهـ. أما عندهما فلأنه نفل وفي النفل تجب القراءة في الكل، وكذا على قول أبي حنيفة لأن الوتر عنده واجب يحتمل أنه نفل ولكن يترجح جهة الفرضية بدليل فيه شبهة فكان الاحتياط فيه وجوب القراءة في الكل، وقد قدمنا من فعله صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه كان يقرأ في الركعة الأولى سبح اسم ربك الأعلى وفي الثانية قل يا أيها الكافرون» وفي الثالثة «قل هو الله أحد». فالحاصل أن قراءة آية في كل ركعة منه فرض وتعيين الفاتحة مع قراءة ثلاث آيات في كل ركعة واجب والسور الثلاث فيه سنة لكن ذكر في النهاية أنه لا ينبغي أن يقرأ سورة متعينة على الدوام لأن الفرض هو مطلق القراءة بقوله تعالى فاقرؤوا ما تيسر من القرآن ﴾ [المزمل : ٢٠] والتعيين على الدوام يفضي إلى أن يعتقد بعض الناس أنه واجب وأنه لا يجوز غيره لكن لو قرأ بما ورد به الآثار أحياناً يكون حسناً، ولكن لا يواظب لما ذكرنا .اهـ.
His statement: (And he recited in every rak'ah of it the Opening of the Book and a surah) is an explanation of its departure from the obligatory prayers, so he recites in every rak'ah of it necessarily. It was transmitted in al-Hidayah that it is by consensus, and in al-Tajnis: If he left the recitation in the third rak'ah of it, it is not permissible in the view of all of them. As for in the view of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is because it is a supererogatory prayer, and in supererogatory prayers, recitation is obligatory in all of it. Similarly, according to Abu Hanifa, because Witr in his view is obligatory but it is possible that it is supererogatory, yet the aspect of obligation prevails due to an evidence containing ambiguity, so precaution dictates the obligation of recitation in all of it. We have already presented from his practice ﷺ that he used to recite in the first rak'ah 'Glorify the name of your Lord the Most High', in the second 'Say, O disbelievers', and in the third 'Say, He is Allah, the One'. The conclusion is that reciting a verse in every rak'ah of it is fard, specifying the Fatiha along with reciting three verses in every rak'ah is wajib, and the three surahs are Sunnah. But it is mentioned in al-Nihayah that one should not recite a specific surah continuously, because the fard is absolute recitation by His statement: 'So recite what is easy of the Quran' [Al-Muzzammil: 20], and continuous specification leads people to believe it is obligatory and that nothing else is permissible. However, if one recites as reported in the traditions sometimes, it is good, but he should not persist in it for what we mentioned.
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the recitation in Witr prayer. The matn states that in every rak'ah of Witr, one recites Fatiha and a surah. The commentator explains that this is a departure from obligatory prayers where recitation is not required in every rak'ah. He notes that the ruling is unanimous among the three imams that recitation in every rak'ah is mandatory, but their reasoning differs. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider Witr a supererogatory prayer (nafl), and in nafl, recitation is obligatory in every rak'ah. Abu Hanifa holds Witr to be wajib, but it has an aspect of nafl, so the precaution is to require recitation in all. The Prophet's practice is cited: he recited specific surahs (Al-A'la, Al-Kafirun, Al-Ikhlas). Then the commentator distinguishes levels: reciting one verse in each rak'ah is fard (obligatory), reciting Fatiha plus three verses is wajib (mandatory but not fard), and reciting the three specific surahs is Sunnah. He adds a caution from al-Nihayah: one should not continuously recite the same surahs to avoid people thinking it is obligatory. It is permissible occasionally but not persistently.

Key Terms
الوتر (al-witr): The Witr prayer, a prayer performed after Isha with odd number of rak'ahs, considered wajib in Hanafi school.
النفل (al-nafl): Supererogatory prayer, not obligatory but recommended.
الفاتحة (al-fatihah): The Opening chapter of the Quran, recited in every rak'ah of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on reciting Fatiha and a surah in each rak'ah of Witr?
A) It is Sunnah, recommended but not required.
B) It is fard to recite at least one verse, and wajib to recite Fatiha plus three verses.
C) It is makruh to recite more than one surah.
D) The recitation is identical to Fajr prayer.

Key Takeaway
In Witr, recitation in every rak'ah is mandatory; the fard is any verse, the wajib is Fatiha plus three verses, and the specific surahs are sunnah; avoid continuously reciting the same surah to prevent misconception.

Witr as Nafl: First Tashahhud and Qada in Disliked Times
Discusses the nature of Witr as nafl regarding recitation, ruling on first tashahhud, and qada in disliked times.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the first tashahhud is not obligatory in Witr, apply the rule on returning when forgotten, and identify the ruling on qada in disliked times based on the nafl aspect.

Core Idea
Witr's nafl aspect makes the first tashahhud non-obligatory and qada in disliked times prohibited.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains that Witr shares characteristics with both fard and nafl prayers. The scholars favored the nafl aspect regarding recitation, leading to specific rulings: the first tashahhud is not obligatory, and missing Witr should not be made up in times when nafl is prohibited. We will explore the reasoning and practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dual nature of Witr
Recognize that Witr is considered wajib but shares some rulings with nafl prayers. The text states that scholars gave weight to the nafl aspect out of precaution in recitation.
This dual nature is key to understanding the subsequent rulings.
2
Extract the ruling on the first tashahhud
From the quotes of al-Mujtaba and al-Imtihan, determine that the first tashahhud is not obligatory in Witr. If forgotten during the second rak'ah and remembered in ruku', one does not return.
Contrast with fard prayers where the first tashahhud is wajib and requires return if remembered before the next rukn.
3
Understand the ruling on qada in disliked times
Because Witr is like nafl in terms of recitation, making up a missed Witr is prohibited in times when nafl is prohibited (e.g., after Fajr and after Asr). This is a precaution due to the nafl aspect.
Note that al-Tajnis has a differing view, but the relied-upon position is to avoid qada in these times.
4
Apply the forgetfulness scenario
If a person forgets the first tashahhud in Witr and remembers while in ruku' of the third rak'ah, they should not return. If they mistakenly return, their ruku' remains valid.
This ruling highlights the flexibility introduced by the nafl aspect.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد يقال : إنهم رجحوا جهة النفلية فيه احتياطاً في القراءة فينبغي أن لا يقضي في الوقت المكروه كما بعد طلوع الفجر وبعد صلاة العصر احتياطاً لجهة النفلية لأن النفل فيه ممنوع ، وقد قدمنا عن التجنيس خلافه وفيه : والوتر بمنزلة النفل في حق القراءة إلا أنه يشبه المغرب من حيث إنه لو استتم قائماً في الثالثة قبل القعود ثم تذكر لا يعود لأنها صلاة واحدة، وفي النفل يعود لأنه كل شفع صلاة على حدة اه... وفي المجتبى : ولا تجب القعدة الأولى في الوتر . وفي الامتحان : صلى الوتر ولم يقعد في الثانية ناسياً ثم تذكر في الركوع لا يعود وإن عاد لا ينتقض ركوعه .اهـ.
And it may be said: They favored the aspect of supererogatory prayer in it out of precaution in recitation, so one should not make it up in a disliked time, such as after the break of dawn and after the Asr prayer, as a precaution due to the supererogatory aspect, because supererogatory prayer is prohibited at those times. And we have already presented from al-Tajnis a differing view: In it: Witr is like supererogatory prayer with respect to recitation, except that it resembles Maghrib in that if he remains standing in the third rak'ah before sitting and then remembers, he does not return because it is one prayer, while in supererogatory prayer he returns because each pair is a separate prayer. In al-Mujtaba: The first sitting is not obligatory in Witr. In al-Imtihan: He prayed Witr and did not sit in the second rak'ah out of forgetfulness, then remembered in the ruku'; he does not return, and if he returns, his ruku' is not invalidated.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage discusses several rulings related to the nature of Witr. It begins by stating that scholars gave more weight to the supererogatory (nafl) aspect of Witr in matters of recitation, and thus one should not perform qada (make-up) of Witr in disliked times like after Fajr and after Asr, because nafl prayers are prohibited at those times. However, it notes that al-Tajnis has a differing view. Then it compares Witr to Maghrib in that if someone remains standing in the third rak'ah before sitting (due to forgetfulness) and then remembers, he does not return to sitting because Witr is a single prayer, whereas in nafl he would return because each pair of rak'ahs is a separate prayer. Next, it quotes al-Mujtaba stating that the first tashahhud (sitting) is not obligatory in Witr. Finally, it quotes al-Imtihan: if someone prays Witr and forgets to sit in the second rak'ah, then remembers while in ruku', he does not return; if he does return, his ruku' is not invalidated.

Key Terms
القعدة الأولى (al-qa'dah al-ula): The first sitting for tashahhud after two rak'ahs, which is not obligatory in Witr.
النفلية (al-nafliyyah): The supererogatory nature of Witr in some aspects.
القضاء (al-qada'): Making up a missed prayer; here referring to making up Witr if missed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on the first tashahhud in Witr according to the Hanafi school?
A) It is wajib and cannot be omitted.
B) It is not obligatory; if forgotten, one does not return.
C) It is fard and invalidates the prayer if missed.
D) It is Sunnah but must be performed if remembered.

Key Takeaway
The first tashahhud is not obligatory in Witr, and qada in disliked times is discouraged due to Witr's nafl aspect.

Types of Supplication and the Dispute on Salawat in Qunut
Describes types of du'a and intra-Hanafi dispute on salawat in qunut.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the four types of supplication by their hand gestures and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on including salawat in qunut.

Core Idea
Not all supplications in prayer require raised palms — each type of du'a has a distinct gesture reflecting its purpose.

In this lesson, we explore a passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq that classifies supplications into four types, each with a specific hand posture, and then addresses a scholarly difference within the Hanafi school: should the imam send blessings upon the Prophet (salawat) during qunut in Witr? This intra-Hanafi dispute has practical implications for how imams lead the congregation. We will analyze the reasoning behind each position and understand why the author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq omitted the issue from the matn.

Guided Path
1
Classify the four types of du'a
Identify each type (raghbah, rahbah, tadarru', khufyah) and associate it with its prescribed hand gesture as stated in the passage.
The gestures are: palms up (raghbah), back of hands towards face (rahbah), specific finger circle (tadarru'), and internal without gesture (khufyah).
2
Locate the disputed ruling
Find the statement that the author (al-Nasafi in Kanz al-Daqa'iq) did not mention sending salawat in qunut due to ikhtilaf. Identify the two Hanafi positions: Abu al-Layth (preferable to include) and Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar (not to include).
The author's deliberate omission signals a known divergence.
3
Analyze the proofs
Examine the dalil for each position: Abu al-Layth argues that qunut is a supplication, and it is better to include salawat because supplication is more likely to be accepted when preceded by praise of the Prophet. Abu al-Qasim relies on reported practice and a narration from Ali (incomplete in the text).
The narration 'كل دعاء' likely ends with 'محجوب حتى يصلي على النبي' (every supplication is veiled until one sends blessings on the Prophet).
4
Determine the preferred view (tarjih)
The passage indicates that the view of Abu al-Layth is considered 'al-ula' (preferable), but it is not obligatory. This is the mufta bihi position.
Many later Hanafi fatwa collections adopt the recommendation to include salawat.
5
Assess practical application (thamarah al-khilaf)
Consider the effect: if an imam omits salawat, the qunut is still valid but missing a recommended element; if he includes it, it is more complete. Followers should follow the local practice.
This is a case of khilaf afdali (dispute about preference), not validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي النهاية معزياً إلى محمد بن الحنفية قال : الدعاء أربعة : دعاء رغبة ودعاء رهبة ودعاء تضرع ودعاء خفية . ففي دعاء الرغبة يجعل بطون كفيه نحو السماء، وفي دعاء الرهبة يجعل ظهر كفيه إلى وجهه كالمستغيث من الشيء، وفي دعاء التضرع يعقد الخنصر والبنصر ويحلق بالإبهام والوسطى ويشير بالسبابة، ودعاء الخفية ما يفعله المرء في نفسه . ولم يذكر المصنف الصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في القنوت للاختلاف فيها، واختار الفقيه أبو الليث أن الأولى الصلاة عليه لأن القنوت دعاء والأولى في الدعاء أن يكون مشتملاً عليها . وذهب أبو القاسم الصفار إلى أنه لا يصلي فيه لأنه ليس موضعها ومشى عليه في الخلاصة، ولما رواه الطبراني عن علي كل دعاء
And in al-Nihayah, attributed to Muhammad ibn al-Hanafiyyah, he said: Supplication is four types: supplication of desire, supplication of fear, supplication of humility, and supplication of secrecy. In supplication of desire, he places the palms of his hands towards the sky; in supplication of fear, he places the backs of his hands towards his face like one seeking refuge from something; in supplication of humility, he intertwines the little finger and ring finger, makes a circle with the thumb and middle finger, and points with the index finger; and supplication of secrecy is what one does in oneself. And the author did not mention sending blessings on the Prophet ﷺ in qunut due to the difference of opinion about it. Al-Faqih Abu al-Layth chose that it is preferable to send blessings because qunut is a supplication, and it is preferable for supplication to include it. Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar held that one should not send blessings because it is not its place, and this is followed in al-Khulasah, and due to what al-Tabarani narrated from Ali: 'Every supplication...'
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage covers two topics: the types of supplication with their associated hand gestures, and the dispute on whether to send salawat (blessings) on the Prophet during qunut. The first part, from Muhammad ibn al-Hanafiyyah, classifies du'a into four types: raghbah (desire), rahbah (fear), tadarru' (humility), and khufyah (secrecy). Each has a specific hand position: for raghbah, palms up; for rahbah, backs of hands towards face; for tadarru', specific finger gestures; for khufyah, internal without gestures. The second topic is the difference among Hanafi scholars regarding sending salawat in qunut. Abu al-Layth considers it preferable because qunut is a supplication and supplications should include praise of the Prophet. Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar disagrees, stating that qunut is not the place for it, and he is followed in al-Khulasah. The passage ends with an incomplete hadith from al-Tabarani that likely supports the second view.

Key Terms
دعاء الرغبة (du'a' al-raghbah): Supplication of desire, made with palms facing up.
الصلاة على النبي (al-salat 'ala al-nabi): Sending blessings upon the Prophet Muhammad, like saying 'Allahumma salli 'ala Muhammad'.
القنوت (al-qunut): A supplication recited in Witr, and by extension in some other prayers.
دعاء الرهبة (du'a' al-rahbah): Supplication of fear, palms reverse towards face.
دعاء التضرع (du'a' al-tadarru'): Supplication of humility with specific finger gesture.
دعاء الخفية (du'a' al-khufyah): Secret supplication within the heart, no gesture.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the view of Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar regarding sending salawat in qunut?
A) It is obligatory.
B) It is preferable.
C) It should not be done because qunut is not the place for it.
D) It is only for the imam.

Key Takeaway
Supplication types have distinct hand gestures, and while sending salawat in qunut is recommended by the preferred Hanafi view, it remains a legitimate area of scholarly difference.

Dispute on Qunut: Calamities vs Permanent
Presents Hanafi position on qunut and responds to Shafi'i argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that qunut is only for calamities and respond to the Shafi'i argument for permanent qunut.

Core Idea
Qunut in Witr is only for calamities, not a permanent sunnah — the Prophet's practice and the Companions' actions prove it.

This lesson examines a key disagreement between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: whether qunut in Witr is a permanent practice or reserved for times of calamity. The Hanafi school, following the majority of scholars, holds that qunut is only performed when a calamity (nāzilah) befalls the community. The opposing view, often associated with Imam al-Shafi‘ī, considers qunut in Witr a regular sunnah. The passage from al-Bahr al-Rā’iq presents the Hanafi evidence and explains why the conflicting reports are reconciled in this way.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: the Hanafi school holds that qunut is not a permanent feature of Witr but is performed only when a calamity occurs (qunut al-nawazil).
This applies to both the Witr prayer and Fajr (though the lesson focuses on Witr).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The opposing school (Shafi'i and others) holds that qunut in Witr is a regular sunnah performed throughout the year, regardless of calamities.
The difference is purely in the frequency of qunut, not its wording.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i rely on the hadith of Anas ibn Malik that the Prophet ﷺ never stopped performing qunut until he left the world, and on the practice of many Companions.
This hadith is transmitted by a number of compilers and is considered authentic by many.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school interprets the hadith of Anas as referring to qunut for calamities being continuous in principle, not that it was performed every night. The Prophet's stopping (as in the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud) indicates that qunut was abrogated or that no calamity occurred later. The Companions' qututs (Abu Bakr, Umar, etc.) were for specific events, not daily.
The Quranic verse 'Laysa laka min al-amri shay' (3:128) is cited as the reason for stopping.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, Hanafis do not recite qunut in Witr except during general calamities (like drought or war), while Shafi'is recite it every night throughout the year.
This difference also applies to qunut in Fajr, though the Hanafi view on that is also restricted to calamities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد أطال المحقق الخ) أقول : ذكر الشيخ إبراهيم الحلبي جملة مما في الفتح إلى أن قال : إن جميع ما ورد من قنوته الله و قنوت الخلفاء الراشدين وغيرهم مما اختلف فيه إنما هو قنوت النوازل فإنه محل الاجتهاد لأن حديث أنس أنه عليه السلام لم يزل يقنت حتى فارق الدنيا ونحوه مما عن الصحابة يثبته فإنه روي عن أبي بكر أنه قنت عند محاربة مسيلمة وكذلك قنت عمر وكذا علي ومعاوية عند تحاربهما، وحديث أبي حنيفة ونحوه أنه عليه السلام قنت شهراً ثم لم يقنت قبله ولا بعده ينفيه فوجب كون بقاء القنوت في النوازل أمراً مجتهداً فيه، وذلك أنه لم يؤثر عنه عليه السلام أنه قال لا قنوت في نازلة بعد هذه بل مجرد العدم بعدها فيتجه الاجتهاد بأن يظن أن ذلك إنما هو لرفع شرعيته ونسخه نظراً إلى سبب تركه عليه السلام وهو أنه لما أنزل ليس لك من الأمر شيء وأنه لعدم وقوع نازلة تستدعي القنوت بعدها فتكون شرعيته مستمرة وهو محمل قنوت من قنت من الصحابة بعد وفاته عليه الصلاة والسلام وهو مذهبنا وعليه الجمهور. قال الحافظ أبو جعفر الطحاوي: إنما لا
The researcher (al-Muhaqqiq) elaborated. I say: Shaykh Ibrahim al-Halabi mentioned a summary from al-Fath until he said: All that has been reported of his qunut and the qunut of the Rightly Guided Caliphs and others is only the qunut of calamities, for it is a matter of ijtihad. Because the hadith of Anas that he (peace be upon him) never stopped performing qunut until he left the world, and similar from the Companions, affirms it. It is narrated that Abu Bakr performed qunut at the war against Musaylimah, and similarly Umar, and also Ali and Mu'awiyah at their war. The hadith of Abu Hanifah and others that he performed qunut for a month and then did not perform it before or after contradicts it. So it became necessary that the continuation of qunut for calamities is a matter of ijtihad. Because it is not reported from him (peace be upon him) that he said there is no qunut after this calamity; rather, the mere absence after it leads to ijtihad that perhaps it was due to the abrogation of its legislation based on the reason for his leaving it, which is when 'You have no part in the matter' was revealed, or because no calamity requiring qunut occurred after it. Thus its legislation continues, and this is the interpretation of the qunut of the Companions after his death, and this is our madhhab and the majority. Al-Hafiz Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi said: It is not...
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi position on qunut, specifically that qunut is only for calamities (nawazil) and not a permanent feature of Witr. The commentator summarizes the argument from Ibrahim al-Halabi. The opposing view (often attributed to the Shafi'i school) holds that qunut in Witr is permanent and continuous. The Hanafi argument uses the hadith that the Prophet ﷺ performed qunut for a month and then stopped, indicating it was for a specific calamity. The narratives that the Prophet never stopped qunut are interpreted as referring to qunut for calamities. The Companions' qunut (Abu Bakr at war with Musaylimah, Umar, Ali, Mu'awiyah) are all for specific events. The text concludes that the continuation of qunut for calamities is an ijtihadi matter, and that the Hanafi school (along with the majority) holds that qunut is not intrinsic to Witr but only done when a calamity occurs.

Key Terms
قنوت النوازل (qunut al-nawazil): Qunut performed only when a calamity befalls the Muslim community.
الاجتهاد (al-ijtihad): Independent reasoning on a legal issue where evidence is not definitive.
النسخ (al-naskh): Abrogation of a ruling by a later revelation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is qunut performed in Witr?
A) Every night of the year.
B) Only during the last ten nights of Ramadan.
C) Only when a calamity befalls the community.
D) Only on Fridays.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, qunut in Witr is not a permanent sunnah but is reserved for times of calamity, based on the Prophet's practice and the interpretation of conflicting hadith.

The Obligatory Status of the First Sitting in Witr
Ruling on witr's resemblance to nafl and maghrib, and obligation of first sitting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the first sitting in witr prayer and explain the reasoning based on witr's resemblance to both fard and nafl.

Core Idea
The first sitting in witr is wajib because witr combines features of fard and nafl, both of which require it.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq, the author addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute: whether the first sitting (qa'dah ula) is obligatory in witr prayer. He critiques the view from al-Mujtabā and al-Imtiḥān that it is not obligatory, arguing instead that since the first sitting is wajib in both fard and nafl, and witr shares characteristics with both, it must be wajib in witr as well.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
The specific issue is whether the first sitting after the second rak'ah in witr prayer is obligatory or not. This is a dispute within the Hanafi school.
2
Trace the evidence cited
The author mentions reports from al-Mujtabā and al-Imtiḥān that the first sitting is not obligatory. He then presents his counter-argument.
3
Analyze the analogy (talil)
The author argues that the first sitting is wajib in both fard and nafl. Witr resembles fard in being a single prayer (like Maghrib) and resembles nafl in recitation rules. By analogy, it should also be wajib in witr.
This is a qiyas based on the common illa of similarity.
4
Note the practical consequence
If the first sitting is wajib, forgetful omission requires sajdah al-sahw. If not obligatory, no compensation is needed. The author's view leads to a different ruling in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحياناً يكون حسناً، ولكن لا يواظب لما ذكرنا .اهـ. وقد يقال : إنهم رجحوا جهة النفلية فيه احتياطاً في القراءة فينبغي أن لا يقضي في الوقت المكروه كما بعد طلوع الفجر وبعد صلاة العصر احتياطاً لجهة النفلية لأن النفل فيه ممنوع ، وقد قدمنا عن التجنيس خلافه وفيه : والوتر بمنزلة النفل في حق القراءة إلا أنه يشبه المغرب من حيث إنه لو استتم قائماً في الثالثة قبل القعود ثم تذكر لا يعود لأنها صلاة واحدة، وفي النفل يعود لأنه كل شفع صلاة على حدة اه... وفي المجتبى : ولا تجب القعدة الأولى في الوتر . وفي الامتحان : صلى الوتر ولم يقعد في الثانية ناسياً ثم تذكر في الركوع لا يعود وإن عاد لا ينتقض ركوعه .اهـ. ولا يخفى ما فيه لأن القعدة الأولى واجبة في الفرض والنفل والوتر ذو شبه لهما فوجبت القعدة الأولى فيه، وقد تقدم أنه يرفع يديه عند تكبيرة القنوت كما يرفعها عند الافتتاح.
Sometimes it is good, but he does not persist due to what we mentioned. End. And it may be said: They gave preponderance to the aspect of nafl in it as a precaution in recitation, so one should not make it up in a disliked time, like after dawn and after Asr, as a precaution for the aspect of nafl because nafl is prohibited at those times. And we have previously reported from al-Tajnīs [that there is] a difference of opinion on it. And in it: Witr is like nafl in terms of recitation, except that it resembles Maghrib in that if he remains standing in the third [rak'ah] before sitting and then remembers, he does not return because it is a single prayer. In nafl he returns because each pair is a separate prayer. End. And in al-Mujtabā: The first sitting is not obligatory in witr. And in al-Imtiḥān: He prayed witr and did not sit in the second rak'ah forgetfully, then remembered in rukū'; he does not return, and if he returns his rukū' is not invalidated. End. And it is not hidden what is in it because the first sitting is obligatory in fard and nafl, and witr has resemblance to both, so the first sitting is obligatory in it. And it has preceded that he raises his hands at the takbīr of qunūt just as he raises them at the opening takbīr.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement on the nature of witr prayer and the obligation of the first sitting. The author begins by commenting on a previous point about something being 'good' but not persisted in, then discusses that scholars prefer treating witr as nafl for recitation purposes, hence one should not delay it to disliked times. Citing from al-Tajnīs, witr is like nafl in recitation but resembles Maghrib in being a single prayer: if one remains standing in the third rak'ah before sitting and then remembers, he does not return because it's one prayer, whereas in nafl he would return because each pair is a separate prayer. Then from al-Mujtabā, the first sitting is not obligatory in witr, and from al-Imtiḥān, if one forgets the second sitting and remembers in rukū', he does not return and returning does not invalidate his rukū'. The author criticizes this, arguing that the first sitting is obligatory in both fard and nafl, and witr resembles both, so it is obligatory in witr. Finally, it mentions that raising hands at takbīr al-qunūt is like raising them at the opening takbīr, a separate ruling. The author's critique shows that the relied-upon position is that the first sitting in witr is wajib, contrary to the view in al-Mujtabā.

Key Terms
الوتر (al-witr): The odd-numbered prayer performed after the night prayer, consisting of three rak'ahs in the Hanafi school, with a single taslīm.
القعدة الأولى (al-qa'dah al-ūlā): The first sitting (tashahhud) in prayers of three or four rak'ahs; in witr, it is the sitting after the second rak'ah.
النفل (al-nafl): Supererogatory prayer; here, each pair of rak'ahs is considered a separate prayer, unlike witr which is a single unit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the ruling on the first sitting in witr prayer?
A) It is not obligatory and may be omitted forgetfully without compensation.
B) It is obligatory (wajib), and forgetful omission requires prostration of forgetfulness.
C) It is a sunnah and its omission is disliked.
D) It is fard and invalidates the prayer if omitted.

Key Takeaway
The first sitting in witr is wajib; forgetful omission requires sujūd al-sahw.

Sending Salat upon the Prophet in Witr Qunut
Ruling on sending salat upon the Prophet in witr qunut

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the preferred Hanafi view on sending salat in witr qunut and explain the supporting hadith evidence.

Core Idea
A supplication without salat upon the Prophet is veiled from acceptance.

Does the witr qunut require sending blessings upon the Prophet? This lesson examines a respected difference of opinion within the Hanafi school. Al-Faqih Abu al-Layth preferred including it, while Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar disagreed. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq weighs the evidence and adopts the view that it is better to include salat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is sending salat upon the Prophet (salawat) within the witr qunut. The ruling is a matter of recommendation (mustahabb), not obligation.
The author uses 'al-ula' (better) indicating preference.
2
State the differing opinions
Two positions: Abu al-Layth al-Samarqandi said it is better to include salat; Abu al-Qasim al-Saffar said it is not the place for salat. The author sides with Abu al-Layth.
Al-Saffar's view was followed in al-Khulasa.
3
Locate the dalil
The hadith from al-Tabarani narrated from Ali: 'Every supplication is veiled until one sends salat upon Muhammad.'
This is an ahad hadith, zanni al-thubut.
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith implies that a supplication lacking salat is not accepted. Since qunut is a supplication, it should include salat to be complete.
The reasoning is that the general command to send salat in supplication applies specifically to qunut.
5
Note the tarjih and mufta bihi
The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and al-Waqi'at support including salat with the formula 'Allahumma salli ala Muhammad wa ala ali Muhammad.' This is the preferred (mufta bihi) view.
An odd ruling from al-Mujtaba is noted but not adopted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي النهاية معزياً إلى محمد بن الحنفية قال : الدعاء أربعة : دعاء رغبة ودعاء رهبة ودعاء تضرع ودعاء خفية . ففي دعاء الرغبة يجعل بطون كفيه نحو السماء، وفي دعاء الرهبة يجعل ظهر كفيه إلى وجهه كالمستغيث من الشيء، وفي دعاء التضرع يعقد الخنصر والبنصر ويحلق بالإبهام والوسطى ويشير بالسبابة، ودعاء الخفية ما يفعله المرء في نفسه . ولم يذكر المصنف الصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في القنوت للاختلاف فيها، واختار الفقيه أبو الليث أن الأولى الصلاة عليه لأن القنوت دعاء والأولى في الدعاء أن يكون مشتملاً عليها . وذهب أبو القاسم الصفار إلى أنه لا يصلي فيه لأنه ليس موضعها ومشى عليه في الخلاصة، ولما رواه الطبراني عن علي كل دعاء محجوب حتى يصلي على محمد وفي الواقعات : ويستحب في كل دعاء أن تكون فيه الصلاة على النبي اللهم صلي على محمد وعلى آل محمد اهـ . وهو يقتضي أنه يصلي عليه في القنوت بهذه الصيغة وهو الأولى. ومن الغريب ما في المجتبى : لو صلى على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم في القنوت لا يصلي في القعدة الأخيرة، وكذا لو صلى عليه في القعدة الأولى سهواً لا يصلي عليه في القعدة الأخيرة ولا يصلي في القنوت اهـ . .
And in al-Nihāyah, attributed to Muhammad ibn al-Hanafiyyah, he said: Supplication is four kinds: supplication of desire, supplication of fear, supplication of humility, and supplication of secrecy. In supplication of desire, he places the palms of his hands towards the sky; in supplication of fear, he places the backs of his hands towards his face like one seeking refuge from something; in supplication of humility, he intertwines the little finger and ring finger, forms a ring with thumb and middle finger, and points with the index finger; and supplication of secrecy is what a person does within himself. And the author (of Kanz al-Daqā'iq) did not mention sending salāt upon the Prophet (ﷺ) in qunūt due to the difference of opinion. Al-Faqīh Abū al-Layth chose that it is better to send salāt upon him because qunūt is a supplication, and it is better for a supplication to include it. Abū al-Qāsim al-Ṣaffār went that one should not send salāt in it because it is not its place, and this was followed in al-Khulāṣah. And because al-Ṭabarānī narrated from 'Alī: 'Every supplication is veiled until one sends salāt upon Muhammad.' And in al-Wāqi'āt: It is recommended in every supplication that it include salāt upon the Prophet: 'O Allah, send salāt upon Muhammad and upon the family of Muhammad.' End. This requires that he send salāt upon him in qunūt with this formula, and it is better. And from al-Mujtabā it is strange: If he sends salāt upon the Prophet (ﷺ) in qunūt, he should not send salāt in the final sitting; and likewise if he sends salāt upon him in the first sitting forgetfully, he should not send salāt upon him in the final sitting, and he should not send salāt in qunūt. End.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on whether to include salāt (blessings) upon the Prophet (ﷺ) in the qunūt of witr. It begins by citing Muhammad ibn al-Hanafiyyah's classification of four types of supplication with corresponding hand gestures. Then it notes that the author of Kanz al-Daqā'iq omitted mentioning salāt in qunūt due to difference of opinion. Two positions are presented: Abū al-Layth al-Samarqandī preferred including it, reasoning that qunūt is a supplication and supplications are more virtuous when accompanied by salāt upon the Prophet. Abū al-Qāsim al-Ṣaffār held the opposite, saying qunūt is not the place for salāt, and this view was followed in al-Khulāṣah. The passage then provides proof from al-Ṭabarānī's hadith from 'Alī that every supplication is veiled until one sends salāt upon Muhammad. Al-Wāqi'āt recommends the formula 'Allāhumma ṣalli 'alā Muhammad wa 'alā āli Muhammad' in every supplication. The author concludes that this implies sending salāt in qunūt with that formula is better (al-ūlā). Finally, a strange ruling from al-Mujtabā is mentioned: if one sends salāt upon the Prophet in qunūt, he should not do so in the final sitting; and if he did so forgetfully in the first sitting, he should not repeat it in the final sitting or in qunūt. The author finds this odd, implying the correct view is to send salāt in qunūt as preferred.

Key Terms
القنوت (al-qunūt): A specific supplication recited in the witr prayer after the bowing (or before, depending on the school), often including a set du'a.
الصلاة على النبي (al-ṣalāh 'alā al-nabī): Sending blessings and salutations upon the Prophet Muhammad (ﷺ), typically the formula 'Allāhumma ṣalli 'alā Muhammad...'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is not allowed because qunūt is not the place for salāt.
B) It is makrūh to include it.
C) It is better to include it based on the hadith that supplication is veiled without it.
D) It is wajib.

Key Takeaway
The preferred Hanafi view is to include salat upon the Prophet in witr qunut, as supplication without it is veiled from acceptance.

Qunut in Fajr and Calamities: The Hanafi vs Shafi'i Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute on qunut

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on qunut in Fajr and for calamities, and explain the key hadith evidence and its implications for the Shafi'i counterargument.

Core Idea
Hanafis restrict regular qunut to witr; Fajr qunut is only during calamities, based on the Prophet's lack of persistence.

The performance of qunut (special supplication) in prayer has been a point of divergence between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the Hanafi stance: qunut is normally confined to the witr prayer, but exceptions exist during times of calamity (nawazil). The author contrasts this with the Shafi'i view and delves into the follower's role when the imam recites qunut. By studying this lesson, you will grasp the hadith evidence that anchors the Hanafi position and learn how to apply it in practice, especially when praying behind a Shafi'i imam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi Default Ruling
Read the opening phrase: 'ولا يقنت في غيره أي في غير الوتر'. This establishes that in the Hanafi school, qunut is regular only in witr. Determine the ruling for other prayers (Fajr, Zuhr, etc.) when there is no calamity.
The default is that qunut is not performed in Fajr or any other prayer regularly.
2
Analyze the Hanafi Proof for Fajr Qunut
Examine the hadith narrated by Abu Hanifa from Ibn Mas'ud: the Prophet (ﷺ) performed qunut in Fajr for only one month against polytheists and then abandoned it. This proves that qunut in Fajr was a temporary, not a permanent sunnah.
The lack of persistence (tark) indicates abrogation or abandonment.
3
Understand the Hanafi View on Qunut for Calamities
The passage states that if a calamity (nazila) befalls, the imam may perform qunut in loud prayers (according to some) or specifically in Fajr (according to others). Note the internal difference within the Hanafi school.
The author notes a potential textual corruption; the relied-upon view is that it is restricted to Fajr.
4
Contrast with the Shafi'i Position
The Shafi'is rely on hadith that the Prophet performed qunut in Fajr, Zuhr, 'Isha, and Maghrib, and they do not consider these abrogated. Identify the thamarah al-khilaf: Shafi'is perform qunut in Fajr regularly and in all prayers during calamities; Hanafis do not.
The Hanafis interpret the Shafi'i evidence as abrogated due to lack of persistence.
5
Apply the Ruling for the Follower
When the imam recites qunut (e.g., in witr or Fajr during calamity), the follower should say 'amin' rather than recite the qunut itself, because qunut has a resemblance to the Qur'an and the follower should not recite the Qur'an behind the imam.
This applies even if the imam is Shafi'i and performs qunut after ruku' in Fajr.

النقاية معزياً إلى الغاية : وإن نزل بالمسلمين نازلة قنت الإمام في صلاة الجهر. وهو قول الثوري وأحمد. وقال جمهور أهل الحديث : القنوت عند النوازل مشروع في الصلوات كلها اهـ. قوله (ويتبع المؤتم قانت الوتر) وقال محمد: لا يأتي به المأموم بل يؤمن لأن للقنوت شبهة القرآن لاختلاف الصحابة في قوله «اللهم إنا نستعينك أنه من القرآن أولاً فأورث شبهة وهو لا يقرأ، حقيقة القرآن فكذا ما له شبهه، والمختار ما في الكتاب المؤتم الإمام القانت يقنت عندنا في صلاة الفجر من غير بلية فإذا وقعت فتنة أو بلية فلا بأس به فعله رسول الله صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم. وأما القنوت في الصلوات كلها عند النوازل فلم يقل به إلا الشافعي الشيخ إسماعيل لكنه عزاه إلى غاية البيان، ولم أجد المسألة فيها فلعله اشتبه عليه غاية السروجي بغاية البيان لكن نقل عن البناية ما نصه : إذا وقعت نازلة قنت الإمام في الصلاة الجهرية. وقال الطحاوي لا يقنت عندنا في صلاة الفجر في غير بلية أما إذا وقعت فلا بأس به ا هـ. ولعل في المسألة قولين فليراجع ثم لينظر هل القنوت للنازلة قبل الركوع أو بعده وظاهر حملهم ما رواه الشافعي في الفجر على النازلة يقضي الثاني، His saying: (And he does not perform qunūt in other than it) i.e., other than witr, because Imām Abū Hanīfah narrated from Ibn Mas'ūd (may Allāh be pleased with him) that the Messenger of Allāh (ﷺ) never performed qunūt in Fajr except for one month, and he was not seen before that nor after. He only performed qunūt in that month supplicating against some polytheists. Similarly, in the two Sahīhs, he (ﷺ) performed qunūt for a month supplicating against a group of Arabs and then abandoned it. And the muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humām has spoken at length here against al-Shāfi'ī, as is his habit, and we are not dealing with that. And in Sharḥ al-Niqāyah, attributed to al-Ghāyah: If a calamity befalls the Muslims, the imām performs qunūt in the loud prayer. This is the view of al-Thawrī and Aḥmad. And the majority of hadith scholars said: Qunūt at times of calamities is prescribed in all prayers. End. His saying: (And the follower follows the one performing qunūt in witr) and Muḥammad said: The follower should not recite it but rather say āmīn, because qunūt has a resemblance to the Qur'an due to the Companions' disagreement over the statement 'O Allāh, we seek Your help' whether it is from the Qur'an or not, so it acquired a resemblance, and he does not recite actual Qur'an; likewise what resembles it. The preferred view is what is in the book, as in al-Muhīt and others, and they authenticated it because it is a supplication in reality, like other supplications, praises, tashahhud, and tasbīhāt. The apparent narration is that it is not disliked for a junub to recite it because it is not Qur'an, and upon this is the fatwa, as in al-Walwālijiyyah. His saying: (No) Fajr) i.e., the follower does not follow the imām performing qunūt in Fajr according to us without a calamity. If a fitna or calamity occurs, there is no harm in it; the Messenger of Allāh (ﷺ) did it. As for qunūt in all prayers at times of calamities, no one except al-Shāfi'ī said it. It is as if they interpreted what is narrated from him (ﷺ) that he performed qunūt in Zuhr and 'Ishā' according to Muslim, and that he performed qunūt in Maghrib as well according to al-Bukhārī, as abrogated, due to the lack of persistence and repetition reported in Fajr from him (ﷺ). End. The consequence is that qunūt for a calamity is specific to Fajr, but this contradicts what the author mentioned attributed to al-Ghāyah that it is in the loud prayer. Perhaps it is a corruption from Fajr, and I found it with this wording in the margins of Miskīn, and likewise in al-Ashbāh and in the commentary of Shaykh Ismā'īl, but he attributed it to Ghāyat al-Bayān. I did not find the issue there; perhaps he confused Ghāyat al-Sirūjī with Ghāyat al-Bayān. But it is transmitted from al-Bināyah: 'If a calamity occurs, the imām performs qunūt in the loud prayer.' And al-Ṭaḥāwī said: 'He does not perform qunūt according to us in Fajr without a calamity, but if it occurs there is no harm.' End. Perhaps there are two opinions on the issue, so let it be checked. Then let it be considered whether the qunūt for a calamity is before rukū' or after. The apparent interpretation of what al-Shāfi'ī narrated about Fajr as being for calamity indicates the second. Then I saw al-Shurunbulālī in Marāqī al-Falāḥ explicitly stating this. Al-Ḥamawī in his glosses on al-Ashbāh preferred the first, but what we mentioned is more apparent. The saying of the author: (And the follower follows the one performing qunūt in witr) meaning even if the imām is a Shāfi'ī and performs qunūt after rukū', because their difference is in
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and the Shāfi'ī school, primarily on the issue of qunūt in Fajr and for calamities. The Hanafi position is that qunūt is performed only in witr, not in Fajr, based on a hadith from Ibn Mas'ūd that the Prophet (ﷺ) only performed qunūt in Fajr for one month supplicating against polytheists and then abandoned it. The Hanafis also hold that qunūt for calamities is permissible only in Fajr (according to some) or in loud prayers (according to others), but they reject the Shāfi'ī view that qunūt is prescribed in all prayers during calamities. The passage discusses the follower's role: the follower says 'āmīn' rather than reciting the qunūt itself, due to its resemblance to the Qur'an. There is also a discussion on whether the imām should perform qunūt before or after rukū', with the relied upon view being after rukū'. The author notes that if the imām is a Shāfi'ī who performs qunūt after rukū', the Hanafi follower should still follow him because the difference is in the place of qunūt. The passage also addresses a contradiction in whether qunūt for calamities is specific to Fajr or includes all loud prayers, suggesting it may be a textual corruption. Ultimately, the Hanafi mufta bihi is that qunūt in Fajr is not performed except in times of calamity, and qunūt for calamities is restricted to Fajr prayer only.

Key Terms
القنوت (al-qunūt): A special supplication in prayer; in this passage, it refers both to the qunūt of witr and to the qunūt for calamities.
النوازل (al-nawāzil): Calamities or disasters that befall the Muslim community, for which qunūt may be performed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is qunūt performed in Fajr?
A) Every day, as a regular sunnah.
B) Only during calamities (nawāzil).
C) Only in the month of Ramadan.
D) Never.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school restricts qunūt to witr normally, and allows it in Fajr only during calamities, based on the Prophet's temporary practice and its abandonment.

Qunut Only in Witr: Evidence and Scope
Provides the ruling that qunut is exclusively for witr with evidence and discussion of calamities

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on qunut and explain the evidence from the sunnah that restricts it to witr.

Core Idea
Qunut is only in witr; evidence shows the Prophet abandoned it in Fajr after one month.

The Hanafi school firmly restricts the qunut supplication to the witr prayer. This lesson examines the primary evidence from the Prophet's practice, as narrated by Ibn Mas'ud, and addresses the scholarly disagreement with the Shafi'i school, particularly regarding Fajr and calamities. Understanding this ruling prevents the common error of regularly reciting qunut in Fajr without a calamity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine that the act under discussion is the qunut supplication. State the Hanafi ruling: it is a confirmed sunnah in witr, and not prescribed in other prayers, except in Fajr during a calamity (where it becomes mubah).
The ruling is derived from the hadith and the practice of the Companions.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the main evidence: the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud (narrated by Imam Abu Hanifa) that the Prophet only did qunut in Fajr for one month and then abandoned it. Also, the two Sahihs report that he did qunut for a month against a specific group and then left it.
This hadith is the core proof for the Hanafi position.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Examine how the hadith proves the ruling. The Prophet's abandonment after a specific period indicates that the practice was temporary and not a continuing sunnah. The Hanafi principle: the Prophet's leaving off an act (tark) can indicate prohibition or non-prescription.
This is based on the principle that the Prophet's actions that he later abandoned are either abrogated or show that the act is not required.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the Shafi'i position: qunut is also performed in Fajr and in all prayers during calamities. They rely on reports that the Prophet did qunut in Zuhr, Maghrib, and 'Isha' during difficult times.
The Hanafi response is that those reports are either abrogated or specific to the context of calamities and not a general practice.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Conclude that the Hanafi position is mufta bihi because the evidence of abandonment is stronger and the continuous practice shows qunut is only in witr. The follower recites qunut in witr, and the ruling is applied accordingly.
This tarjih is supported by al-Hidayah and later Hanafi authorities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ولا يقنت في غيره أي في غير الوتر لما رواه الإمام أبو حنيفة عن ابن مسعود الله عنه أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لم يقنت في الفجر قط إلا شهراً واحداً لم ير قبل ذلك ولا بعده، وإنما قنت في ذلك الشهر يدعو على أناس من المشركين وكذا في الصحيحين أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام قنت شهراً يدعو على قوم من العرب ثم تركه. وقد أطال المحقق ابن الهمام هنا في الكلام مع الشافعي كما هو دأبه ولسنا بصدده. وفي شرح النقاية معزياً إلى الغاية : وإن نزل بالمسلمين نازلة قنت الإمام في صلاة الجهر. وهو قول الثوري وأحمد. وقال جمهور أهل الحديث : القنوت عند النوازل مشروع في الصلوات كلها اهـ. قوله (ويتبع المؤتم قانت الوتر) وقال محمد: لا يأتي به المأموم بل يؤمن لأن للقنوت شبهة القرآن لاختلاف الصحابة في قوله «اللهم إنا نستعينك أنه من القرآن أولاً فأورث شبهة وهو لا يقرأ حقيقة القرآن فكذا ما له شبهه، والمختار ما في الكتاب كما في المحيط وغيره وصححوه لأنه دعاء حقيقة كسائر الأدعية والثناء والتشهد والتسبيحات، وظاهر الرواية أنه لا يكره قراءته للجنب لأنه ليس بقرآن وعليه الفتوى كما في الولوالجية قوله (لا) الفجر ) أي لا يتبع المؤتم الإمام القانت يقنت عندنا في صلاة الفجر من غير بلية فإذا وقعت فتنة أو بلية فلا بأس به فعله رسول الله صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم. وأما القنوت في الصلوات كلها عند النوازل فلم يقل به إلا الشافعي وكأنهم حملوا ما روي عنه عليه السلام أنه قنت في الظهر والعشاء على ما في مسلم، وأنه قنت في المغرب أيضاً على ما في البخاري على النسخ لعدم ورود المواظبة والتكرار الواردين في الفجر عنه عليه الصلاة والسلام اهـ. ومقتضى هذا أن القنوت لنازلة خاص بالفجر ويخالفه ما ذكره المؤلف معزياً إلى الغاية من قوله في صلاة الجهر، ولعله محرف عن الفجر وقد وجدته بهذا اللفظ في حواشي مسكين، وكذا في الأشباه وكذا في شرح الشيخ إسماعيل لكنه عزاه إلى غاية البيان، ولم أجد المسألة فيها فلعله اشتبه عليه غاية السروجي بغاية البيان لكن نقل عن البناية ما نصه : إذا وقعت نازلة قنت الإمام في الصلاة الجهرية. وقال الطحاوي لا يقنت عندنا في صلاة الفجر في غير بلية أما إذا وقعت فلا بأس به ا هـ . ولعل في المسألة قولين فليراجع ثم لينظر هل القنوت للنازلة قبل الركوع أو بعده وظاهر حملهم ما رواه الشافعي في الفجر على النازلة يقضي الثاني، ثم رأيت الشرنبلالي في مراقي الفلاح صرح بذلك، واستظهر الحموي في حواشي الأشباه الأول وما ذكرناه أظهر
His saying (And he does not do qunut in other than it, i.e., other than witr) because of what Imam Abu Hanifa narrated from Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him) that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) never did qunut in Fajr except for one month, never seen before or after, and he only did qunut in that month praying against some polytheists. Similarly, in the two Sahihs, he (peace be upon him) did qunut for a month praying against a group of Arabs, then left it. Al-Muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam has discussed at length with al-Shafi'i here as is his habit, but we are not concerned with that. In Sharh al-Niqayah, attributed to al-Ghayah: If a calamity befalls the Muslims, the imam does qunut in the loud prayer. This is the view of al-Thawri and Ahmad. The majority of hadith scholars say: Qunut at times of calamity is prescribed in all prayers. His saying (And the follower follows the imam of witr in qunut). Muhammad said: The follower does not perform it, but rather says 'amen', because qunut has a resemblance to the Quran due to the disagreement of the Companions about the phrase 'Allahumma inna nasta'inuk' whether it is from the Quran or not, so it acquired a resemblance, and he does not read the actual Quran, so likewise what resembles it. But the chosen view is what is in the book, as in al-Muhit and others, and they corrected it because it is a supplication truly like other supplications, praise, tashahhud, and glorifications. The apparent narration is that it is not disliked for a junub to recite it because it is not Quran, and upon this is the fatwa as in al-Walwalijiyyah. His saying (No) for Fajr, i.e., the follower does not follow the imam doing qunut; we do not do qunut in Fajr prayer without a calamity. If a trial or calamity occurs, then there is no harm in doing it, as the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) did it. As for qunut in all prayers at times of calamities, only al-Shafi'i said it. It is as if they interpreted what was narrated from him (peace be upon him) that he did qunut in Zuhr and 'Isha' as in Muslim, and that he did qunut in Maghrib as in Bukhari, as abrogated due to the lack of continuous practice and repetition that occurred for Fajr from him (peace be upon him). This implies that qunut for a calamity is specific to Fajr. This contradicts what the author mentioned attributing to al-Ghayah: that it is in loud prayer. Perhaps it is a corruption from Fajr, and I found it with this wording in the margins of Miskin, and similarly in al-Ashbah and in the commentary of Shaykh Isma'il, but he attributed it to Ghayat al-Bayan. I did not find the issue there; perhaps he confused Ghayat al-Saruji with Ghayat al-Bayan. However, it is transmitted from al-Binayah: 'If a calamity occurs, the imam does qunut in the loud prayer.' Al-Tahawi said: 'We do not do qunut in Fajr without a calamity; if it occurs, there is no harm.' Perhaps there are two opinions in the issue, so it should be referred. Then consider whether the qunut for a calamity is before or after ruku'. The apparent interpretation of what al-Shafi'i narrated about Fajr as being for a calamity indicates the second (after ruku'). Then I saw al-Shurnablali in Maraqi al-Falah stated that, and al-Hamawi in his margins on al-Ashbah preferred the first (before ruku'), and what we mentioned is more apparent.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It establishes that qunut (the supplication) is performed only in the witr prayer, not in any other obligatory prayer. The evidence is a hadith narrated by Imam Abu Hanifa from Ibn Mas'ud that the Prophet only did qunut in Fajr for one month (to pray against polytheists) and then abandoned it, indicating abrogation. Similarly, authentic reports show he did qunut for a month for a specific reason and then stopped. The commentator refrains from the lengthy debate with al-Shafi'i, but notes that for calamities, some scholars (al-Thawri, Ahmad) allow qanut in loud prayers, while the majority of hadith scholars allow it in all prayers. The author then discusses the follower's action: Muhammad ibn al-Hasan said the follower should not recite qunut but say 'amen', because it resembles Quran. However, the chosen view (al-mukhtar) is that the follower does recite it because it is essentially a supplication. The ruling also clarifies that qunut is not done in Fajr without a calamity; if a calamity occurs, it is allowed. The commentator reconciles different transmissions about whether it is before or after ruku', concluding that the apparent meaning from Shafi'i's narrations indicates after ruku'. There is disagreement about whether qunut for calamities is specific to Fajr or includes all loud prayers; the author notes a possible confusion in sources and suggests the issue has two views.

Key Terms
القنوت (al-qunut): A supplication recited in prayer, specifically in witr according to Hanafis.
النوازل (al-nawazil): Calamities or difficult situations that befall the Muslim community.

C) Never.
D) Only during Ramadan.

Key Takeaway
Qunut is a sunnah only in witr; evidence from the Prophet's practice shows it was abandoned in Fajr except during specific calamities.

Following a Shafi'i Imam in Fajr Qunut: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on follower's action in Fajr qunut

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three positions within the Hanafi school regarding the follower's action during Fajr qunut and apply the preferred view (standing silent) to a real-world scenario.

Core Idea
Hanafi follower stands silent during Shafi'i imam's Fajr qunut because the qunut is abrogated.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies the general rule that a follower must follow the imam in witr qunut. However, when the imam is Shafi'i and performs qunut in Fajr—which Hanafis consider non-prescribed—an intra-Hanafi disagreement arises. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) hold that the follower should not recite the qunut but stand silently, while Abu Yusuf argues for following. This lesson unpacks the reasoning, analogy with funeral prayer, and the preferred view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base rule
The matn states: 'The follower follows the imam of witr in qunut.' This is the default ruling for witr prayer.
This applies when the imam is also Hanafi or when the qunut is in witr.
2
Recognize the exception
When the imam is Shafi'i and performs qunut in Fajr (which Hanafis consider abrogated), the follower's duty is disputed.
3
State the two positions
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say the follower does not follow (i.e., does not recite the qunut). Abu Yusuf says the follower does follow (recites the qunut). A third view suggests sitting down.
The third view (sitting) is rejected by most.
4
Understand the dalil of the majority
They argue that qunut in Fajr is abrogated (mansukh), so it is non-prescribed. They draw an analogy: if an imam says five takbirs in funeral prayer (instead of four), the follower does not follow in the fifth.
This is a qiyas jali (clear analogy).
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The preferred view, as stated in al-Hidayah and confirmed by later authorities, is that the follower stands silently without reciting the qunut.
Standing silently avoids both following a non-prescribed act and creating unnecessary difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (ويتبع المؤتم قانت الوتر أي ولو كان الإمام شافعياً يقنت بعد الركوع لأن اختلافهم في صلاة الفجر، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد وقال أبو يوسف : يتابعه لأنه تبع للإمام والقنوت مجتهد فيه . ولهما أنه منسوخ فصار كما لو كبر خمساً في الجنازة حيث لا يتابعه في الخامسة، وإذا لم يتابعه فيه فقيل يقعد تحقيقاً للمخالفة لأن الساكت شريك الداعي بدليل مشاركة الإمام في القراءة وإذا قعد فقدت المشاركة. ولا يقال كيف يقعد تحقيقاً للمخالفة مفسدة وهي للصلاة لأن المخالفة فيما هو من الأركان والشرائط مفسدة لا في غيرها. قال في الهداية : والأظهر وقوفه ساكتاً وصححه قاضيخان وغيره لأن فعل الإمام يشتمل على مشروع وغيره، فما كان مشروعاً يتبعه فيه، وما كان غير مشروع لا يتبعه . كذا في العناية. وقد يقال : إنَّ طول القيام بعد رفع الرأس من الركوع ليس بمشروع فلا يتابعه فيه . قال في الهداية : ودلت المسألة على جواز الاقتداء بالشفعوية. وإذا علم المقتدي منه ما يزعم به فساد صلاته كالفصد وغيره لا يجزئه اهـ. ووجه دلالتها أنه لو لم يصح الاقتداء به لم يصح اختلاف علمائنا في أنه يسكت أو يتابعه، ووقع في بعض نسخها بالشافعية وهو الصواب لما عرف من وجوب حذف ياء النسب إذا نسب إلى ما هي فيه ووضع الياء الثانية مكانها حتى تتحد الصورة قبل النسبة الثانية وبعدها والتمييز حينئذ من خارج فالياء المشددة فيه ياء النسبة لا آخر الكلمة ككرسي. وذكر في النهاية بن عبد مناف بنو شافع من بني منهم الإمام الشافعي الفقيه رحمها ومن قال في نسبته الشفعوي فهو عامي وحقه أن يقال بالشافعي المذهب. فحاصله أن صاحب الهداية جوز الاقتداء بالشافعي بشرط أن لا يعلم المقتدي منه ما يمنع صحة صلاته في رأي المقتدي كالفصد ونحوه وعدد مواضع عدم صحة الاقتداء به في العناية وغاية البيان بقوله كما إذا لم يتوضأ من خصوص المطلب الله ، الفجر مع كونه منسوخاً دليل على أنه يتابعه في قنوت الوتر لكونه ثابتاً بيقين. كذا في الدرر وصدر الشريعة وفي الشرنبلالية لا يخفى أن الشافعي يقنت بـ اللهم «اهدنا والحنفي بـ«اللهم إنا نستعينك» فما يفعله فلينظر ا هـ . قال في حواشي مسكين والظاهر أن المتابعة في مطلق القنوت لا في ما قنت به، ثم رأيت الشيخ عبد الحي ذكر طبق ما فهمته ا.هـ. على أنه قدم المؤلف أن ظاهر الرواية أنه لا توقيت فيه قوله : ( ولهما أنه منسوخ قال العلامة نوح أفندي : هذا على إطلاقه مسلم في غير النوازل، وأما عند النوازل في القنوت في الفجر فينبغي أن يتابعه عند الكل لأن القنوت فيها عند النوازل ليس بمنسوخ على ما هو التحقيق كما مر وأما في القنوت في غير الفجر عند النوازل كما هو مذهب الشافعي فلا يتابعه عند الكل فإن القنوت في غير الفجر منسوخ عندنا اتفاقاً اهـ . فعلى هذا فالمراد نسخ عموم الحكم لا نسخ الحكم قوله : (لأن الساكت شريك الداعي) قال في الفتح : مشترك الإلزام فإن الجالس أيضاً ساكت فلا بد من تقييده مشاركته الداعي بحال موافقته في خصوص هيئة الداعي لكنه يقتضي أنه إنما يكون مشاركاً إذا رفع يده مثله لأنها من هيئة الإمام إلا أن يلغي ذلك ويقال مجرد الوقوف خلف الداعي الواقف ساكتاً يعد شركة له في
His saying (And the follower follows the imam of witr in qunut), i.e., even if the imam is Shafi'i and does qunut after ruku', because their difference is in Fajr prayer. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: He follows him because the follower follows the imam and qunut is a matter of ijtihad. According to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), it is abrogated, so it is like if he said five takbirs in the funeral prayer, where he does not follow him in the fifth. And when he does not follow him in it, some say he sits down to effectuate the difference, because the silent one is a partner of the one supplicating, as evidenced by the follower's participation in recitation. If he sits, the participation is lost. It is not said: How can he sit to effectuate the difference, which is a corruption for the prayer? Because differing in what are pillars and conditions is a corruption, not in other things. In al-Hidayah: The most apparent is that he stands silently, and Qadikhan and others corrected it because the imam's action includes both prescribed and non-prescribed, so what is prescribed he follows, what is not prescribed he does not follow. Similarly in al-'Inayah. It may be said: The prolonged standing after raising the head from ruku' is not prescribed, so he does not follow him in it. In al-Hidayah: The issue indicates the validity of following a Shafi'i. If the follower knows from the imam something that invalidates his prayer in his view, like phlebotomy, etc., it does not suffice. The point of its indication is that if following him were not valid, our scholars' disagreement about whether he is silent or follow would not be valid. In some copies it is 'al-Shafi'iyyah' and that is correct... The summary is that the author of al-Hidayah allowed following a Shafi'i on condition that the follower does not know from the imam something that prevents the validity of his prayer in the follower's view, like phlebotomy, etc. [Text continues but breaks off].
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the follower's actions when the imam performs qunut. The matn states: 'The follower follows the imam of witr in qunut.' The sharh explains that even if the imam is Shafi'i and does qunut in Fajr (which Hanafis consider abrogated), the follower's action is disputed. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say the follower does not follow the imam in the qunut (i.e., does not recite it), but Abu Yusuf says he does follow because qunut is a matter of ijtihad. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad compare it to a funeral prayer where the imam says five takbirs: the follower does not join in the fifth. Some scholars say the follower should sit down to clearly differ, but al-Hidayah prefers that he stand silently, as the imam's action includes both prescribed and non-prescribed parts. The passage also indicates that following a Shafi'i imam is valid as long as the follower does not know of something that would invalidate the prayer in his own madhhab (like phlebotomy). The discussion includes a critique of the claim that the silent one is a partner in supplication, and concludes that standing silently is the preferred position. Later scholars like 'Allamah Nuh Afendi add that the ruling of abrogation applies only to qunut without calamity; during calamity, the Hanafi follower should follow the Shafi'i imam in qunut in Fajr, but not in other prayers. The passage ends with a discussion of the phrase 'the silent one is a partner of the supplicant' and its implications.

Key Terms
المؤتم (al-mu'tamm): The follower in congregational prayer.
القنوت (al-qunut): The supplication recited in prayer.
الشفعوية (al-shafa'awiyyah): The followers of Imam al-Shafi'i (the Shafi'i school).
منسوخ (mansukh): Abrogated; a ruling that has been superseded by later revelation or prophetic practice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred Hanafi view, what should a Hanafi follower do when following a Shafi'i imam who performs qunut in Fajr?
A) Recite the qunut loudly with the imam.
B) Sit down until the imam finishes the qunut.
C) Stand silently and not recite the qunut.
D) Leave the prayer.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi follower stands silent during a Shafi'i imam's Fajr qunut because the qunut is abrogated, and the follower only follows prescribed actions.

Following a Shafi'i Imam and the Qunut Dispute
Intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute on iqtida and qunut

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on following a Shafi'i Imam in Fajr, explain the disagreement between the majority (Abu Hanifa & Muhammad) and Abu Yusuf regarding qunut, and apply the condition that iqtida is valid unless the follower knows of a factor invalidating the imam's prayer according to Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
A Hanafi follower behind a Shafi'i Imam should stand silent during qunut in Fajr because it is abrogated and not a prescribed act to follow.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a common scenario: a Hanafi praying behind a Shafi'i Imam who recites qunut in Fajr. The Hanafi school holds that qunut in Fajr is abrogated (mansukh), while the Shafi'i school considers it sunnah. The scholars debate whether the follower should join in qunut or remain silent, and the general ruling on the validity of following a Shafi'i Imam is clarified with conditions.

Guided Path
1
State the intra-Hanafi positions
Identify the two views: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say the follower does not follow the imam in qunut; Abu Yusuf says he does follow because the imam is followed and qunut is a matter of ijtihad.
The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) rely on abrogation; Abu Yusuf on the principle of taba'iyyah.
2
Identify the opposing school's proof
The Shafi'i school (and Abu Yusuf) argue that the imam's action is followed as long as it is ijtihadi, and qunut is not decisively abrogated.
They also cite the hadith that the imam is appointed to be followed.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response using qiyas
The Hanafi response uses an analogy: if the imam says five takbirs in janazah prayer, the follower does not follow the extra takbir. Similarly, qunut in Fajr is an extra, non-prescribed act.
The illa (effective cause) is that not every action of the imam is followed—only prescribed acts.
4
Apply the general condition for valid iqtida
The Hidayah states that following a Shafi'i is permissible on condition that the follower does not know of any factor that, in his own madhhab, invalidates the imam's prayer (e.g., not performing wudu from qullatayn, raising hands, etc.).
If such a factor is known, the iqtida is not valid.
5
Determine thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
The practical consequence: a Hanafi follower in Fajr will either follow in qunut (Abu Yusuf) or remain silent (majority). The mufta bihi is to remain silent, as preferred by al-Marghinani and Qadikhan.
This does not invalidate the prayer; the follower's act is valid.

والشافعية لا ينحرفون هذا الانحراف . الرابع . مسألة التعصب وهو تعصب لأن التعصب على تقدير وجوده منهم إنما يوجب الفسق لا الكفر والفسق لا يمنع صحة الاقتداء، والظاهر من الشارطين لعدمه أنه يوجب الكفر لكونه في الدين وهو بعيد كما لا يخفى. الخامس مسألة الاستثناء في اء في الإيمان . من قال فاعلم أن عبارتهم قد اختلفت في هذه المسألة ؛ فذهب طائفة . من الحنفية إلى تكفير . «أنا مؤمن إن شاء الله ولم يقيدوه بأن
