فليتأمل ما المراد قوله : والشافعية لا ينحرفون هذا (الانحراف) أقول : بل لا ينحرفون أصلاً لأن مذهبهم أضيق من مذهبنا في هذه المسألة لوجوب استقبال العين عندهم، وغاية ما يفعلونه
Book of Prayer, Chapter of Witr and Supererogatory Prayers. Regarding the Fajr prayer, this is according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: He follows him because he is a follower of the Imam, and qunut is a matter of ijtihad. According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), it is abrogated, so it becomes like if he said five takbirs in the funeral prayer, where he does not follow him in the fifth. If he does not follow him in it, it is said he sits to actualize opposition, because the silent one is a partner of the supplicator, by evidence of the Imam's participation in recitation, and if he sits, the participation is lost. It cannot be said: How can he sit to actualize opposition, which is a corrupting factor for prayer? Because opposition in what is among the pillars and conditions is corruptive, not in other matters. In al-Hidayah it is said: The most apparent is that he stands silent, and Qadikhan and others corrected it, because the Imam's action includes both prescribed and non-prescribed, so what is prescribed he follows him in, and what is not prescribed he does not follow him in. Likewise in al-Inayah. It may be said: Prolonged standing after raising the head from bowing is not prescribed, so he does not follow him in it. In al-Hidayah it is said: The issue indicates the permissibility of following the Shafi'i. And if the follower knows from him something that he deems invalidates his prayer, like phlebotomy and the like, it does not suffice him. The evidence for its indication is that if following him were not valid, the disagreement of our scholars on whether he remains silent or follows him would not occur. In some copies it is written 'al-Shafi'iyyah', which is correct, due to the known rule of dropping the nisbah ya' when attributing to what it is in, and placing the second ya' in its place... The summary is that the author of al-Hidayah permitted following the Shafi'i on condition that the follower does not know from him what prevents the validity of his prayer in the follower's view, like phlebotomy and the like, and he enumerated places where following him is not valid in al-Inayah and Ghayat al-Bayan...
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab and intra-Hanafi dispute analysis from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. It addresses the permissibility of a Hanafi follower praying behind a Shafi'i Imam, focusing on the issue of qunut in Fajr. The author first presents the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (who say the follower should not follow the Imam in qunut because it is abrogated) and Abu Yusuf (who says he should follow because the Imam is followed and qunut is ijtihadi). The preferred view, as quoted from al-Hidayah, is that the follower stands silent, not reciting qunut, and this is the mufta bihi view. The passage then explains the reasoning using an analogy to the funeral prayer: if the Imam says an extra takbir, the follower does not follow; similarly, the abrogated qunut is not followed. The text then broadens to the general ruling: following a Shafi'i Imam is permissible provided the follower does not know of any factor that, in his own madhhab, invalidates the Imam's prayer. Several examples are given (e.g., not performing wudu from qullatayn, raising hands, etc.), and then five specific items are discussed in detail, showing that some apparent invalidators are not actually invalid according to the Hanafi school, thereby preserving the validity of iqtida. The passage concludes with a discussion of the issue of istithna' in iman (saying 'if Allah wills' regarding faith) and whether it affects the validity of iqtida.

Key Terms
الاقتداء (al-iqtida'): Following the Imam in congregational prayer as a ma'mum.
القنوت (al-qunut): A supplication recited in prayer; specifically, in this context, the qunut recited in Fajr by Shafi'is and in Witr by Hanafis.
المنسوخ (al-mansukh): A legal ruling that has been abrogated by a later revelation, thus no longer operative.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), what should a Hanafi follower do if the Shafi'i Imam recites qunut in Fajr?
A) Follow the Imam and recite the Hanafi qunut.
B) Sit down to indicate disagreement.
C) Remain silent and do not recite qunut.
D) Recite the Shafi'i qunut with the Imam.

Key Takeaway
A Hanafi may pray behind a Shafi'i Imam provided he does not know of any invalidating factor, and during qunut in Fajr, the Hanafi stands silent as the mufta bihi position.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Leading Prayer Behind a Shafi'i Imam: Three Cases and the Better Option
Ruling on praying behind a Shafi'i with three cases based on knowledge of his practice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three cases for the validity of following a Shafi'i imam and evaluate the preferred opinion on whether following or praying alone is better.

Core Idea
Following a cautious Shafi'i imam is valid without dislike; when his state is unknown, it is makruh tanzihi.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on praying behind a Shafi'i imam, a common scenario for Hanafis living in non-Hanafi majority areas. The text divides the situation into three cases based on knowledge of the imam's practice and concludes with a discussion on whether it is better to follow such an imam or to pray alone.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three cases
The author presents three scenarios: (1) known caution, (2) known lack of caution, (3) unknown state. Note the ruling for each.
2
Define 'caution'
Determine whether caution refers only to performing the conditions and integrals or also includes avoiding makruh acts. The text points to the first opinion.
This affects whether karaha applies.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi disagreement
The text records a difference on whether knowledge of lack of caution must be specific to the act or general. Nihaya prefers specific; others general.
4
Evaluate which is better: following or praying alone
Al-Ramli and the author argue that following a cautious Shafi'i is better than praying alone because it preserves the congregation.
This is the mufta bihi.

ثم اعلم أنه قد صرح في النهاية والعناية وغيرهما بكراهة الاقتداء بالشافعي إذا لم يعلم حاله حتى صرح في النهاية بأنه إذا علم منه مرة عدم الوضوء من الحجامة ثم غاب عنه ثم رآه يصلي فالصحيح جواز الاقتداء به مع الكراهة، فصار الحاصل أن الاقتداء بالشافعي على ثلاثة أقسام : الأول أن يعلم منه الاحتياط في مذهب الحنفي فلا كراهة في الاقتداء به الثاني أن يعلم منه عدمه فلا صحة لكن اختلفوا هل يشترط أن يعلم منه عدمه دمه في خصوص ما يقتدى به أو في الجملة، صحح في النهاية الأول وغيره اختار الثاني . وفي فتاوى الزاهدي : إذا رآه احتجم ثم غاب فالأصح أنه . الاقتداء به لأنه يصح يجوز أن يتوضأ احتياطاً وحسن الظن به أولى الثالث أن لا يعلم شيئاً فالكراهة ولا خصوصية قوله : (وهو) تفسير للشرط قوله : (الأول) أن يعلم منه الاحتياط في مذهب الحنفي) انظر هل المراد بالاحتياط الإتيان بالشروط والأركان أو ما يشمل ترك المكروه عندنا كترك رفع اليدين رفع اليدين عند الانتقالات وتأخير القيام عن محله وفي القعود الأول بسبب الصلاة على النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم، وظاهر كلام الشيخ ابراهيم في شرح المنية الأول فإنه قال : وأما الاقتداء بالمخالف في الفروع كالشافعي فيجوز ما لم يعلم منه ما يفسد الصلاة على اعتقاد المقتدي عليه الإجماع إنما اختلف في الكراهة ا هـ . إذ مفهومه أن الاختلاف في الكراهة عند عدم العلم بالمفسد والمفسد إنما هو ترك رط أو ركن فقط، ثم رأيت التصريح بذلك في رسالة في الاقتداء لمنلا علي القاري وأنه فيما عدا المبطل يتبع مذهبه وأن الاحتياط في المبطل، فإذا فعل فهو جائز بدون كراهة، وهذ هو المتبادر من سياق كلام المؤلف وعلى عدم الكراهة فهل الاقتداء به أفضل أم الانفراد؟ قال الرملي : لم أره وظاهر كلامهم الثاني والذي يحسن عندي الأول وربما أشعر كلامهم به وقد كتبت على شرح زاد الفقير للغزي كتابة حسنة في هذه المسألة فراجعها إن شئت. صورة ما كتبه عليه قوله جاز الاقتدا به بلا كراهة بقي الكلام في الأفضل ما هو الاقتداء به أو الانفراد لم أر من صرح به من علمائنا ، وظاهر كلامهم الثاني والذي يظهر ويحسن عندي الأول لأن في الثاني ترك الجماعة حيث لا تحصل إلا به، ولو لم يكن بأن كان هناك حنفي يقتدي به الأفضل الاقتداء به وكيف يكون الأفضل أن يصلي منفرداً مع وجود شافعي صالح عالم تقي نقي يراعي الخلاف به تحصل فضيلة الجماعة ما أظن فقيه نفس يقول به، وربما أشعر كلامهم بما جنحت إليه والله تعالى الموفق ا.هـ. قلت: ويدل عليه ما في السراج حيث قال : فإن قلت فما الأفضل أن يصلي خلف هؤلاء أو الانفراد؟ قيل : أما في حق الفاسق فالصلاة خلفه أولى فإنه ذكر في الفتاوي أن الرجل إذا صلى خلفه يحرز ثواب الجماعة لكن لا ينال ثواب من يصلي خلف تقي، وأما الآخرون يعني العبد والأعرابي والفاسق وولد الزنا فيمكن أن يكون الانفراد أولى لجهلهم إمامتهم ،الصلاة ويمكن أن يكونوا على قياس الصلاة خلف الفاسق، والأفضل أن يصلي خلف غيرهم لأن الناس تكره ذكرنا أنه إذا كان شافعي تقي يحتاط لم توجد فيه علة الكراهة المذكورة هنا وإذا كانت أفضل خلف فاسق مع أنه غير مأمون علي الدين فما بالك بشافعي تقي؟! والحاصل أن الظاهر ما قاله الرملي ويدل عليه أيضاً نفي المؤلف الكراهة، والظاهر أن المراد بها التنزيهية الثابتة في غيره قوله : (الثاني أن يعلم تقدم عن المجتبي أنه إن كان مراعياً للشرائط والأركان عندنا فالاقتداء به صحيح على الأصح ويكره وإلا فلا يصح أصلاً قوله: (في خصوص ما يقتدي به أي بأن رآه احتجم وصلى من غير غيبة ولا إعادة وضوء فلا يصح الاقتداء به
Then know that it has been stated in al-Nihaya, al-Inaya, and others that it is makruh to follow a Shafi'i if his state is unknown, to the extent that al-Nihaya states: if one once knew that he did not perform wudu from cupping, then he disappeared, then later saw him praying, the correct view is that following him is permissible with karaha. So the result is that following a Shafi'i is of three types: First, that one knows he is cautious in the Hanafi school—then no karaha in following him. Second, that one knows he is not cautious—then it is not valid, but they differ whether one must know his lack of caution specifically in what he is being followed in, or in general. In al-Nihaya the first is considered correct, others chose the second. In Fatawa al-Zahidi: if one sees him being cupped and then he disappears, the most correct is that it is permissible to follow him because it is possible that he performed wudu cautiously, and good opinion of him is preferable. Third, that one knows nothing—then karaha, and no specificity. His statement '(it is)' is an interpretation of the condition. His statement '(first)' that one knows he is cautious in the Hanafi school. Consider: does 'cautious' mean performing the conditions and integrals, or does it also include avoiding what is makruh for us, like raising the hands during transitions, delaying standing from its place, and in the first sitting due to sending blessings on the Prophet (peace be upon him)? The apparent meaning of Shaykh Ibrahim's words in Sharh al-Munya is the first, for he said: 'As for following a dissenter in branches like a Shafi'i, it is permissible as long as one does not know something that invalidates the prayer according to the follower's belief; there is scholarly consensus on this. The only disagreement is about karaha.' End. So its implication is that the disagreement about karaha occurs when there is no knowledge of invalidator, and invalidator is only leaving a pillar or integral. Then I saw explicit mention of this in a treatise on following by Mulla Ali al-Qari: that apart from what invalidates, one follows his own madhhab, and caution is regarding invalidators. So if he does it, it is permissible without karaha. And this is what is apparent from the context of the author's words. On the issue of no karaha, is following him better or praying alone? al-Ramli said: I have not seen it, and the apparent meaning of their words is the second (praying alone), but the better in my view is the first (following him). Perhaps their words allude to it. I have written a good note on Sharh Zad al-Faqir by al-Ghazzi on this issue, so refer to it if you wish. The text of what he wrote on it: 'His statement: following him is permissible without karaha. The remaining issue is what is better: following him or praying alone? I have not seen any of our scholars explicitly state it. The apparent meaning of their words is the second. What appears and is better in my view is the first, because in the second there is abandonment of congregation when it can only be achieved by following him. And if not—if there is a Hanafi who follows him—then following him is better. How could it be better to pray alone when there is a righteous, learned, pious Shafi'i who observes differences, whereby the virtue of congregation is attained? I do not think any discerning jurist would say so. And perhaps their words indicate what I lean towards. And Allah is the Grantor of success.' End. I say: This is supported by what is in al-Siraj where it says: If you ask: what is better, praying behind these people or alone? It is said: Regarding the corrupt person, praying behind him is better, for it is mentioned in the Fatawa that if a man prays behind him, he attains the reward of congregation, but not the reward of praying behind a pious person. As for others—meaning the slave, the Bedouin, the corrupt, and the child of fornication—it may be that praying alone is better due to their ignorance of imamate of prayer, and it may be that they are analogous to praying behind a corrupt person. It is better to pray behind others because people dislike... We mentioned that if a Shafi'i is pious and cautious, the reason for karaha mentioned here does not exist. And if it is better to pray behind a corrupt person even though he is not trustworthy in religion, what about a pious Shafi'i?! The conclusion is that what al-Ramli said is apparent, and it is also supported by the author's negation of karaha. The apparent meaning is that it refers to tanzihi karaha (disliked but not prohibited) established for others. His statement: (second) that one knows... It was previously mentioned in al-Mujtaba that if he observes the conditions and integrals according to us, then following him is sound according to the most correct view, but is makruh. Otherwise it is not sound at all. His statement: (specifically in what he is being followed in) meaning such as if one saw him being cupped and praying without being absent or repeating wudu, then following him is not sound.
Source pages p. 81

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the ruling on leading prayer behind a Shafi'i (or other non-Hanafi) imam. The author summarizes three cases: (1) If the Shafi'i is known to be cautious regarding Hanafi conditions—no karaha, his imamate is valid and not disliked. (2) If he is known not to be cautious—his imamate is invalid, but there is a difference on whether the knowledge must be specific to the act being followed or general. (3) If his state is unknown—following is valid but makruh. The author then discusses the meaning of 'caution' and the issue of whether following such an imam is better than praying alone. Al-Ramli and others lean towards following being better because it preserves the congregation. The relied-upon position is that if the Shafi'i is known to be pious and careful about Hanafi conditions, it is not only valid but better than praying alone. The karaha mentioned is tanzihi (a minor dislike) in the case of unknown state.

Key Terms
الاقتداء (al-iqtida'): Following an imam in prayer.
الكراهة التنزيهية (al-karahah al-tanzihiyyah): A minor dislike that does not affect validity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling on following a Shafi'i imam when his state is unknown?
A) Invalid
B) Valid without karaha
C) Valid with karaha tanzihi
D) Valid but only if you assume the best

Key Takeaway
The ruling on following a Shafi'i imam depends on knowledge of his caution; if known cautious, no karaha; if unknown, valid but makruh tanzihi; if known not cautious, invalid. It is better to follow a cautious Shafi'i than to pray alone.

Salah — Prayer

The Ruling on Following a Mukhalif Imam: Conditions and Disputes
Explaining the three conditions for valid iqtida behind a non-Hanafi imam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for valid iqtida behind a non-Hanafi imam and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whose belief determines validity.

Core Idea
Valid iqtida behind a mukhalif imam depends on the follower's knowledge of the imam's caution according to Hanafi rules.

The Hanafi school permits following an imam from another madhhab (such as a Shafi'i) under certain conditions. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq unpacks those conditions, focusing on what the follower knows about the imam's care in observing Hanafi requirements. It also explores a debated point: does validity depend on the imam's own belief or the follower's? Finally, it addresses whether it is better to follow such an imam or pray alone. We will work through these layers to understand the correct Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three conditions from the text
The passage presents three scenarios based on the follower's knowledge of the imam's caution (ihtiyat). First, if the follower knows the imam is cautious (muhtat) according to the Hanafi school, there is no dislike (karaah). Second, if he knows the imam is not cautious, the prayer is invalid. Third, if he knows nothing, it is disliked (makruh).
Caution here includes performing all conditions and pillars, and avoiding clear invalidators.
2
Distinguish between specific and general knowledge of lack of caution
For the second condition, scholars differ: does the follower need to know the imam's lack of caution specifically in the act being followed (e.g., that very prayer), or is general knowledge sufficient? The text notes a difference between 'in particular' and 'in general'.
The correct opinion in al-Nihayah is that specific knowledge is required; others choose general.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on whose belief governs
The passage presents a dispute between the majority (including Abu Hanifa's view as transmitted) and al-Hindwani. The majority holds that validity depends on the follower's belief: if the follower believes the imam's prayer is valid according to Hanafi fiqh, then following is valid even if the imam himself thinks his prayer is invalid. Al-Hindwani says it depends on the imam's belief.
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the majority view, as stated in al-Hidayah and Fath al-Qadir.
4
Determine the preference: following or praying alone
If following is valid without dislike, is it better to follow or to pray alone? The passage reports that al-Ramli and others prefer following, especially if the imam is a righteous Shafi'i who is cautious, because it preserves congregational reward.
The author supports following over alone, citing that even following a fasiq is better than missing congregation.

Source Text

قوله: (في خصوص ما يقتدي به أي بأن رآه احتجم وصلى من غير غيبة ولا إعادة وضوء فلا يصح الاقتداء به لأنه علم منه عدم المراعاة في خصوص ما يقتدي به، وقوله «أو في الجملة» أي بأن رآه صلى بلا إعادة الوضوء ثم (وقال الهندواني وجماعة لا يجوز) أي بناء على أن المعتبر عندهم هو رأي الإمام. قال في النهر وعلى هذا فيصح الاقتداء وإن لم يحتط ا هـ. وظاهره الجواز وإن ترك بعض الأركان والشرائط عندنا لكن ذكر العلامة نوح غيره. وأيضاً ينبغي حمل حال الإمام على التقليد لأبي حنيفة حملاً لحال المسلم على الصلاح ما أمكن فيتحد اعتقادهما وإلا لزم الدخول في الصلاة بغير طهارة على اعتقاده وهو حرام إلا أن تفرض المسألة أن المأموم The Hanafi school: there is no dislike in following him. Second: if he knows he is not cautious, then no validity, but they differed whether it is required to know his lack of caution specifically in what is followed or in general. Corrected in al-Nihayah the first, and others chose the second. In Fatawa al-Zahidi: if he sees him cupping and then he disappears, the correct is that following him is valid because it is permissible for him to perform ablution precautionarily, and good opinion of him is better. Third: he knows nothing, then dislike, and no specificity. His statement: (and it is) explanation of the condition. His statement: (first) that he knows from him caution in the Hanafi school. Consider: is caution intended as performing conditions and pillars, or includes leaving disliked acts like raising hands at transitions, delaying the standing from its place, and in the first sitting due to sending blessings on the Prophet? The apparent of Shaykh Ibrahim's statement in Sharh al-Munyah is the first, for he said: as for following a dissenter in branches like a Shafi'i, it is permissible as long as he does not know from him what invalidates the prayer according to the follower, upon which there is consensus; they only differed regarding dislike. Its implication is that the difference in dislike exists when there is no knowledge of the invalidator, and the invalidator is only leaving a rukn or pillar. Then I saw explicit mention in a treatise on following by Mulla Ali al-Qari that apart from invalidators, he follows his own madhhab, and precaution in invalidators, so if he does it, it is permissible without dislike. This is the apparent from context of the author's words. And upon no dislike, is following him better or praying alone? Al-Ramli said: I did not see it, and the apparent of their words is the second, and what seems good to me is the first, and perhaps their words suggest it. I have written on Sharh Zad al-Faqir by al-Ghazzi a good note on this issue, so consult it. The text of what he wrote: his statement 'it is permissible to follow without dislike' – the discussion remains on what is better: following him or alone? I have not seen any of our scholars explicitly state it; apparent of their words is the second. What appears and seems good to me is the first, because in the second is leaving the congregation when it is only obtained by it. Even if not, and there is a Hanafi who follows him, following him is better. How can praying alone be better when there is a righteous, learned, God-fearing, pure Shafi'i who considers the differing, and thereby the virtue of congregation is attained? I do not think any jurist would say it. And perhaps their words suggest what I lean towards. And Allah is the granter of success. I say: and it is supported by what is in al-Siraj where he said: if you ask what is better: to pray behind these or alone? He said: as for the wicked person, prayer behind him is better, for it is mentioned in al-Fatawa that if a man prays behind him, he attains the reward of congregation but does not attain the reward of praying behind a God-fearing person. As for the others, i.e., the slave, Bedouin, wicked person, and son of adultery, it is possible that praying alone is better due to their ignorance of imamate of prayer, and it is possible that they are analogous to prayer behind the wicked. Better to pray behind others because people dislike it. We mentioned that if there is a God-fearing Shafi'i who is cautious, then the mentioned cause for dislike is not present. If it is better behind a wicked person despite him not being trustworthy regarding religion, what about a God-fearing Shafi'i? The conclusion: the apparent is what al-Ramli said, and it is supported by the author's negation of dislike, and the apparent is that it means the preferable dislike (makruh tanzihi) proven regarding others. His statement: (second) that it was previously mentioned from al-Mujtaba that if he is observant of conditions and pillars according to us, then following him is valid according to the correct opinion and is disliked, otherwise it is not valid at all. His statement: (specifically in what is followed) meaning that if he sees him cupping and praying without disappearance nor redoing wudu, then following him is not valid. He said: (or in general) i.e., that he sees him praying without redoing wudu, then after that he sees him praying – this second prayer he does not know his lack of caution in it, but he has known it from him in another prayer, so he knows his lack of caution in general. The ruling of invalidity of following in this scenario is more restrictive than the first. His statement: (and al-Hindwani and a group said it is not valid) meaning on the basis that according to them the consideration is the imam's opinion. In al-Nahr it is said: on this, following is valid even if he is not cautious. Its apparent is permissibility even if he leaves some pillars and conditions according to us. But Allamah Nuh Afandi in Hawashi al-Durar mentioned that the consideration for permissibility of following a dissenter is the imam's opinion according to a group including al-Hindwani; he intended both the imam's and the follower's opinion, not only the imam's as some people understood. For the difference is in considering the imam's opinion, not in considering the follower's opinion, for considering his opinion in permissibility and impermissibility is agreed upon. Then he said: So the Hanafi follower, if he sees in... [PAGE_083] ... the following. End. It is transmitted for his Shafi'i school. Rather, if a Hanafi prays behind a dissenter of a school, the ruling is likewise. The apparent of al-Hidayah is that consideration is the follower's belief, and not the imam's belief, such that if the Hanafi sees his Shafi'i imam touching a woman without performing wudu, then follows him, then most of our scholars said it is permissible and it is the correct opinion, as in Fath al-Qadir and others. Al-Hindwani and a group said it is not valid. He argued in al-Nihayah that it is more analogous because the imam thinks his prayer is not prayer, so following would be building existence upon non-existence in the imam's opinion, and it is the basis. No. Because the follower sees its permissibility, and what matters for him is his own opinion, not others. Also, the imam's state should be interpreted as following Abu Hanifa, as much as possible, to interpret the Muslim's state as righteous, so their beliefs unite; otherwise, entering prayer without purity according to his belief would be necessary, which is haram, unless the scenario is that the follower knows it and the imam does not, as the commentator mentioned, so we restrict to the first answer. It is valid from him intentionally.
Source pages p. 82

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (gharh) on the ruling of following a mukhalif imam. It discusses three conditions based on what the follower knows about the imam: (1) if the follower knows the imam is cautious (muhtat) according to Hanafi fiqh, there is no karaah; (2) if he knows he is not cautious, then the prayer is invalid; (3) if he knows nothing, it is makruh. The author explores the meaning of 'caution' – whether it covers only pillars/conditions or also avoiding makruh acts. Most scholars agree that caution regarding invalidators suffices. The passage also addresses the betterment: following such an imam or praying alone? The author leans towards following to attain congregational reward, especially if the imam is pious and learned. Then follows discussion on the second condition: is knowledge of lack of caution required specifically for the act in question or generally? The author presents different views. Finally, an intra-Hanafi dispute: does validity depend on the imam's own belief or the follower's? The majority (including most mashayikh) consider the follower's belief, while al-Hindwani considers the imam's. The relied-upon position is that the follower's belief is the criterion, as stated in al-Hidayah. The passage concludes that if the follower knows the imam is not cautious in a specific act, following is invalid; but if he only knows generally, there is disagreement.

Key Terms
المخالف (al-mukhalif): A person whose fiqh follows a different madhhab, here specifically a Shafi'i imam.
الاحتياط (al-ihtiyat): Caution in observing all conditions and pillars according to the Hanafi madhhab, possibly including avoidance of makruh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a Hanafi follower knows nothing about whether the Shafi'i imam is cautious, what is the ruling on following him?
A) It is invalid (la sihha).
B) It is valid without dislike (bila karaah).
C) It is valid but disliked (makruh).
D) It is valid only if the imam is also Hanafi.

Key Takeaway
The validity of following a non-Hanafi imam hinges on the follower's knowledge: if he knows the imam is cautious, it is valid and not disliked; if he knows he is not cautious, it is invalid; if he knows nothing, it is valid but disliked; and the follower's own belief, not the imam's, is the criterion.

The Twelve (or Fourteen) Sunnah Rak'ahs: Numbers and Proof
Stating the number of sunan rak'ahs for each daily prayer and for Friday.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the exact number of sunnah muakkadah rak'ahs for each daily prayer and for Friday, and cite the primary hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Twelve sunnah rak'ahs daily, fourteen on Friday; perseverance earns Paradise.

This lesson covers the number of sunnah muakkadah rak'ahs that are strongly recommended for each prayer time. The Hanafi school has agreed upon these numbers based on authentic hadith. We will learn the breakdown and the primary evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Recognize that the matn lists sunnah prayers that are sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah), not fard or wajib. The passage states: 'السنة قبل الفجر وبعد الظهر والمغرب والعشاء ركعتان وقبل الظهر والجمعة وبعدها أربع'.
Sunnah muakkadah is a category between wajib and mandub.
2
Memorize the numbers for each prayer
For Fajr: 2 before. Zuhr: 4 before, 2 after. Maghrib: 2 after. Isha: 2 after. Friday: 4 before and 4 after.
These are the routinely performed rak'ahs.
3
Compute the daily total
Add: 2 + 4 + 2 + 2 + 2 = 12. On Friday, the Zuhr sunnah is replaced by the Jumu'ah sunnah (4+4), so total becomes 2(for Fajr) + 4(before Jumu'ah) + 4(after Jumu'ah) + 2(Maghrib) + 2(Isha) = 14.
The commentary explicitly states these totals.
4
Cite the hadith evidence
The primary proof is the hadith from Aisha in al-Tirmidhi: 'Whoever perseveres in twelve rak'ahs of sunnah, Allah will build for him a house in Paradise.'
This is dalil naqli (textual evidence) for the virtue of these rak'ahs.
5
Note the special status of Fajr sunnah
The author begins with Fajr sunnah because it is the strongest, as per hadith: the Prophet was most diligent with it, and 'two rak'ahs of Fajr are better than the world and everything in it.'
This indicates higher reward compared to other sunnan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والسنة قبل الفجر وبعد الظهر والمغرب والعشاء ركعتان وقبل الظهر والجمعة وبعدها أربع شروع في بيان النوافل بعد ذكر الواجب فذكر أنها نوعان: سنة ومندوب. فالأول في كل يوم ما عدا الجمعة ثنتا عشرة ركعة وفي يوم الجمعة أربع عشرة ركعة، والأصل فيه ما رواه الترمذي وغيره عن عائشة رضي الله عنها قالت قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم «من ثابر على ثنتي عشرة ركعة من السنة بنى الله له بيتاً في الجنة وذكرها كما في الكتاب. وروى مسلم أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان يصليها، وبدأ المصنف بسنة الفجر لأنها أقوى السنن باتفاق الروايات لما في الصحيحين عن عائشة رضي الله عنها قالت: لم يكن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم على شيء من النوافل أشد تعاهداً منه على ركعتي الفجر. وفي لفظ لمسلم «ركعتا الفجر خير من الدنيا وما فيها) (۱)
His statement: (And the sunnah before Fajr, after Zuhr, Maghrib, and Isha are two rak'ahs, and before Zuhr, Jumu'ah, and after it are four.) Beginning of explanation of nawafil after mentioning the obligatory. He mentioned that they are two types: sunnah and mandub. The first in every day except Friday is twelve rak'ahs, and on Friday it is fourteen rak'ahs. The proof for this is what al-Tirmidhi and others narrated from Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her, who said: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Whoever perseveres in twelve rak'ahs of sunnah, Allah will build for him a house in Paradise,' and she mentioned them as in the book. Muslim narrated that he used to pray them. The author began with sunnah of Fajr because it is the strongest of the sunan according to all narrations, as in the two Sahihs from Aisha: 'The Prophet was never more diligent with any nawafil than he was with the two rak'ahs of Fajr.' In a wording of Muslim: 'The two rak'ahs of Fajr are better than the world and everything in it.'
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage begins the explanation of the nawafil (voluntary prayers) after the section on obligatory prayers. The matn states that the sunnah prayers before Fajr, after Zuhr, Maghrib, and Isha are two rak'ahs each, and before Zuhr and Jumu'ah and after Jumu'ah are four rak'ahs. The commentary clarifies that nafilah is of two types: sunnah and mandub (recommended). The daily sunan amount to twelve rak'ahs on normal days and fourteen on Friday. The primary evidence is the hadith narrated by al-Tirmidhi and others from Aisha: whoever constantly prays twelve rak'ahs of sunnah will have a house built for him in Paradise. Additionally, Muslim narrates that the Prophet himself prayed them. The author gives special emphasis to the Fajr sunnah, as it is the strongest voluntary prayer, supported by multiple hadiths including the statement that it is better than the entire world.

Key Terms
السنة (al-sunnah): In this context, sunnah refers to the non-obligatory prayers that the Prophet consistently performed (sunnah muakkadah).
المندوب (al-mandub): Recommended acts that are not sunnah muakkadah; mentioned here as the second type of nawafil.

The Fixed Sunnah Prayers (Rawātib) and the Emphasis on Fajr
Explanation of fixed sunnah prayers and emphasis on Fajr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the number and category of the rawātib prayers and explain why the Fajr sunnah is considered the strongest sunnah mu'akkadah.

Core Idea
The Fajr sunnah is sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib, but so strongly emphasized that it is almost treated as obligatory.

In this passage, the author explains the fixed sunnah prayers (rawātib) that accompany the daily obligatory prayers. He lists the specific numbers for each prayer and presents the primary evidence from hadith. Special attention is given to the two rak'ahs before Fajr, which are highlighted as the strongest of all sunnah prayers. We will explore the ruling, the evidence, and the scholarly discussion around whether it reaches the level of obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on rawātib numbers
Locate the specific numbers of rak'ahs for each sunnah prayer: before Fajr (2), after Zuhr (2), before Zuhr (4), after Jumu'ah (4), etc. Note the total daily without Friday is 12, with Friday 14.
The matn gives the basic numbers; the commentary explains the total.
2
Examine the primary dalil
The hadith from Aisha (ra) promises a house in Paradise for persisting (thābara) on 12 rak'ahs of sunnah. This is the main evidence for the rawātib.
The word thābara indicates continuity, not obligation.
3
Analyze the emphasis on Fajr sunnah
Multiple narrations show the Prophet's diligence on the Fajr sunnah, never leaving it even in travel or illness. One hadith states it is better than the world and its contents.
This emphasis is why the author begins with Fajr.
4
Understand the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some Hanafi sources (al-Khulasah, al-Atabi) indicate wujūb due to severe warnings, but the majority (zahir al-riwayah) classifies it as sunnah mu'akkadah.
The passage presents both sides but concludes with the majority view.
5
Determine the mufta bihi ruling
The relied-upon position is sunnah mu'akkadah. It is not fard or wajib, but it should never be abandoned.
The practical effect: a sin is not incurred for missing it, but it is highly discouraged.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والسنة قبل الفجر وبعد الظهر والمغرب والعشاء ركعتان وقبل الظهر والجمعة وبعدها أربع شروع في بيان النوافل بعد ذكر الواجب فذكر أنها نوعان: سنة ومندوب. فالأول في كل يوم ما عدا الجمعة ثنتا عشرة ركعة وفي يوم الجمعة أربع عشرة ركعة، والأصل فيه ما رواه الترمذي وغيره عن عائشة رضي الله عنها قالت قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم «من ثابر على ثنتي عشرة ركعة من السنة بنى الله له بيتاً في الجنة وذكرها كما في الكتاب. وروى مسلم أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان يصليها، وبدأ المصنف بسنة الفجر لأنها أقوى السنن باتفاق الروايات لما في الصحيحين عن عائشة رضي الله عنها قالت: لم يكن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم على شيء من النوافل أشد تعاهداً منه على ركعتي الفجر. وفي لفظ لمسلم «ركعتا الفجر خير من الدنيا وما فيها) (۱) وفي أوسط الطبراني عنها أيضاً : لم أره ترك الركعتين قبل صلاة الفجر في سفر ولا حضر ولا صحة ولا سقم. وقد ذكروا ما يدل على وجوبها قال في الخلاصة : أجمعوا أن ركعتي الفجر قاعداً من غير عذر لا يجوز . كذا روى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة ا هـ . وفي النهاية قال مشايخنا : العالم إذا صار مرجعاً في الفتاوى يجوز له ترك سائر السنن الحاجة الناس إلى فتواه إلا سنة الفجر ا.هـ. وفي المضمرات معزياً إلى العتابي : من أنكر سنة الفجر يخشى عليه الكفر. وفي الخلاصة : الظاهر من الجواب أن السنة لا تقضي إلا سنة الفجر . ومما يدل على وجوبها ما في سنن أبي داود عن أبي هريرة قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم «لا تدعوا ركعتي الفجر ولو طردتكم الخيل (۲) فقد وجدت المواظبة عليها بما قدمناه والنهي عن تركها لكن المنقول في أكثر الكتب أنها سنة مؤكدة، وإن قلنا إنها بمعنى الواجب هنا لم يصح لأنها تتأدى بمطلق النية . قال في التجنيس : رجل صلى ركعتين تطوعاً وهو يظن أن الفجر لم يطلع فإذا الفجر طالع يجزئه عن ركعتي الفجر هو الصحيح لأن السنة تطوع فتتأدى بنية التطوع لكن في الخلاصة : الأصح أنها لا تنوب وهو يدل على الوجوب .
His statement: (And the sunnah before Fajr and after Zuhr, Maghrib, and Isha is two rak'ahs, and before Zuhr and Jumu'ah and after them four) is a commencement in explaining the nawafil after mentioning the obligatory. He mentioned that they are two types: sunnah and mandub. The first in every day except Jumu'ah is twelve rak'ahs, and on Jumu'ah fourteen rak'ahs. The basis for that is what al-Tirmidhi and others narrated from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Whoever persists on twelve rak'ahs of sunnah, Allah will build for him a house in Paradise,' and he mentioned them as in the book. Muslim narrated that he (peace be upon him) used to pray them. The author began with the sunnah of Fajr because it is the strongest of the sunnahs by agreement of narrations, due to what is in the two Sahihs from Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) who said: 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) was not more diligent over any nawafil than he was over the two rak'ahs of Fajr.' In a wording of Muslim: 'The two rak'ahs of Fajr are better than the world and what is in it.' And in al-Awsat of al-Tabarani from her also: 'I never saw him leave the two rak'ahs before Fajr prayer, whether traveling or at home, healthy or sick.' They have mentioned what indicates their obligation. It is said in al-Khulasah: They agreed that praying the two rak'ahs of Fajr sitting without an excuse is not permissible. Similarly, al-Hasan reported from Abu Hanifa. In al-Nihayah, our scholars said: A scholar who becomes a reference for fatwas is allowed to leave other sunnahs due to people's need for his fatwa, except the sunnah of Fajr. In al-Mudmarat, citing al-Atabi: Whoever denies the sunnah of Fajr, it is feared that he will fall into disbelief. In al-Khulasah: The apparent from the answer that the sunnah is not made up except the sunnah of Fajr. And among what indicates its obligation is what is in Sunan Abi Dawud from Abu Hurairah who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Do not leave the two rak'ahs of Fajr even if horses trample you.' So, constant observance of it as we have mentioned and the prohibition of leaving it is found, but what is transmitted in most books is that it is a strongly emphasized sunnah. And if we say it is in the meaning of obligatory here, it would not be correct because it is performed by absolute intention. It is said in al-Tajnis: A man prayed two rak'ahs voluntarily thinking that Fajr had not risen, but Fajr had risen; it suffices for the two rak'ahs of Fajr; this is the correct view, because the sunnah is voluntary and is performed by intention of voluntary. But in al-Khulasah: The most correct is that it does not count, and that indicates obligation.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the fixed sunnah prayers (rawātib) that accompany the five daily prayers. The author lists the numbers: 2 before Fajr, 4 before Zuhr (and 2 after, but the matn says 2 after Zuhr? Actually the matn says: 'before Fajr, after Zuhr, Maghrib, Isha: 2; before Zuhr and Jumu'ah and after them: 4.' The commentary clarifies that the daily total is 12 rak'ahs (or 14 on Jumu'ah). The primary evidence is the hadith of Aisha promising a house in Paradise for persisting on 12 rak'ahs. The author emphasizes the two rak'ahs before Fajr as the strongest sunnah, citing multiple hadith, including the Prophet's diligence, their superiority over the world, and never leaving them even in travel or illness. Some scholars even indicate obligation (wujūb) because of the severe warnings against abandoning them, though the classical books call it mu'akkadah (emphasized). The passage also discusses a practical ruling: if one intends voluntary prayer and then realizes Fajr has risen, does it count for the sunnah? The correct view in al-Tajnis is yes, because the sunnah is a type of nafl, but al-Khulasah says no, indicating obligation. The relied-upon view is that the Fajr sunnah is a strongly emphasized sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah), not obligatory, but it is treated with extreme care.

Key Terms
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): A strongly emphasized sunnah that the Prophet always performed and rarely left
راتبة (rātibah): Fixed sunnah prayer associated with a particular fard prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) 10
B) 12
C) 14
D) 16

Key Takeaway
The Fajr sunnah is the strongest of the rawātib and is sunnah mu'akkadah; it should be guarded diligently, and it is not permissible to abandon it even for a scholar's needs.

The Legal Status of the Two Rak'ahs of Fajr: Sunnah Mu'akkadah or Wajib?
Discussion of evidence for obligation and the final ruling of sunnah mu'akkadah for Fajr sunnah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the two rak'ahs of Fajr, identify the key evidence used, and explain why the school rules it as sunnah mu'akkadah despite strong indications of obligation.

Core Idea
The Fajr sunnah is sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib—the imperative hadith is interpreted as emphasis, not obligation due to its zanni transmission.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents various pieces of evidence that strongly emphasize the two rak'ahs before Fajr, including a hadith with an imperative, agreement of scholars on certain aspects, and statements that a scholar may leave other sunnahs but not this one. Yet the consistent Hanafi position, as transmitted in most books, is that it remains sunnah mu'akkadah. Understanding why requires distinguishing between strong recommendation and legal obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal category
The act is the two rak'ahs performed before the obligatory Fajr prayer. Determine what type of prayer it is (sunnah, wajib, fard).
The text initially presents evidence that might suggest obligation.
2
Examine the evidence for obligation
List the proofs mentioned: 1) Ijma' that it is not permissible to pray them sitting without excuse (as reported by al-Hasan from Abu Hanifa). 2) The hadith: 'Do not leave the two rak'ahs of Fajr, even if horses trample you.' 3) Statements that a scholar may leave other sunnahs but not this one, and that it is the only sunnah that is made up (qada).
These are strong indicators but not definitive.
3
Note the concluding ruling
Despite the above, the majority of Hanafi books state it is sunnah mu'akkadah. The author explains that if we claimed it is wajib, it would not be valid because it is performed with absolute intention (unlike wajib prayers which require specific intent).
This indicates the school's reliance on other principles.
4
Understand the hanafi usul reasoning
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), so the imperative is not sufficient to establish obligation unless supported by other qat'i evidence. The school interprets the imperative as emphasizing strong recommendation, and the consensus of most books supports the sunnah status.
This shows the role of usul al-fiqh in deriving rulings.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, the two rak'ahs of Fajr are sunnah mu'akkadah: regularly performed, reward for doing, no sin for leaving, but leaving is disliked (makruh tanzihan if habitual).
Contrast with wajib like Witr where leaving is sinful.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد ذكروا ما يدل على وجوبها قال في الخلاصة : أجمعوا أن ركعتي الفجر قاعداً من غير عذر لا يجوز . كذا روى الحسن عن أبي حنيفة ا هـ . وفي النهاية قال مشايخنا : العالم إذا صار مرجعاً في الفتاوى يجوز له ترك وجوبها ما في سنن أبي داود عن أبي هريرة قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم «لا تدعوا ركعتي الفجر ولو طردتكم الخيل» فقد وجدت المواظبة عليها بما قدمناه والنهي عن تركها لكن المنقول في أكثر الكتب أنها فتتأدى بنية التطوع لكن في الخلاصة : الأصح أنها لا تنوب وهو يدل على الوجوب . وفيها أيضاً : اهـ. عن ثوب الشافعي الإمام منياً لا يجوز له الاقتداء به اتفاقاً لأن المني نجس على رأي الحنفي، وإذا رأى في ثوبه لا يحل وهو غير سديد ا هـ . قلت : قد مر عدم جواز صلاة الوتر قاعداً عند الإمامين أيضاً مع أنهما قائلان بسنيته تأمل قوله : يخشى عليه الكفر) وقع في عبارة مسكين حتى يكفر جاحدها واستشكله بعض الفضلاء بما صرحوا به من عدم تكفير جاحد الوتر إجماعاً وغاية ركعتي الفجر أن تكون كالوتر فكيف يكفر جاحدها؟ وأجاب بأن المراد من الجحود في جانب الوتر جحود وجوبه لا أصله بخلافه في جانب ركعتي الفجر فإن المراد به جحود د ويأتي قريباً فكان حق التعبير أن يقول وإن المؤكدة هي قلنا إنها واجبة . مر الألفاظ المكفرة
They have mentioned what indicates its obligation. He said in al-Khulasa: They agreed that the two rak'ahs of Fajr sitting without excuse are not permissible. Thus has al-Hasan reported from Abu Hanifa. End. In al-Nihaya, our scholars said: The scholar, when he becomes a reference for fatwas, may leave the rest of the sunnahs due to people's need for his fatwa, except the Sunnah of Fajr. In al-Mudmarat, attributed to al-Utabi: Whoever denies the Sunnah of Fajr, it is feared for him disbelief. In al-Khulasa: The apparent from the answer is that no sunnah is made up except the Sunnah of Fajr. Among what indicates its obligation is what is in Sunan Abi Dawud from Abu Hurayra, who said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'Do not leave the two rak'ahs of Fajr, even if horses trample you.' I have found continuous practice on them as we have presented, and the prohibition of leaving them. But what is transmitted in most books is that they are a stressed sunnah. And if we say they are in the sense of obligation here, it is not valid because they are performed with absolute intention. He said in al-Tajnis: A man prayed two rak'ahs voluntarily thinking that Fajr had not risen, and then Fajr rose, it suffices for the two rak'ahs of Fajr; that is the correct view because the sunnah is voluntary and is performed with the intention of voluntary prayer. But in al-Khulasa: The more correct view is that it does not substitute, and that indicates obligation. And in it also: End. Regarding the garment of a Shafi'i imam with semen, it is not permissible to follow him by agreement because semen is impure according to the Hanafi view. And if he sees a small amount of impurity on his garment, following him is permissible according to the majority and not permissible according to some because a small amount of impurity is a preventer according to the Imam's view, but the relied-upon view is the two imams'. End. But let this be considered: what has passed of the permissibility of a Hanafi following one who makes taslim from the two rak'ahs in Witr, based on the fact that this taslim does not exit him in his belief, while in the follower's view he has exited. So let it be verified. His statement: (it is not permissible). Al-Ramli said: Meaning it is not valid, as indicated by his statement earlier: 'They have mentioned what indicates its obligation.' And some understood that its meaning is that it is not lawful, and that is not sound. End. I say: The impermissibility of praying Witr sitting has passed also according to the two imams, even though they hold its sunnah status. Consider his statement: 'it is feared for him disbelief.' It occurred in the expression of Miskin: 'so that its denier disbelieves.' Some scholars objected to it based on what they have explicitly stated of the non-declaration of disbelief of the denier of Witr by consensus. And the utmost of the two rak'ahs of Fajr is that they are like Witr, so how can its denier be declared a disbeliever? He answered that what is meant by denial in the case of Witr is denial of its obligation, not its origin, contrary to the case of the two rak'ahs of Fajr, for what is meant is denial of the origin of the sunnah. So there is no contradiction. Even if one denies Witr itself, he disbelieves. Some supported him with what he transmitted from al-Shaykh Qasim in his statement: 'Whoever denies the origin of Witr and the origin of the sacrifice disbelieves.' End. But it is contradicted by the apparent statement of al-Zayla'i: 'And its denier is not declared a disbeliever because it is established by a solitary report, so it is not free from doubt.' End. It may be said: What is meant is denial of obligation, not the origin of legislation because of the consensus on it. Consider his statement: (And if we say it is in the sense of obligation) it is not hidden that the sunnah is what is in the sense of obligation from the aspect of sin, as will come soon. So the right expression would be to say: 'and if we say it is obligatory.' The statements of declaring disbelief have passed.
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expanded commentary on the ruling of the two rak'ahs of Fajr (sunnah al-Fajr). The author presents various evidence indicating the strong emphasis on this sunnah, to the point where some scholars argued it is wajib, though the relied-upon position is that it is sunnah mu'akkadah. The passage includes a hadith from Abu Dawud, a statement about the permissibility of a mufti leaving other sunnahs but not this one, and a discussion on the kufr of denying it. The author then addresses a dispute about whether one can count a voluntary prayer as the Fajr sunnah if done unintentionally, and also the issue of an Imam with impurity on his clothes. The central point is the distinction between denying the origin of the sunnah (which is kufr) and denying its obligation (which is not kufr). The commentary emphasizes that despite the strong evidence, the school maintains it is sunnah mu'akkadah, and the chapter ends with clarification of the terminology.

Key Terms
سنة الفجر (sunnah al-Fajr): The two rak'ahs prayed before the obligatory Fajr prayer.
مؤكدة (mu'akkadah): A sunnah that the Prophet consistently performed and encouraged, but not to the level of obligation.
الجحود (al-jahud): Denial or rejection of a religious ruling, which can lead to kufr if it involves denying what is necessarily known.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority of Hanafi books, what is the ruling of the two rak'ahs of Fajr?
A) Wajib
B) Sunnah mu'akkadah
C) Fard
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
The two rak'ahs of Fajr are sunnah mu'akkadah: highly recommended but not obligatory, based on the hadith's zanni transmission and school consensus.

Denial of the Fajr Sunnah and the Limits of Takfir
Discussion of the judicial ruling on denying the Fajr sunnah and the limits of takfir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between denying the origin of the Fajr sunnah (which may lead to kufr) and denying its obligation (which does not), applying the Hanafi position on takfir.

Core Idea
Denying the origin of the Fajr sunnah risks kufr, but denying its obligation does not—the ruling is zanni, so takfir requires caution.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a critical issue: the ruling on a person who denies the Fajr sunnah. While some statements indicate fear of kufr, the author clarifies that this applies only to denying the origin of the sunnah (its being from the Prophet), not to denying its obligation. This distinction is essential for proper application of takfir in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The text discusses the statement: 'Whoever denies the Sunnah of Fajr, it is feared for him disbelief.' This raises the question of when denial leads to kufr.
2
Distinguish between origin and obligation
The author explains that denial can be of two types: (a) denial of the very existence of this prayer as a sunnah from the Prophet (origin), and (b) denial of its legal obligation (i.e., claiming it is not wajib).
Denying the origin attacks the basis of the ruling; denying obligation simply rejects a particular legal classification.
3
Apply the hanafi principle on takfir
Hanafis hold that denial of matters established by definitively certain (qat'i) evidence leads to kufr. The Fajr sunnah is established by ahad hadith (zanni), so denying its origin may still be problematic but not automatically kufr. Denying its obligation is not kufr because the obligation itself is not qat'i.
The text cites al-Zayla'i: 'Its denier is not declared a disbeliever because it is established by a solitary report.'
4
Analyze the counterpoint
Some scholars argued that denying the origin of Witr leads to kufr, and by analogy, denying the origin of Fajr sunnah would also. But the Hanafi school distinguishes: the origin of Witr is also zanni, so the same principle applies.
The text resolves by saying what is meant is denial of obligation, not origin, in the case of Fajr sunnah.
5
Conclude the practical ruling
One who denies that the Prophet taught the Fajr sunnah may be in danger of kufr because it rejects a known sunnah. One who says it is not wajib is not a disbeliever, as the school itself says it is sunnah mu'akkadah.
This shows the importance of precise language in fatwa.

They have mentioned what indicates its obligation. He said in al-Khulasa: They agreed that the two rak'ahs of Fajr sitting without excuse are not permissible. Thus has al-Hasan reported from Abu Hanifa. End. In al-Nihaya, our scholars said: The scholar, when he becomes a reference for fatwas, may leave the rest of the sunnahs due to people's need for his fatwa, except the Sunnah of Fajr. In al-Mudmarat, attributed to al-Utabi: Whoever denies the Sunnah of Fajr, it is feared for him disbelief. Among what indicates its obligation is what is in Sunan Abi Dawud from Abu Hurayra, who said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'Do not leave the two rak'ahs of Fajr, even if horses trample you.' I have found continuous practice on them as we have presented, and the prohibition of leaving them. But what is transmitted in most books is that they are a stressed sunnah. And if we say they are in the sense of obligation here, it is not valid because they are performed with absolute intention. He answered that what is meant by denial in the case of Witr is denial of its obligation, not its origin, contrary to the case of the two rak'ahs of Fajr, for what is meant is denial of the origin of the sunnah. But it is contradicted by the apparent statement of al-Zayla'i: 'And its denier is not declared a disbeliever because it is established by a solitary report, so it is not free from doubt.' End. It may be said: What is meant is denial of obligation, not the origin of legislation because of the consensus on it. Consider his statement: (And if we say it is in the sense of obligation) it is not hidden that the sunnah is what is in the sense of obligation from the aspect of sin, as will come soon. So the right expression would be to say: 'and if we say it is obligatory.' The statements of declaring disbelief have passed.

When the Last Two of Four Night Rak'ahs Fall After Dawn: Do They Count as Fajr Sunnah?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on substitution of night voluntary for Fajr sunnah, with sunan listed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on whether the last two of four night rak'ahs count as the Fajr sunnah, and identify the relied-upon fatwa and its practical consequence.

Core Idea
Voluntary prayer can substitute for the Fajr sunnah if intended generally, according to the Sahibayn and the fatwa.

A worshipper prays four rak'ahs at night, but after finishing realizes the last two occurred after dawn. Should he perform the Fajr sunnah separately? The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the last two already count, while some later scholars, like the author of al-Tajnis, disagree. This lesson unpacks the dispute, the opposing proof via qiyas with Zuhr, and the operative ruling for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario and legal question
Read the passage: a man prayed four rak'ahs at night, and it becomes clear that the last two were after dawn. The legal question is whether those two rak'ahs fulfill the sunnah of Fajr.
The scenario assumes the person intended voluntary prayer for all four.
2
State the position of the Sahibayn and the fatwa
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), and one narration from Abu Hanifa, the last two rak'ahs count for the Fajr sunnah. The text explicitly says 'wa bihi yufta' (with it fatwa is given).
This is the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school.
3
Present the opposing view and its proof
The author of al-Tajnis argues they do not count, using qiyas with Zuhr: if one prays six rak'ahs for Zuhr and sits after four, the extra two do not count. Similarly, the Fajr sunnah requires a new opening takbir (tahrimah mubtada'ah).
The opposing view is also intra-Hanafi.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response distinguishing the cases
The Hanafi response is that the Zuhr case differs because the extra rak'ahs were not intended for Zuhr (they were superfluous), whereas here the entire four were intended as voluntary prayer. Since voluntary prayer is general, it can encompass the sunnah of Fajr.
The key distinction is the intention (niyyah) covering the act.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and its consequence
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that the last two count, so the person does not need to repeat the Fajr sunnah. If he relied on the opposing view, he would have to make it up later.
The fatwa follows the Sahibayn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Miscellaneous from Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani: A man prayed four rak'ahs at night, and it became clear that the last two rak'ahs were after the rise of Fajr. They count for the two rak'ahs of Fajr according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and in one of the two narrations from Abu Hanifa. He said: And with it fatwa is given. End. And it was refuted in al-Tajnis that the more correct view is that they do not substitute for the two rak'ahs of Fajr, just as if one prayed six rak'ahs for Zuhr and sat at the end of the fourth, the two rak'ahs do not substitute for the two rak'ahs in the correct answer. This because the sunnah is what the Prophet, peace be upon him, consistently performed, and his consistent practice was with a new opening takbir. In al-Khulasa: The sunan in the two rak'ahs of Fajr are three: one is to recite in the first rak'ah 'Qul ya ayyuha al-kafirun' and in the second 'al-Ikhlas'. The second is to perform them at the beginning of the time. The third is to perform them in his house, otherwise at the door of the mosque, otherwise in the winter part of the mosque if the Imam is in the summer part or vice versa if he hopes to catch up. And if the mosque is one, he should perform them in a corner of the mosque and not pray them mingling with the rows, contrary to the congregation; if he does so, it is severely disliked, and he should not lengthen the recitation. And if he remembers during Fajr that he did not pray the two rak'ahs of Fajr, he does not interrupt.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a specific scenario: a man prays four rak'ahs at night, and it becomes apparent that the last two occurred after dawn. The question is whether these two can count as the sunnah of Fajr. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn), they do count, and this is the position given for fatwa. There is also a narration from Abu Hanifa agreeing, but another narration rejects it. The author of al-Tajnis refutes the substitution, arguing that the sunnah requires a new intention and opening takbir, similar to the case of Zuhr where extra rak'ahs after the prescribed number do not count. The passage then lists the recommended practices for the Fajr sunnah: reciting specific surahs, performing them early, and in the house or a specific location. It also mentions the ruling if one forgets them and remembers during the obligatory prayer.

Key Terms
تحريمة مبتدأة (tahrimah mubtada'ah): A new opening takbir separate from the previous prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon fatwa, if a man prays four rak'ahs at night and the last two are after dawn, what is the ruling?
A) They do not count as Fajr sunnah
B) They count as Fajr sunnah
C) They are invalid and must be repeated
D) They count only if he intended specifically for Fajr

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi view is that the last two of four night rak'ahs count as Fajr sunnah, and one should not interrupt one's Fajr obligation to make them up.

Ruling on Praying Fajr Sunnah in the Outer Mosque
Ruling on location of Fajr sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying the Fajr sunnah in the outer mosque when the imam is in the inner mosque and identify the basis for its permissibility.

Core Idea
The inner and outer mosque are one place, so praying separately is not disliked.

This lesson addresses a common scenario in large mosques: can one pray the Fajr sunnah in an outer area while the imam leads the fard inside? The text clarifies that the entire mosque complex is considered one location, so it is not disliked to pray separately. This ruling is based on the unity of the place for following the imam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The text presents an imam leading Fajr in the inner mosque and a man coming to pray Fajr (the sunnah) in the outer mosque.
‘Fajr’ here refers to the two rak‘ahs of the sunnah, as clarified in the commentary.
2
Note the difference of opinion
Some scholars said it is makruh, some said it is not. The reason for the disagreement is not fully given, but the text notes that when scholars differ, precaution is not to do it.
This is an internal Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Understand the reasoning for permissibility
Those who said it is not makruh argue that the inner and outer mosque are like one place, as evidenced by the permissibility of someone in the outer mosque following the imam in the inner mosque.
The unity of the mosque is the key principle.
4
Conclude the preferred view
The text does not explicitly give tarjih, but the reasoning based on unity of place suggests that the view of permissibility is stronger. The precautionary view is to avoid it, but the prayer is valid either way.
5
Apply to practice
If you are in a mosque with multiple areas, you may pray the Fajr sunnah in any part without it being disliked, provided the whole area is considered part of the mosque.
This applies to modern mosque complexes with halls and courtyards.

وذكر الولوالجي : إمام يصلي الفجر في المسجد الداخل فجاء رجل يصلي الفجر في المسجد الخارج اختلف المشايخ فيه ؛ قال بعضهم يكره، وقال بعضهم لا يكره لأن ذلك كله كمكان واحد بدلیل جواز الاقتداء لمن كان في المسجد الخارج بمن كان في المسجد الداخل، وإذا اختلف المشايخ فالاحتياط أن لا يفعل ا هـ. وفي القنية : إذا لم يسع وقت الفجر إلا الوتر والفجر أو السنة والفجر فإنه يوتر ويترك السنة عند أبي حنيفة وعندهما السنة أولى من الوتر . وفي المحيط ولو صلى ركعتي الفجر مرتين بعد الطلوع فالسنة آخرهما لأنه أقرب إلى المكتوبة ولم يتخلل بينهما صلاة والسنة ما تؤدي متصلاً بالمكتوبة ا هـ . وفي القنية واختلف اهـ. تتأدى إلا بالتعيين وهو الذي صححه قاضيخان وإن كان الجمهور على خلافه كما مر في شروط الصلاة، ويدل على ما قلنا ما في الذخيرة من الفصل الحادي عشر قال شمس الأئمة: وهذه الرواية تشهد أن السنة تحتاج إلى النية ا هـ . والإشارة إلى الرواية التي صححها صاحب الخلاصة قوله: (ورده في التجنيس) قال في النهر وترجيح التجنيس في المسألتين أوجه أي في هذه المسألة والتي قبلها قوله : فجاء رجل يصلي الفجر) أي ركعتي الفجر كما هو مصرح به في عبارة التجنيس قوله : (فالسنة آخرهما الخ) قال في النهر : هو مبني على أن الأفضل إيلاؤهما للفرض، وقيل تقديمهما أول الوقت، وجزم في الخلاصة به وعليه فينبغي كون السنة أولاهما ا هـ . خاتمة : في الموطأ أخبرنا مالك أخبرنا نافع عن عبد الله بن عمر رضي الله تعالى عنهما أنه رأى رجلاً ركع ركعتي الفجر ثم اضطجع فقال ابن عمر رضي الله عنه : ما شأنه؟ فقال نافع قلت : يفصل بين صلاته. قال ابن ضي الله تعالى عنهما وأي فصل أفضل من السلام؟ قال محمد: وهو قول أبي حنيفة ا هـ. كذا في شرح الشيخ إسماعيل قوله : (وفي القنية بقول ابن عمر نأخذ عمر
And al-Walwaliji mentioned: An Imam leading Fajr in the inner mosque, and a man came to pray Fajr in the outer mosque. The scholars differed regarding it; some said it is disliked, some said it is not disliked because all of that is like one place due to the permissibility of following for one in the outer mosque one in the inner mosque. And when scholars differ, the precaution is not to do it. End. In al-Qunyah: If the time of Fajr does not accommodate both Witr and Fajr, or the sunnah and Fajr, then he performs Witr and leaves the sunnah according to Abu Hanifa, while according to the two (disciples) the sunnah is preferable to Witr. In al-Muhit: If one prays the two rak'ahs of Fajr twice after sunrise, the sunnah is the latter because it is closer to the obligatory prayer and no prayer intervened between them, and the sunnah is performed immediately before the obligatory prayer. End. In al-Qunyah: And they differed. End. It is not performed except with specific intention, and that is what Qadikhan corrected, although the majority are contrary, as passed in the conditions of prayer. And it indicates what we said what is in al-Dhakhira from the eleventh chapter: Shams al-A'imma said: This narration witnesses that the sunnah needs intention. End. And the reference is to the narration that the author of al-Khulasa corrected. His statement: (And he refuted it in al-Tajnis). He said in al-Nahr: And the preference of al-Tajnis in the two issues is stronger, i.e., in this issue and the one before it. His statement: (Then a man came to pray Fajr) meaning the two rak'ahs of Fajr as is explicit in the expression of al-Tajnis. His statement: (The sunnah is the latter, etc.) He said in al-Nahr: It is based on the fact that the best is to adjoin them to the obligatory prayer, and it was said to do them at the beginning of the time. Al-Khulasa decisively stated it, and accordingly the sunnah should be the first. End. Conclusion: In al-Muwatta, Malik informed us, Nafi' informed us from Abdullah ibn Umar, may Allah be pleased with them, that he saw a man bowing the two rak'ahs of Fajr and then lying down. Ibn Umar said: What is the matter with him? Nafi' said: I said: He separates between his prayers. Ibn Umar said: And what separation is better than the taslim? Muhammad said: That is the statement of Abu Hanifa. End. Thus in the commentary of Shaykh Isma'il. His statement: (And in al-Qunyah, we take the statement of Ibn Umar, Umar.
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on the Fajr sunnah with several subsidiary issues. First, the location: if the imam is in the inner mosque, it is permissible for one in the outer mosque to follow, and it is not disliked to pray separately. Second, when time is short for both Witr and Fajr sunnah, Abu Hanifa prefers Witr, while the two disciples prefer the Fajr sunnah. Third, if one prays the Fajr sunnah twice after sunrise (i.e., after the time has passed), the second set is better as it is immediately before the missed obligatory prayer? Actually, the text is about repeating after sunrise? It says 'after sunrise' and the later one is considered sunnah because it is closer to the obligatory prayer? This seems problematic because after sunrise the Fajr time has passed. It might be about cases where one delays the sunnah until after the obligatory prayer? The commentary clarifies that the preferred view is to adjoin the sunnah to the fard. Finally, a report from the Muwatta of Malik about Ibn Umar seeing a man lie down after the Fajr sunnah, approving it as a separation between sunnah and fard. This practice is attributed to Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms
المسجد الداخل والخارج (al-masjid al-dakhil wa al-kharij): The inner and outer parts of a mosque complex.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why is it not considered makruh to pray the Fajr sunnah in the outer mosque when the imam is in the inner mosque?
A) Because the sunnah is best prayed at home.
B) Because the entire mosque is considered one place for following.
C) Because the man had not yet prayed the fard.
D) Because the imam's prayer is valid for all.

Key Takeaway
The inner and outer parts of a mosque are one place, so praying the Fajr sunnah in the outer mosque is not disliked.

7 min
Precedence of Witr over Fajr Sunnah When Time is Short
Intra-Hanafi dispute on precedence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on whether to pray Witr or the Fajr sunnah when time is short and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa prioritizes Witr; the Sahibayn prioritize the Fajr sunnah.

When the morning is tight and you fear missing the Fajr fard, which sunnah should you pray first? The Hanafi school has an internal difference. This lesson explains the views of Abu Hanifa and his two main disciples, and the practical consequence of their disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the scenario
The time for Fajr is short, and a person cannot pray both the Witr and the two rak‘ahs of Fajr sunnah and still catch the Fajr fard.
'The time of Fajr' here means the time remaining before sunrise.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa said: pray Witr and leave the Fajr sunnah.
Witr is considered wajib by Abu Hanifa, which may be why it takes precedence.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani said: the Fajr sunnah is preferable to Witr.
They may consider the Fajr sunnah more directly connected to the time of Fajr.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if time is short, a Hanafi following Abu Hanifa will pray Witr and miss the Fajr sunnah; one following the Sahibayn will pray the Fajr sunnah and miss Witr.
The mufta bihi in later fatwa is often the Sahibayn's view.
5
Note the absence of explicit tarjih
The text presents both views without stating which is stronger. Later Hanafi sources may prefer the Sahibayn's view.
The author of al-Bahr al-Raiq does not give tarjih here.

Source Text

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Witr

C) Both
D) Neither

5 min
The Practice of Lying Down After the Fajr Sunnah
Ruling on a recommended practice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi recommendation to lie down after the Fajr sunnah as a separation before the fard, and cite the relevant hadith from Ibn Umar.

Core Idea
Lying down after the Fajr sunnah is a recommended practice to separate between the sunnah and the fard.

The final part of the passage quotes a narration from the Muwatta of Imam Malik, where Abdullah ibn Umar approved of a man lying down after the Fajr sunnah. This lesson explores the Hanafi view that this practice is recommended, as it was adopted by Imam Abu Hanifa.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith
The text reports: Ibn Umar saw a man bow the two rak‘ahs of Fajr (the sunnah) and then lie down. Ibn Umar asked why, and the man said it was to separate between the prayers.
The hadith is from the Muwatta via Nafi‘.
2
Understand Ibn Umar's response
Ibn Umar remarked: 'And what separation is better than the taslim?' meaning the greeting of peace at the end of the sunnah already serves as a separation.
Ibn Umar's comment does not reject the practice; it acknowledges that the taslim is a separation, implying that lying down is an additional act.
3
Note the Hanafi adoption
Muhammad al-Shaybani said: 'That is the statement of Abu Hanifa,' indicating that Abu Hanifa adopted this practice as recommended.
Thus, the Hanafi school considers it sunnah to lie down after the Fajr sunnah.
4
Apply to practice
After completing the two rak‘ahs of Fajr sunnah, one may lie down for a short while before standing for the Fajr fard. This is a recommended act, not obligatory.
If one cannot lie down, the prayer is still valid.

Source Text

8 min
Substitution of Night Prayers for Sunnah of Fajr After Dawn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on substitution of night rak'ahs for Fajr sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on whether night prayer rak'ahs after dawn substitute for the sunnah of Fajr and evaluate the preponderant view.

Core Idea
Sunnah prayers require separate intention; time overlap does not automatically substitute one for another.

This passage examines a specific scenario: a person prays four rak'ahs at night, but the last two occur after dawn. Do those two count as the sunnah of Fajr? The Hanafi school has divergent views, and the passage presents the arguments and the relied-upon ruling. You will learn to identify the positions and understand the reasoning behind the preponderant view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the core issue
Recognize that the scenario involves a person who prayed four rak'ahs at night, then discovered that the last two were after Fajr time. The issue is whether those two rak'ahs can substitute for the sunnah of Fajr.
The key is that the intention was for night prayer, not specifically for Fajr sunnah.
2
State the positions of the Sahibayn and Abu Hanifa
According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (Sahibayn), and one narration from Abu Hanifa, the two rak'ahs do count as the sunnah of Fajr. This was the basis for fatwa.
The phrase 'عندهما' refers to both companions.
3
Analyze the refutation from al-Tajnis
The author of al-Tajnis argues that the correct view is no substitution, using an analogy: if one prays six rak'ahs for Dhuhr and sits after the fourth, the extra two do not count as the sunnah of Dhuhr.
This analogy rests on the principle that supererogatory prayers must be intended as such.
4
Understand the underlying rationale
The sunnah of Fajr is defined by the Prophet's continuous practice (muwazabah). Substitution would require a specific intention or textual indication, which is absent here.
The text breaks off but the logic is clear: the sunnah is a distinct act of worship.
5
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
Although the fatwa was initially given on the substitution view, al-Tajnis declares it incorrect. Later Hanafi practice generally adopts the view that substitution does not occur.
This shows how later scholarship can supersede earlier fatwa practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
متفرقات شمس الأئمة الحلواني رجل صلى أربع ركعات في الليل فتبين أن الركعتين الآخرتين بعد طلوع الفجر تحتسب عن ركعتي الفجر عندهما وإحدى الروايتين عن أبي حنيفة قال وبه يفتي ا هـ . ورده في التجنيس بأن الأصح أنها لا تنوب عن ركعتي الفجر كما إذا صلى الظهر ستاً وقد قعد على رأس الرابعة فإنه لا تنوب الركعتان عن ركعتي في الصحيح من الجواب كذا .هذا وهذا لأن السنة ما واظب النبي يا الله عليها ومواظبته عليه
From the scattered notes of Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani: A man prayed four rak'ahs during the night, and it became clear that the last two rak'ahs were after the break of dawn. According to them (Sahibayn) they count as the two rak'ahs of Fajr, and one of the two narrations from Abu Hanifa (he said: and on this the fatwa is given). And it was refuted in al-Tajnis by saying that the correct view is that they do not substitute for the two rak'ahs of Fajr, just as if he prayed six rak'ahs for Dhuhr and sat at the end of the fourth, then the two extra rak'ahs do not substitute for the two rak'ahs of Dhuhr in the correct answer. This is because the sunnah is what the Prophet, peace be upon him, adhered to, and his adherence...
Source pages p. 85

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the substitution of night supererogatory prayers for the sunnah of Fajr. The scenario: a person prays four rak'ahs during the night but then realizes that the last two rak'ahs occurred after the time of Fajr had begun. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (Sahibayn), these last two rak'ahs are deemed to count as the sunnah of Fajr. There is also a narration from Abu Hanifa that agrees with this, and it is stated that the fatwa is given on this view. However, the author of al-Tajnis refutes this, asserting that the correct stance is that the two rak'ahs do not substitute for the Fajr sunnah. He draws an analogy: if a person prays six rak'ahs for Dhuhr and sits after the fourth, the subsequent two rak'ahs do not replace the regular two rak'ahs of the sunnah. The underlying rationale is that the sunnah is defined by the Prophet's continuous practice, and that practice involved a separate intention for the sunnah prayer.

Key Terms
تحتسب (tuhtasib): Counts or is considered as fulfilling the sunnah of Fajr
عندهما (indahuma): Refers to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the two companions of Abu Hanifa)
التجنيس (al-Tajnis): A work by an unnamed Hanafi scholar that refutes the substitution view

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to al-Tajnis, what is the correct ruling for the two rak'ahs prayed after dawn?
A) They count as the sunnah of Fajr.
B) They do not count as the sunnah of Fajr.
C) They are invalid and must be repeated.
D) They are optional and may be considered either way.

Key Takeaway
Sunnah prayers require specific intention and separate practice; time overlap does not automatically substitute one sunnah for another.
