للنفي أعني قوله لم تكن. وحاصل كلامه أن الحديثين المذكورين قد اتفقا على ركعتين وزاد أحدهما على الآخر ركعتين، ومقتضى ذلك أن يكون ما اتفقا عليه سنة لأنه ثابت منهما بيقين ويكون الأربع مستحباً والجواب أنه لم يكن كذلك لأنه لم يذكر في حديث عائشة رضي الله تعالى عنها للعصر سنة راتبة لا ركعتين ولا أربعاً فيقتضي عدم المواظبة على الركعتين أيضاً، ولا بد من المواظبة حتى تثبت السنة. وهذا ومقتضى الحديث الأول أن الأولى في الأربع الفصل لكن ذكر الشيخ إسماعيل عن الترمذي أن إسحق بن إبراهيم اختار أن لا يفصل في الأربع قبل العصر واحتج بهذا الحديث وقال : معنى أنه يفصل بينهن بالمسليم يعني التشهد ا هـ . ولعله جواب علمائنا أيضاً قوله : (ولم ينقلوا حديثاً فيه بخصوصه) نقل في الاختيار عن رضي الله عنها أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام كان يصلي قبل العشاء أربعاً ثم يصلي بعدها أربعاً ثم يضطجع ا هـ. ونقله عنه أيضاً في إمداد الفتاح ثم قال : وذكر في المحيط أن تطوع قبل العصر بأربع
Book of Prayer, Chapter of Witr and Supererogatory Prayers. Four, and the recommendation of four before Asr and Isha and after them, and six after Maghrib, and it is disliked to increase beyond four of the supererogatory prayers, end. And he corrected in his fatwas that he does not perform them in the mosque because it is one prayer, end. And it is not hidden what is in it, so the apparent is the first. And the evidence for the recommendation of four before Jumu'ah is what Muslim narrated as a marfu' hadith: 'Whoever prays before Jumu'ah, let him pray four,' along with what Ibn Majah narrated from Ibn Abbas that the Messenger of Allah used to pray four before Jumu'ah without separating between them. And for the recommendation of four after it is what is in Sahih Muslim from Abu Huraira as marfu': 'When one of you prays Jumu'ah, let him pray after it four.' And in another narration: 'When you pray after Jumu'ah, pray four.' And it is mentioned in al-Bada'i' that it is the apparent narration. And from Abu Yusuf that he should pray four then two. And Muhammad mentioned in Kitab al-I'tikaf that the mu'takif stays in the congregational mosque the amount of time to pray four or six, end. And in al-Dhakhira and al-Tajnis: many of our mashayikh follow Abu Yusuf's saying. And in Munyat al-Musalli: the best in our view is to pray four then two. And in al-Qunyah: He prayed the obligatory prayer and food came; if the taste of the food or part of it goes away, he should eat then perform the sunnah; and if he fears the time will go, he performs the sunnah then eats. And if he vowed the sunnah and performed what he vowed, it is the sunnah. And Taj al-Din Abu Sahib al-Muhit said: He is not considered as performing the sunnah because when he committed to it, it became something else, so it does not substitute for the sunnah. And if he delays the sunnah after the obligatory prayer and then performs it at the end of the time, it is not sunnah; and it is said it is sunnah, end. And the best in the sunan is to perform them at home except for Tarawih; and it is said that virtue is not specific to one way over another, and that is the most correct, but whatever is farthest from ostentation and most conducive to humility and sincerity is best. Thus in al-Nihayah. And in al-Khulasah regarding the sunnah of Maghrib: If he fears that returning home will occupy him with other matters, he performs it in the mosque; and if he does not fear, he prays it at home. Similarly for all other sunan, even Jumu'ah, and Witr at home is better, end. His saying: (and the recommendation of four before Asr and Isha and after them and six after Maghrib) is an explanation of the recommended, for a morsel or a sip does not nullify the sunnah, i.e., does not diminish its reward, since actual nullification is unlikely due to the absence of a contradicting factor, reflect. His saying: (in the whole because it is one prayer) and it has preceded in the explanation of his saying 'and after the first two he suffices with al-Fatiha' that what was mentioned of Muslim regarding before Zuhr, because they explicitly stated that the preemption of the first intercessor is not nullified by transferring to the second pair from it, and if one corrupts it, he makes up four; and the four before Jumu'ah are like it. As for the four after Jumu'ah, it is not accepted, rather it is like other sunan, because they have not established for them those mentioned rulings, end. But he mentioned in Sharh al-Munyah these three sunan and derived those rulings from them. His saying: (and on the recommendation of four after it is what is in Sahih Muslim etc.) The first hadith indicates obligation, and the second indicates recommendation, so we say it is a confirmed sunnah to combine between them. Thus it is stated in Sharh al-Munyah. And in al-Sharnablaliyya: and the apparent statement of the author, meaning the author of al-Durar, is that the ruling of the sunnah of Jumu'ah is like that before Zuhr, so that if one performs it with two taslims, it is not considered valid, and it should be restricted to when there is no excuse, because of the Prophet's saying: 'When you pray after Jumu'ah, pray four; if something hurries you, pray two in the mosque and two when you return.' The hadith is mentioned in al-Burhan as evidence for establishing the four after Jumu'ah, end. His saying: (and from Abu Yusuf etc.) He said in al-Dhakhira: and from Ali that he prayed six: two then four; and from him another narration that he prayed after it six: four then two; and this is what Abu and al-Tahawi and many mashayikh took, may Allah have mercy on them. And on this, Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani said: The principle is to pray four then two; he indicated that he has a choice between presenting the four and presenting the two, but the best is to present the four so that he does not become a supererogatory worshiper after the obligatory prayer like it, end. His saying: (because it is established with certainty) is the reason for the negation. And his saying 'and it is' is a new sentence, and it would be better to be in the jussive as a conjunct to the negated 'it is not' with 'lam'. And his saying 'because he did not mention' is the reason for the negation, i.e., his saying 'it was not'. The summary of his words is that the two mentioned hadiths agree on two rak'ahs, and one of them added two more, so what is agreed upon should be sunnah because it is established with certainty from both, and the four are mustahab. The answer is that it is not so, because in Aisha's hadith no regular sunnah is mentioned for Asr, neither two nor four, so it implies that even the two are not regularly performed; and regularity is required for the sunnah to be established. This and the implication of the first hadith is that it is preferable to separate in the four, but Sheikh Ismail reported from Tirmidhi that Ishaq ibn Ibrahim chose not to separate in the four before Asr, and he used this hadith as evidence, saying: the meaning of 'he separated between them with the salam' means the tashahhud, end. Perhaps it is also the answer of our scholars. His saying: (and they did not narrate a hadith specifically about it) He narrated in al-Ikhtiyar from Aisha that the Prophet used to pray four before Isha, then four after it, then lie down, end. And it was also narrated from him in Imdad al-Fattah, then he said: and it is mentioned in al-Muhit that voluntary prayer before Asr with four...
Source pages p. 87

Commentary
This passage is a commentary expansion from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, specifically on the section regarding supererogatory prayers (sunan) associated with Jumu'ah, Asr, Maghrib, and Isha. The author begins by stating the ruling: it is recommended to pray four rak'ahs before and after Jumu'ah and Isha, four before Asr, and six after Maghrib. He then clarifies a previous correction that one should not combine two sets of four in the mosque because they constitute one prayer. The commentator prefers the apparent meaning. He then provides proofs from hadith: for the four before Jumu'ah, a hadith from Muslim and Ibn Majah; for the four after Jumu'ah, a hadith from Muslim and Abu Huraira with an additional narration. He notes that in Al-Bada'i' this is considered the apparent position of the school. The passage then discusses the view of Abu Yusuf that one should pray four then two. Muhammad al-Shaybani mentions that a mu'takif should stay the time of four or six. Many later mashayikh follow Abu Yusuf. The author also presents the best practice from Munyat al-Musalli and various rulings on performing sunan at home vs. mosque, including special considerations for Maghrib and Jumu'ah. The commentary then delves into the specifics of the sunan for Jumu'ah, equating them with Zuhr sunnas. It addresses a textual issue regarding whether the hadith indicates obligation or recommendation, resolving it by considering it a confirmed sunnah. The passage includes a detailed discussion on the sunnah of Asr: two rak'ahs are a confirmed sunnah because they are found in both narrations, while four are mustahab. This is based on the absence of a regular sunnah in Aisha's hadith. For Isha, the author notes that although no specific hadith is transmitted, practice from Aisha shows four before and after. The commentary ends with a reference to the voluntary prayer before Asr with four. Throughout, the author follows the Hanafi madhhab, presenting evidences and resolving internal differences.

Key Terms
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): A confirmed supererogatory prayer that the Prophet regularly performed and recommended.
نفل (nafl): Voluntary prayer, less emphasized than sunnah mu'akkadah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following sunnan is specifically mentioned as six rak'ahs?
A) Before Asr
B) After Maghrib
C) Before Isha
D) After Isha

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prescribes 2 sunnah before Asr (plus 2 mustahab), 6 after Maghrib, and 4 before and after Isha, all based on practice and hadith.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Distinguishing Sunnah Ratibah from Mustahabb in Supererogatory Prayers
Commentary on the legal status of supererogatory prayers associated with obligatory prayers, distinguishing sunnah ratibah from mustahabb.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the status of supererogatory prayers before and after Asr, Maghrib, Isha, and Zuhr, and apply the principle of muwazabah to distinguish sunnah ratibah from mustahabb.

Core Idea
Consistent prophetic practice (muwazabah) determines sunnah ratibah; occasional practice renders it mustahabb.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi classification of the nawafil that accompany the five daily prayers. Using the commentary of al-Bahr al-Raiq, we will see how the Hanafi school applies the principle of muwazabah to determine which prayers are sunnah ratibah (confirmed regular sunnah) and which are merely mustahabb (recommended). Understanding this distinction is crucial for correctly practicing the sunan al-rawatib and for issuing fatwas on prayer recommendations.

Guided Path
1
Identify each prayer time and the number of rak'ah under discussion
The passage covers before Asr (2 or 4), after Maghrib (6), after Isha (2 vs 4), and before/after Zuhr (2 vs 4). List each case separately.
2
Locate the primary hadith evidence for each case
For Asr, hadith of Ali; for Maghrib, hadith of Ibn Umar; for Isha, hadith of Aisha (four) and Ibn Umar/Hafsa (two); for Zuhr, hadith of Ibn Umar and Hafsa. Write down the sources.
3
Apply the criterion of muwazabah (regular observance)
Determine which acts the Prophet consistently performed. The two before Asr were not regularly practiced, so not ratibah. The two after Isha and after Zuhr are consistently reported in the Sahihayn. The four after Isha and six after Maghrib are occasional.
4
Classify each act as sunnah ratibah or mustahabb
Based on muwazabah: before Asr: mustahabb; after Maghrib: mustahabb; after Isha: sunnah ratibah (the two) plus mustahabb (additional two); before/after Zuhr: sunnah ratibah (two each) plus mustahabb (additional two each).
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute on the four after Isha; the mufta bihi is two.
5
State the practical ruling (mufta bihi) for each case
Summarize: For Asr, pray 2 or 4 before, both mustahabb (4 better). For Maghrib, 6 after mustahabb (in three sets). For Isha, 2 after sunnah ratibah, plus 2 nafl if desired. For Zuhr, 2 before and 2 after sunnah ratibah, plus 2 before and 2 after nafl.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من النوافل . أما الأربع قبل العصر فلما رواه الترمذي وحسنه عن علي رضي الله عنه قال : كان النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يصلي قبل العصر أربع ركعات يفصل بينهن بالتسليم على الملائكة المقربين ومن تبعهم من المسلمين والمؤمنين. وروى أبو داود عنه أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يصلي قبل العصر ركعتين، فلذا خيره في الأصل بين الأربع وبين الركعتين والأفضل الأربع. وإنما لم تكن الركعتان سنة راتبة لأنها ثابتة بيقين ويكون الأربع مستحباً لأنه لم يذكر في حديث عائشة رضي الله عنها للعصر سنة راتبة أصلاً كما في البدائع فلذا لم يجعل له سنة، وأما الأربع قبل العشاء فذكروا في بيانه أنه لم يثبت أن التطوع بها من السنن الراتبة فكان حسناً لأن العشاء نظير الظهر في أنه يجوز التطوع قبلها وبعدها كذا في البدائع. ولم ينقلوا حديثاً فيه بخصوصه لاستحبابه، وأما الأربع بعدها ففي سنن أبي داود عن شريح بن هانئ قال: سألت عائشة عن صلاة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فقالت : ما صلى العشاء قط فدخل بيتي إلا صلى فيه أربع ركعات أو ست ركعات. قال في فتح القدير : الذي يقتضيه النظر كون الأربع بعد العشاء سنة لنقل المواظبة عليها في أبي داود فإنه نص في مواظبته على الأربع دون الست للمتأمل ا هـ. وقد يقال: إنما لم تكن الأربع سنة لما في الصحيحين عن ابن عمر قال : صليت مع رسول الله ركعتين قبل الظهر وركعتين بعدها وركعتين بعد المغرب وركعتين بعد العشاء وركعتين بعد الجمعة. وحدثتني حفصة بنت عمر أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم كان يصلي ركعتين خفيفتين بعد ما يطلع الفجر ا هـ. فهو معارض لنقل المواظبة على الأربع فلذا لم تكن سنة. وأما الستة بعد المغرب فلما روى ابن عمر رضي الله عنهما أنه صلى الله عليه وسلم قال من صلى بعد المغرب ست ركعات كتب من الأوابين وتلا قوله تعالى فإنه كان للأوابين غفورا [الإسراء: ٢٥] وذكر في التجنيس أنه يستحب أن يصلي الست بثلاث تسليمات. ولم يذكر المصنف من المندوبات الأربع بعد الظهر. وصرح باستحبابها جماعة من المشايخ الحديث أبي داود والترمذي والنسائي. وحكى في فتح القدير اختلافاً بين أهل عصره في مسألتين: الأولى هل السنة المؤكدة محسوبة من المستحب في الأربع بعد الظهر وبعد العشاء وفي الست بعد المغرب أو لا. الثانية على تقدير الأولى هل يؤدي الكل بتسليمة واحدة أو بتسلمتين. واختار الأول فيهما وأطال الكلام
From the supererogatory prayers: As for the four before Asr, because al-Tirmidhi reported and classified as hasan from Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: The Prophet (peace be upon him) used to pray four rak'ahs before Asr, separating between them with salutations upon the angels brought near and those who follow them from Muslims and believers. Abu Dawud reported from him that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to pray two rak'ahs before Asr, so in principle one is given choice between the four and the two, and the four are better. The two are not a confirmed sunnah because they are proven with certainty, and the four are mustahabb because in the hadith of Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) no confirmed sunnah for Asr is mentioned at all, as in al-Bada'i. So no sunnah is established for it. As for the four before Isha, they mentioned in its explanation that it is not established that voluntary prayer is from the confirmed sunnahs, so it is good because Isha is similar to Zuhr in that voluntary prayer is permissible before and after it, as in al-Bada'i. They did not transmit a specific hadith for its recommendation. As for the four after Isha: in Sunan Abi Dawud from Shurayh ibn Hani who said: I asked Aisha about the prayer of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), and she said: He never prayed Isha and entered my house except that he prayed four or six rak'ahs. He said in Fath al-Qadir: What consideration requires is that the four after Isha are sunnah due to the transmission of regular observance of them in Abu Dawud, for it is a text on his regular observance of four, not six, for one who reflects. End quote. It may be said: They were not made sunnah because of what is in the two Sahihs from Ibn Umar who said: I prayed with the Messenger of Allah two before Zuhr, two after it, two after Maghrib, two after Isha, and two after Jumu'ah. And Hafsa bint Umar narrated to me that the Prophet (peace be upon him) used to pray two light rak'ahs after the dawn breaks. End quote. So it opposes the transmission of regular observance of four, so it was not sunnah. As for the six after Maghrib, because Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with them both) narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: Whoever prays six rak'ahs after Maghrib will be written among the penitent (awwabin) and recited His statement: 'Indeed He is Forgiving to the penitent' (Surah al-Isra: 25). And mentioned in al-Tajniss that it is recommended to pray the six with three taslims. The author did not mention the four after Zuhr among the recommended acts. A group of mashayikh expressed its recommendation based on the hadith of Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, and al-Nasa'i. And he narrated in Fath al-Qadir a difference of opinion among the people of his era on two issues: First, is the confirmed sunnah counted from the mustahabb in the four after Zuhr, after Isha, and in the six after Maghrib or not? Second, on the assumption of the first, is the entire (prayer) performed with one taslim or two? He chose the first in both and elaborated.
Source pages p. 88

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe from al-Bahr al-Raiq, commenting on Kanz al-Daqaiq regarding the legal status of various supererogatory prayers (nawafil) associated with the five daily prayers. The author, Zayn al-Din ibn Nujaym, clarifies which are sunnah ratibah (confirmed regular sunnah) and which are merely mustahabb (recommended). 

First, for Asr: there are two narrations from Ali—one of four rak'ah and one of two. The Hanafi position gives a choice between two or four, with four being better. However, neither is a sunnah ratibah because Aisha's hadith does not mention a confirmed sunnah for Asr. Hence, the two are considered sunnah ghayr mu'akkadah, and four are mustahabb. The key principle is that regular observance (muwazabah) is required for a sunnah to be ratibah; since the Prophet did not constantly pray two before Asr, it is not ratibah. 

Second, for Isha: the four before Isha are not sunnah ratibah because no specific hadith proves regularity. The four after Isha, however, are debated. Fath al-Qadir holds that the hadith in Abu Dawud shows the Prophet consistently prayed four, making it a sunnah. But this is countered by Ibn Umar's report mentioning only two after Isha. The Hanafi resolution is that the two are the sunnah ratibah (as per the sahih hadith), while the four are mustahabb. 

Third, for Maghrib: six rak'ah after Maghrib are recommended based on a hadith from Ibn Umar; it is a mustahabb not a sunnah ratibah, and it is preferred to pray them with three taslims (two rak'ah each). 

Fourth, for Zuhr: the four before Zuhr are not explicitly mentioned by the author of Kanz, but many mashayikh consider them mustahabb based on hadith from Abu Dawud, al-Tirmidhi, and al-Nasa'i. There is also a dispute whether the confirmed sunnah (the two before Zuhr) is included within the four mustahabb. The preferred view in Fath al-Qadir is that they are separate, and one should pray the two sunnah then the two nafl with separate taslims. 

The passage reflects the Hanafi methodology of weighing conflicting hadith evidence and relying on the principle of muwazabah (regular practice) for establishing sunnah ratibah.

Key Terms
سنة راتبة (sunnah ratibah): A confirmed regular supererogatory prayer that the Prophet consistently performed and ordered.
مستحب (mustahabb): A recommended act that is not regularly performed by the Prophet but is encouraged.
مواظبة (muwazabah): Regular and consistent performance of an act by the Prophet, used to establish a sunnah ratibah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the status of the two rak'ah before Asr in the Hanafi school?
A) Sunnah ratibah (confirmed sunnah).
B) Mustahabb (recommended).
C) Wajib.
D) Makruh.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes sunnah ratibah from mustahabb by the criterion of muwazabah (regular observance), not merely by the existence of a hadith.
